# Review de Prontidão pra Produção — DADOS COMPLETOS

> Swarm: 79 agentes · 16 subsistemas · verificação adversarial · 2026-06-05

Score médio geral: **7.13/10** · 31 blockers confirmados · 20 parciais · 11 refutados


---

## Database — schema & migrations

The database schema supports a multi-tenant SaaS platform with three main agent types (SparkBot rep-facing, sales/recruitment/custom lead-facing) plus complex features: bulk messaging with sequences/A-B variants, filter engine, billing with multi-modal usage tracking, RLS-protected data, and proactive scheduling. 98 migrations track schema evolution from core tables (locations, agents, conversation_state) through advanced features (modular agent platform, lead awareness, handoff). Schema has been heavily iterated (many drift fixes post-00040), with recent critical fixes for scheduled_followups and conversation_state columns that affected prod functionality.

### Funcionalidades

**Core Multi-Tenant Structure (locations → agents → agent_configs) — 9/10**
- ✅ Clean FK chains with proper CASCADE deletes. Unique partial index on agents(location_id, type) allows multiple custom_agent per location. All core tables have RLS via 00028 + 00088 deny-anon policies. Indexes on location_id, agent_id, status for fast queries.
- ⚠️ locations table has no explicit updated_at trigger (only created_at via default now()), but this table rarely changes. agent_configs lacks explicit updated_at, relies on default now() — no UPDATE trigger.
- 🔧 Add UPDATE triggers to locations and agent_configs to properly track schema_updated_at for audit trails (same pattern as location_settings 00040:231).

**Lead-Facing Pipeline (message_queue → execution_log → conversation_state) — 8/10**
- ✅ conversation_state has UNIQUE(agent_id, contact_id) ensuring singleton per conversation. Proper indexes on location, contact, status. ai_paused_at column re-added in 00085 after production drift discovery. ai_resumed_at added in 00098 for GU-6 override semantics. Status enum covers full lifecycle (active→qualified→booked→disqualified→handed_off→stale).
- ⚠️ conversation_state.collected_data is JSONB with no schema validation — admin could write arbitrary shapes. no generated updated_at trigger (relies on INSERT/UPDATE default). execution_log lacks action_type CHECK constraints (any string allowed, hard to audit).
- 🔧 (1) Add CHECK (action_type IN (...valid types...)) to execution_log. (2) Add BEFORE UPDATE trigger on conversation_state to set updated_at = now() for consistency. (3) Document collected_data shape in migration comment or create partial index for specific keys.

**SparkBot Rep-Facing (rep_identities → assistant_conversations → sparkbot_messages) — 8/10**
- ✅ rep_identities has phone UNIQUE, ghl_users JSONB storing multi-location enrollments. Silence tracking fields (last_inbound_at, consecutive_proactive_without_reply, proactive_paused_at) with proper indexes (00054). terms_accepted_at/terms_rejected_at persist opt-in state. All tables have RLS deny-anon. GHL message idempotency via unique index on sparkbot_messages(ghl_message_id) WHERE ghl_message_id IS NOT NULL.
- ⚠️ assistant_conversations.pending_action is JSONB with no shape validation. assistant_conversations.pending_messages is JSONB array with no schema. ghl_users in rep_identities is JSONB — migration has no comment on expected shape (breaking if schema changes). Debounce logic relies on debounce_expires_at timestamp without partial index.
- 🔧 (1) Add comment to 00029 describing rep_identities.ghl_users expected shape [{location_id, ghl_user_id, location_name, role}]. (2) Create partial index on assistant_conversations(debounce_expires_at) WHERE debounce_expires_at IS NOT NULL. (3) Add CHECK or trigger to validate pending_action/pending_messages JSONB shapes.

**Billing & Usage Tracking (usage_records with multi-modal telemetry) — 7/10**
- ✅ usage_records has all required columns post-00056 drift fix: cached_tokens, cache_creation_tokens, audio_seconds, image_count, audio_model, claim_token, claimed_at. Atomic claim token prevents double-charge in retries. Proper indexes on location_created, unbilled_capready (partial). RLS deny-anon via 00040. Monthly spend cap tracked with cap_blocked flag.
- ⚠️ cost_usd, total_charge_usd, markup_usd are NUMERIC but no CHECKs for non-negative. audio_model TEXT has no enum validation (billing depends on parsing it correctly). claim_token lacks a UNIQUE constraint — concurrent claims on same record could cause issues (no-op but inefficient). No foreign key on contact_id (soft link for audit).
- 🔧 (1) Add CHECKs: cost_usd >= 0, total_charge_usd >= 0, markup_usd >= 0. (2) Add UNIQUE(claim_token) WHERE claim_token IS NOT NULL. (3) Enumerate audio_model into proper CHECK (whisper_1|whisper-1). (4) Add index on usage_records(contact_id) for contact-level usage audits.

**Bulk Messages V2 (jobs → recipients → sequences → sequence_state) — 8/10**
- ✅ Comprehensive multi-table design for drip, sequences, A-B variants. bulk_message_recipients has variant_id for A-B stats, segment_label for multi-segment, personalized_message snapshot for audit. Sequence state tracks next_send_at + status (active/paused_by_reply/completed). RLS deny-anon via 00088 batch. Partial indexes on (next_send_at, status) for cron queries.
- ⚠️ bulk_message_jobs.filter_config is JSONB with no schema validation (admin could break runner by invalid config). Variation_mode has CHECK but no doc on what each mode does (light/medium/none). ab_variants JSONB in bulk_message_jobs has no shape validation. delivery_channel enum doesn't cover 'whatsapp_api' properly documented (was SMS before rename).
- 🔧 (1) Add migration comment documenting filter_config expected shape. (2) Add CHECK or trigger to validate ab_variants JSONB structure [{template, weight}]. (3) Add partial index on bulk_message_recipients(job_id, status) WHERE status = 'pending' for runner queries. (4) Document variation_mode behavior in migration.

**Prospection 2.0 Infrastructure (outreach_runs, recurring_campaigns, optouts, sequences) — 7/10**
- ✅ 00089 introduces complete outreach/recurring framework: outreach_runs logs daily executions, recurring_campaigns stores cron patterns (with next_run_at for scheduler), bulk_message_sequences for multi-touch with pause_on_reply logic, outreach_optouts UNIQUE(location_id, contact_id) for dedup. All tables RLS deny-anon. Indexes on next_run_at for cron, on (recipient_id) for sequence state lookup.
- ⚠️ recurring_campaigns.filter_config is JSONB with no validation (references FEL DSL but no schema spec in migration). cron_expression is TEXT with no parsing/validation CHECK. per_run_cap has CHECK (1-50000) but no docs on why 50K limit. bulk_message_sequence_state.recipient_id→bulk_message_recipients is CASCADE, but if job deleted, recipient AND state both cascade (potential orphans if job delete is racing with scheduler).
- 🔧 (1) Add migration comment documenting filter_config DSL shape and cron_expression format (POSIX crontab). (2) Add CHECK to recurring_campaigns to validate cron syntax (or move validation to runtime). (3) Add index on bulk_message_sequence_state(job_id, status) for job cleanup queries. (4) Document per_run_cap rationale.

**Lead Awareness & Handoff (lead_history_config, handoff_policy, handoff_notifications) — 8/10**
- ✅ F37 adds lead_history_config + handoff_policy JSONBs to agent_configs with sensible defaults (enabled=false). handoff_notifications table tracks what bot told rep via SparkBot when it decided to skip responding. Indexes on (location_id, contact_id, reason, created_at) for idempotency checks (cooldown 4h per reason). RLS deny-anon via 00096.
- ⚠️ lead_history_config and handoff_policy defaults in migration are hardcoded JSONBs — if admin edits one, no way to revert to migration default (need admin UI or script). skip_if_human_replied_within_minutes is 60 but no CHECK constraint (could be negative). handoff_notifications.metadata is JSONB with no schema doc.
- 🔧 (1) Add CHECK constraints for numeric fields in handoff_policy (minutes >= 0, etc). (2) Add migration comment documenting lead_history_config and handoff_policy schemas. (3) Add index on handoff_notifications(agent_id, created_at DESC) for dashboard queries.

**Modular Agent Platform (templates, modules, instances, entitlements) — 8/10**
- ✅ 00075 foundation: agent_templates stores metadata (key UNIQUE, version, audience). agent_modules has key + version unique index, category enum covers 9 domains (behavior/scheduling/compliance/crm_ops/knowledge/etc). agent_module_instances tracks per-agent overrides with prompt_override TEXT (allows per-agent customization). agent_entitlements has UNIQUE(location_id, capability) WHERE status='active' (singleton active grant per capability). All RLS deny-anon. Cascading deletes on agent.
- ⚠️ agent_modules.allowed_tools is TEXT[] with no validation (could have invalid tool names, breaks at runtime). prompt_fragment TEXT is nullable (expects registry TS to fill in Fase 1 — risky if registry is outdated). agent_templates.default_modules is JSONB array but no CHECK that module keys exist (could reference non-existent module). agent_entitlements.monthly_price_usd default 50 but no CHECK for positive.
- 🔧 (1) Add CHECK (monthly_price_usd > 0) to agent_entitlements. (2) Add migration comment documenting allowed_tools expected format (array of tool_id strings). (3) Add trigger/CHECK to agent_templates to validate default_modules references valid agent_modules.key. (4) Create foreign key from agent_modules to agent_templates(default_modules) or document the intentional loose coupling.

**Filter Engine & Execution Audit (filter_executions, bulk_message_recipients extensions) — 8/10**
- ✅ 00063 audit log captures every FEL execution: fel_input JSONB stores full query, plan_steps tracks optimizer output, applied_aliases documents type/name resolutions. duration_ms and hit_safety_cap track perf/abuse. Indexes on rep_created, slow (>5s), consumer_tool for analytics. personalized_message snapshot in bulk_message_recipients enables per-contact audit (what was actually sent post-interpolation).
- ⚠️ filter_executions.total_reported_by_ghl is nullable but no CHECK that it >= total_returned (data quality issue). consumer_tool is TEXT with no enum (could be any string, hard to group). plan_steps and applied_aliases are JSONB with no shape validation. Retention policy ("30 days automatically via cleanup job") is mentioned in comment but no actual cron job implemented.
- 🔧 (1) Add CHECK (total_reported_by_ghl IS NULL OR total_reported_by_ghl >= total_returned). (2) Add enum CHECK for consumer_tool. (3) Create cron job (pg_cron) to DELETE from filter_executions WHERE created_at < now() - interval '30 days'. (4) Add index on filter_executions(duration_ms DESC) for perf monitoring.

**RLS & Anon Denial (deny-anon RESTRICTIVE policies) — 9/10**
- ✅ 00028 establishes deny-anon pattern for all tables using service_role (which bypasses RLS). 00088 extends to 19 tables created after 00028 (bulk_*, sparkbot_dedup_locks, cron_config, stevo_instances, etc.) ensuring if anon key is ever used accidentally, all queries return 0 rows. RESTRICTIVE policies prevent privilege escalation. Pattern is idempotent (IF NOT EXISTS).
- ⚠️ Several tables (agent_test_sessions, agent_test_messages, knowledge_base, media_library, media_reactions) initially created without RLS, then added in 00088 via batch DO block — but if someone deployed past 00028 without 00088, those tables are still vulnerable. Migration 00088 comment admits this is 'zero impact on normal flow (service_role bypasses)' but it's a safety gap.
- 🔧 Document in CLAUDE.md or runbook: RLS is not the primary security boundary (service_role/pg_cron used everywhere), it's a defense-in-depth fallback. Ensure new tables get RLS in their creation migration, not in a later batch. Audit that all 53 tables have deny-anon policies (script to verify post-deploy).

### Structural issues
- **[CRITICAL] Schema Drift: Critical Missing Columns Fixed Post-Production (00040 → 00056, 00085)** — Migration 00040 declared usage_records columns (cached_tokens, cache_creation_tokens, audio_seconds, image_count, audio_model, charged_at, claim_token, claimed_at) but production database created via old SETUP.sql never received those columns. Runtime code silently failed: Whisper billing, Vision billing, cache billing, atomic claim — all broken. Fixed in 00056 via ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS. Similarly, conversation_state.ai_paused_at/ai_paused_reason were declared in 00009 but missing from prod (discovered 2026-05-26), causing opt-out/pausing to silently fail for leads. Fixed in 00085 with re-ADD COLUMN. This indicates gap between what migrations declare and what actually runs in production. (supabase/migrations/00040_usage_records_and_drift_recovery.sql, 00056_usage_records_schema_drift_recovery.sql, 00009_add_handoff_pause.sql, 00085_readd_conversation_state_pause.sql)
- **[HIGH] Unvalidated JSONB Schemas (agent_configs, bulk_message_jobs, recurring_campaigns, etc.)** — Multiple critical JSONB columns lack schema validation: agent_configs.data_fields (shape can break tools), agent_configs.alert_toggles, bulk_message_jobs.filter_config (if invalid, runner silently skips), recurring_campaigns.filter_config (ditto), agent_configs.lead_history_config/handoff_policy defaults are hardcoded (if admin edits, no revert path), agent_modules.allowed_tools is TEXT[] (could have typos). At runtime, invalid JSONB usually results in 'undefined' access rather than DB-level error, causing silent failures or LLM tools breaking. (supabase/migrations/00003_create_agent_configs.sql, 00050_bulk_messages.sql, 00089_prospeccao_v2_infra.sql, 00096_lead_awareness_handoff.sql, 00075_modular_agent_platform.sql)
- **[HIGH] Missing CHECK Constraints & Enum Validations** — Key columns lack CHECKs: (1) usage_records cost/charge amounts not validated >=0 (billing could charge negative?). (2) recurring_campaigns.per_run_cap has CHECK (1-50000) but no rationale doc. (3) agent_entitlements.monthly_price_usd default 50 with no CHECK >0 (free agents possible). (4) audio_model TEXT has no enum validation (code expects 'whisper-1', but could store anything). (5) filter_executions.total_reported_by_ghl nullable, no CHECK that >= total_returned. (6) recurring_campaigns.cron_expression is TEXT, no format validation (could be invalid cron). These holes allow garbage data that breaks downstream logic. (supabase/migrations/00040_usage_records_and_drift_recovery.sql, 00049_monthly_spend_cap.sql, 00056_usage_records_schema_drift_recovery.sql, 00077_entitlement_monthly_price.sql, 00063_filter_engine.sql, 00089_prospeccao_v2_infra.sql)
- **[MEDIUM] Missing Update Triggers on Key Tables (locations, agent_configs, etc.)** — Several tables lack BEFORE UPDATE triggers to auto-set updated_at: locations, agent_configs, agent_templates, agent_modules (manually created in some migrations but not universally applied). This means admin edits to agent_configs don't leave an audit trail of when they changed, breaking change-detection in dashboards/audits. Inconsistent pattern: location_settings (00040) has trigger, but agent_configs does not. (supabase/migrations/00001_create_locations.sql, 00003_create_agent_configs.sql, 00075_modular_agent_platform.sql (creates touch_updated_at for agent_* tables but not older ones))
- **[MEDIUM] RLS Coverage Was Incomplete Pre-00088 (Bulk, Sparkbot, Sequences Missing)** — bulk_message_jobs, bulk_message_recipients, sparkbot_dedup_locks, stevo_instances, followup_sequences/messages, etc. were created in migrations 00050-00067 without RLS ENABLE or deny-anon policies. RLS only retroactively added in 00088 via batch DO block (2026-05-26). If prod deployed past 00050 without 00088, those PII tables (contact names, messages, rep data) were unprotected at RLS layer (though service_role bypasses anyway). This is a safety gap in the deployment workflow. (supabase/migrations/00050_bulk_messages.sql, 00042_sparkbot_web_channel.sql, 00044_sparkbot_dedup_locks_and_reaper.sql, 00067_followup_feature.sql, 00072_stevo_instances.sql, 00088_rls_deny_anon_coverage.sql)
- **[MEDIUM] No Retention/TTL Policies (Data Grows Unbounded)** — Multiple high-volume tables lack cleanup: (1) sparkbot_messages intended 30-day TTL via migration comment (00040:210) but no cron job created. (2) filter_executions intended 30-day cleanup (00063 comment) but no cron job. (3) sparkbot_dedup_locks, admin_signals, filter_executions, execution_log all grow forever unless manually pruned. At scale (1K+ messages/day, 100s of leads), these tables balloon to multi-GB, slowing queries. Production likely has orphaned rows >90 days old consuming space. (supabase/migrations/00040_usage_records_and_drift_recovery.sql:210, 00063_filter_engine.sql:62, 00034_sparkbot_cleanup_cron.sql (mentions cleanup but doesn't implement full TTL), 00006_create_execution_log.sql)
- **[LOW] Loose Coupling Between agent_templates & agent_modules (No FK Validation)** — agent_templates.default_modules is JSONB array of module keys, but no CHECK or FK ensures those keys exist in agent_modules. Likewise, agent_modules.allowed_tools is TEXT[] with no validation against actual tool registry. If admin creates a template with non-existent module keys, the modular assembler (Fase 1, 00075 notes) will silently skip or error at runtime. This is partly by design ('loose coupling for extensibility') but should be documented and ideally have a post-deployment validation script. (supabase/migrations/00075_modular_agent_platform.sql)
- **[LOW] Concurrent Claim Token Race (usage_records atomic claim not fully atomic)** — usage_records.claim_token is used for idempotent billing retries (cron marks a batch with UUID to claim before charging). But there's no UNIQUE constraint on claim_token — two concurrent chargeWallet() calls could both claim the same token, resulting in double-charge. Migration 00056 added the claim_token column but no constraint. The code relies on SELECT FOR UPDATE or application-level locking (not visible in schema). (supabase/migrations/00056_usage_records_schema_drift_recovery.sql (adds claim_token but no UNIQUE))

### Production blockers
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] Missing Cron Job for sparkbot_messages TTL (30-day data accumulation)** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: Migration 00040 creates index idx_sparkbot_messages_old targeting >30d rows and comments 'TTL: cron de cleanup remove >30d (a ser adicionado em 00034 ou cron novo)'. But there's no actual cron job to DELETE old rows. At scale, sparkbot_messages table grows unbounded: 1 SparkBot rep sending 100 msgs/day × 365 days = 36.5K rows per rep (small now, but 1000 reps = 36.5M rows). Query perf degrades. No data retention compliance.
  - Fix: Create a pg_cron job in a new migration (or via MCP in prod): `SELECT cron.schedule('cleanup-sparkbot-messages', '0 2 * * *', 'DELETE FROM sparkbot_messages WHERE created_at < now() - interval ''30 days''');`. Verify index idx_sparkbot_messages_old is used. Add to ops runbook.
  - Veredicto: 
/Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/supabase/migrations/00040_usage_records_and_drift_recovery.sql:210 — Comment explicitly states "TTL: cron de cleanup remove >30d (a ser adicionado em 00034 ou cron novo)", indicating cleanup was planned but not yet implemented.

/Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/supabase/migrations/00034_sparkbot_cleanup_cron.sql:20-31 — The cron job 'sparkbot-cleanup' only deletes from assistant_scheduled_tasks (line 24) and assistant_alert_state (line 28), with no DELETE FROM sparkbot_messages statement.

/Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/supabase/migrations/00040_usage_records_and_drift_recovery.sql:211-213 — Index idx_sparkbot_messages_old is created (WHERE created_at < now() - interval '30 days') but never used by any DELETE operation.

Grep for DELETE FROM sparkbot_messages across all migrations and source code returns no results, confirming no cleanup exists.

- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] Missing Cron Job for filter_executions TTL (30-day audit log accumulation)** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: Migration 00063 comments that filter_executions cleanup (30-day retention) will happen 'via automatic job (futuro)' but no job is created. table grows with every FEL query: 1 location × 50 queries/day = 50 rows/day. 1000 locations = 50K rows/day. In 90 days = 4.5M rows (small but slows index scans). No audit retention enforcement.
  - Fix: Create pg_cron job: `SELECT cron.schedule('cleanup-filter-executions', '0 3 * * *', 'DELETE FROM filter_executions WHERE created_at < now() - interval ''30 days''');`. Confirm index idx_filter_executions_slow picks right rows. Document retention policy.
  - Veredicto: 
1. /Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/supabase/migrations/00063_filter_engine.sql:62 — COMMENT: 'Mantém 30 dias automaticamente via job de cleanup (futuro).'

2. /Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/src/lib/account-assistant/filter-engine/audit.ts — auditFilterExecution() fires on every get_contacts_filtered / get_opportunities_filtered / count_filtered call, inserting 1 row per query without any cleanup mechanism

3. Git log: Commit 757d4c9 (2026-05-15) introduced filter_executions; zero subsequent migrations (00064-00098 checked) implement cleanup

4. Precedent: /Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/supabase/migrations/00034_sparkbot_cleanup_cron.sql shows pattern — assistant_scheduled_tasks + assistant_alert_state have cron.schedule job 'sparkbot-cleanup' running daily; same pattern missing for filter_executions

5. No cron endpoint found in /src/app/api/cron/* that references filter_executions or deletes rows

6. /Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/supabase/migrations/00040_usage_records_and_drift_recovery.sql:Line describing sparkbot_messages has identical issue: 'TTL: cron de cleanup remove >30d (a ser adicionado em 00034 ou cron novo)' — also not implemented

Volume evidence: Migration 00063 deployed 2026-05-15, today is 2026-06-04 (20 days). Prompt-builder instructs LLM to call get_contacts_filtered/get_opportunities_filtered/count_filtered frequently (audit.ts shows fire-and-forget INSERT at every call). Estimated 50K rows/day × 20 days = 1M accumulated rows. No truncation exists; table will grow unbounded at linear rate without enforcement.

- **[PARTIAL/LOW] usage_records Billing Columns Never Validated in Schema (cost_usd/total_charge_usd can be negative)** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: usage_records.cost_usd, markup_usd, total_charge_usd are NUMERIC(12,6) with no CHECK (>= 0). If billing cron or manual correction accidentally writes negative values, they silently persist. Dashboard totals could show bogus negative charges. No data quality enforcement at schema layer. Discovered via inspection; no explicit bug report but drift_recovery.sql mentions this was masked by silent failures.
  - Fix: Add migration: `ALTER TABLE usage_records ADD CHECK (cost_usd >= 0), ADD CHECK (markup_usd >= 0), ADD CHECK (total_charge_usd >= 0);`. Run validation query to detect any existing negative rows before adding constraint.
  - Veredicto: 00040_usage_records_and_drift_recovery.sql:44-46 — columns declared NUMERIC(12,6) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0 with zero CHECK constraints. However: (1) pricing.ts:147-161 — calculateCost() guarantees non-negative output via Math.max(0,...) on every component before sum, making negative insertion impossible via normal code path; (2) charge.ts:48-77 — insertUsageRecord always receives output from calculateCost(), never user input; (3) usage-records.repo.ts:289-315 — only UPDATE operations are markWalletCharged/markCapBlocked/releaseClaimForRecord, which never touch cost fields; (4) Ultra-review 2026-05-26 C3-SINTESE.md lists 8 billing issues (C3-1 through C3-8) but does not cite this as a known issue; (5) chargeUnbilledRecords filters total_charge_usd > 0 (idx_usage_records_unbilled_capready WHERE total_charge_usd > 0), silently skipping any theoretical negative value from query results.
- **[CONFIRMED/MEDIUM] recurring_campaigns.cron_expression TEXT with No Format Validation** (conf: medium)
  - Porquê: recurring_campaigns stores POSIX cron strings (e.g., '0 9 * * 1') in TEXT field with no format CHECK. Admin could enter invalid cron like '99 99 * * *' or '* * * * * *' (quartz format), and the cron scheduler would fail silently or reject the job at execution time. No pre-deployment validation.
  - Fix: Add migration with CHECK constraint or app-level validation. Either: (a) Add CHECK using regex pattern for POSIX cron (difficult in SQL), or (b) document in migration that validation happens in runtime (src/lib/queue/recurring-runner.ts) and add unit test. Audit existing rows for invalid cron.
  - Veredicto: 
**Schema issue:**
- /Users/pedropoleza/SPARK\ APPS/AI\ platform/supabase/migrations/00089_prospeccao_v2_infra.sql:106 — `cron_expression TEXT NOT NULL` with no CHECK constraint on format or value ranges

**API validation gaps:**
- /Users/pedropoleza/SPARK\ APPS/AI\ platform/src/app/api/hub/campaigns/recurring/route.ts:27 — Zod schema only validates length `min(7).max(40)`, not field values
- /Users/pedropoleza/SPARK\ APPS/AI\ platform/src/app/api/hub/campaigns/recurring/route.ts:53-60 — Sanity check only verifies 5 space-separated parts exist, NOT that values are within POSIX ranges (minuto 0-59, hora 0-23, dia 1-31, mês 1-12, dow 0-6)

**Broken field validation logic:**
- /Users/pedropoleza/SPARK\ APPS/AI\ platform/src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/cron-evaluator.ts:130-144 — `matchField()` function receives `_min` and `_max` parameters (underscored = ignored) but NEVER uses them. Example: `matchField("99", 99, 0, 59)` returns true even though 99 > max 59. Lines 138-139 show range parsing "1-5" also doesn't validate bounds.

**Silent runtime failure:**
- /Users/pedropoleza/SPARK\ APPS/AI\ platform/src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/cron-evaluator.ts:92-108 — `computeNextRunAt()` exhausts 144,000 minute iterations without finding a match if cron is invalid (e.g. '99 99 * * *'), returns null
- /Users/pedropoleza/SPARK\ APPS/AI\ platform/src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/recurring-runner.ts:155-164 — When `computeNextRunAt()` returns null, campaign is silently disabled (`enabled = false`) with no admin notification
- /Users/pedropoleza/SPARK\ APPS/AI\ platform/src/app/api/hub/campaigns/recurring/route.ts:96-103 — Error message is vague: "Não consegui calcular o próximo disparo — confirme cron=..." without explaining WHAT is invalid about the cron expression

**Example attack scenario:**
Admin enters `cron_expression = "99 99 * * *"`:
1. POST /api/hub/campaigns/recurring accepts it (5-field check passes)
2. computeNextRunAt('99 99 * * *', 'UTC') returns null after 144k iterations
3. API rejects with generic error message
4. If admin enters a cron that somehow passes but is malformed (e.g., range out of bounds like "50-100 * * * *" for minutes), it goes to DB and will periodically fail at runtime with silent campaign disablement

**Missing test coverage:**
- /Users/pedropoleza/SPARK\ APPS/AI\ platform/scripts/test-recurring.ts tests `computeNextRunAt()` with valid crons only (line 89 tests "invalid" string but not out-of-range numerics like "99 99 * * *")

- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] agent_entitlements.monthly_price_usd Default 50 with No Positive CHECK** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: Migration 00077 adds monthly_price_usd with DEFAULT 50 (cents implied?) but no CHECK (> 0). Could theoretically set to 0 or negative, making free agents or credits. Also unclear if 50 = $0.50 or $50 (off-by-100 risk). Costing logic depends on this being positive and properly scaled.
  - Fix: Add CHECK (monthly_price_usd > 0). Add migration comment clarifying unit: 'monthly_price_usd in USD cents (e.g., 5000 = $50.00)'. Audit all rows to ensure >0. Update CLAUDE.md Billing section with unit clarity.
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] Unvalidated JSONB: bulk_message_jobs.filter_config Can Cause Silent Runner Failure** (conf: med)
  - Porquê: bulk_message_jobs.filter_config stores FEL (Filter Expression Language) queries for 'dispatch to contacts matching this filter'. If admin saves invalid JSON or malformed FEL (e.g., {tag: [1,2,3]} instead of {tag: 'tagname'}), the runner (queue/bulk-runner.ts) may fail to parse/apply the filter. Results in 0 contacts enqueued silently, or wrong subset. No schema validation at write time.
  - Fix: Add FEL schema validation to the tool that creates bulk_message_jobs (tools/bulk-messages-v2.ts) before INSERT. Store validation error if fails. Alternatively, add migration comment documenting filter_config shape and add trigger to validate basic JSON structure. Create test cases for invalid configs.
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] conversation_state ai_paused_at & ai_paused_reason Were Missing from Production Until 00085** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: This is a CRITICAL BUG FIXED in 00085 (discovered 2026-05-26). conversation_state.ai_paused_at was declared in 00009 but never applied to prod database. Result: opt-out/pausing for lead-facing agents was completely broken — inbound 'STOP' messages couldn't pause the bot. Code tried to UPDATE ai_paused_at → column doesn't exist → upsert silently failed (supabase-js anti-pattern) → bot continued responding. Fixed in 00085 by re-adding the columns. But if this migration hasn't been applied to prod yet, pausing is still broken.
  - Fix: Verify 00085 has been applied to production (check pg_migrations or run: SELECT * FROM pg_migrations WHERE name='00085_readd_conversation_state_pause';). If missing, apply immediately via MCP or manual SQL. Verify ai_paused_at column exists in conversation_state. Run smoke test: pause a lead in GHL, verify bot stops responding.
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] Modular Agent Platform Modules/Templates Have No Runtime Registry Link (Fase 1 Incomplete)** (conf: med)
  - Porquê: Migration 00075 creates agent_modules table with prompt_fragment TEXT nullable, intending that 'NULL = registry TS provê (Fase 1)'. This means the DB schema is defined but the prompt fragments are split between DB (if filled) and src/lib/agent-platform/modules/*.ts registry. If a module in the registry is updated but not in DB, or vice versa, assembler could use stale logic. No constraint ensures they're in sync. Fase 1 status per CLAUDE.md is 'prontas' but tight coupling not tested.
  - Fix: Verify Fase 1 integration tests pass: scripts/test-motor-parity.ts (7/7 cases). Ensure every agent_modules.key that has a default_modules reference in agent_templates also has a corresponding module object in modules/{registry,behavior,scheduling,etc}.ts. Document registry→DB sync requirement in CLAUDE.md. Create pre-deployment check.


---

## Database — multi-tenant, RLS & seguranca de dados

O sistema usa Supabase com autenticação via GHL SSO (JWT custom). RLS está habilitado em 50+ tabelas, mas com políticas RESTRICTIVE deny-anon apenas (que não protegem contra service_role). Service_role key é usado em TODAS as rotas API + cron jobs, e bypass RLS por padrão. A aplicação tenta isolamento multi-tenant via filtros aplicados (location_id em cadeias de query), mas **três camadas críticas de vazamento estão descobertas**: (1) claimUnbilledBatch e findStaleUnbilledRecords aceitam unbilled records de QUALQUER location; (2) admin_signals não têm isolamento por tenant (acessível globalmente); (3) inbound_webhook_samples sem verificação de location_id em leitura/deleção. RLS não oferece proteção (service_role bypassa) e não há auditoria de acesso cruzado.

### Funcionalidades

**RLS Policy Coverage (Deny-Anon) — 4/10**
- ✅ RLS está habilitado em 50+ tabelas incluindo sparkbot_messages, usage_records, location_settings, bulk_message_*. Policies RESTRICTIVE deny_anon aplicadas em migrations 00007, 00028, 00088. Anti-malveille defensiva contra acesso acidental via anon key.
- ⚠️ Policies são deny-by-default para anon, mas **não protegem contra service_role** (que bypassa RLS por design no Supabase). A aplicação usa SEMPRE service_role via createAdminClient(), então RLS é inert pra qualquer acesso legítimo. Nenhuma policy permissiva definida pra service_role — depende de app-level filtering.
- 🔧 RLS fornece baseline zero-trust pra acidentes, mas é security theater contra ataques no app layer. Adicionar policies permissivas explícitas (ex: `location_id = current_setting('app.location_id')`) não ajuda porque o app não seta esse setting. SOLUÇÃO REAL: (a) migrar pra auth nativa Supabase (não SSO custom) OU (b) mudar service_role queries pra SELECT explícito com location_id em TODA query sensível e testes de regressão (risk alto). Curto prazo: adicionar MATERIALIZED VIEW wrapper com força location_id no WHERE obrigatório.

**Multi-Tenant Location Filtering — API Routes — 6/10**
- ✅ sparkbot_messages, agents, agent_configs: todos filtram por location_id ou hub_location_id explicitamente nas SELECT/UPDATE. Webhook handler (webhook-handler.ts) extrai hubLocationId e passa como parâmetro. Queue processor (queue-processor.ts) filtra group.locationId em queries críticas. Sparkbot rep-facing isolado por rep_id + hub_location_id (2 níveis).
- ⚠️ **Inconsistência crítica**: queries de leitura/contagem no dashboard admin (00040, findStaleUnbilledRecords, countMessagesByRole) contam registros de TODAS as locations sem filtro. Um admin pode enumerar uso de outra location. **inbound_webhook_samples** em /lib/account-assistant/inbound-webhook-capture.ts: insert sim filtra location_id, mas DELETE no cleanup NÃO verifica — qualquer código pode deletar amostras de outra location.
- 🔧 CRÍTICO: (1) findStaleUnbilledRecords deve aceitar locationId param (ou uma lista de location_ids). Todos os callers devem filtrar ANTES. (2) countMessagesByRole / getMetricsForDashboard devem aceitar filtro por location_id (admin painel vê tudo, mas query auditável). (3) inbound_webhook_samples DELETE: adicionar location_id na cláusula WHERE antes de rodar em prod.

**Billing & Charge Atomicity — Claim Idempotency — 5/10**
- ✅ Atomic claim via claimUnbilledBatch: SELECT ids + UPDATE by ids com claim_token UUID único evita double-charge em retry de cron. UNIQUE INDEX em ghl_message_id (sparkbot_messages) + dedup locks (sparkbot_dedup_locks) adicionam camadas 6-7 de idempotência. Reaper de claims órfãos (15min) libera records travados. Usage records schema completo com cached_tokens, audio_seconds, image_count (audit trail correto).
- ⚠️ **CRITICAL**: claimUnbilledBatch seleciona records de QUALQUER location — não há filtro por location_id no query. Se 2 locations têm unbilled records, o claim pode pegar misturado. Exemplo: location A tem $50, location B tem $10 unbilled; cron roda, claim pega mix, processa com getCompanyId() que será WRONG pra metade. Mesmo findStaleUnbilledRecords (chamado pra alertar) é global.
- 🔧 BLOCKER: claimUnbilledBatch precisa aceitar optional locationIds: string[] filter. Cada call-site deve passar sua location (ou null pra admin-only global). findStaleUnbilledRecords idem. Alternativa mais robusta: adicionar location_id como parte da clause WHERE em ambas funções e refactor callers.

**Admin Signals — Global (No Tenant Scope) — 3/10**
- ✅ Anti-duplicação via fingerprint (determinístico) evita spam. Race condition 23505 capturada + retry. Metadata bem-formado em JSONB com samples (últimas 10). Queries por fingerprint são fast.
- ⚠️ **STRUCTURAL ISSUE**: admin_signals tabela NÃO tem location_id, company_id, ou nenhum campo de scope. É global por design (feedback pra Pedro). Qualquer service_role query pode LERS todos os signals de todas as locations (privacy risk zero, mas inconsistente com isolamento aplicado). Query de SELECT por fingerprint não filtra nada — acesso pleno.
- 🔧 Admin signals são intencionalmente globais (hub painel único). Se design foi assim, OK. Mas DOCUMENTAR que admin_signals NÃO respeitam multi-tenant e dados ali são legíveis por qualquer rota admin (ex: futura API /api/admin/signals?type=error pode vazar issues de outra location).

**Idempotency — Dedup Layers 1-7 — 7/10**
- ✅ 7 camadas de idempotência: (1) in-memory mutex inFlightMessages; (2) SELECT by ghl_message_id; (3) UNIQUE constraint sparkbot_dedup_locks (PK dedup_key); (4-5) content-match + timing-match SELECTs com janelas; (6) UNIQUE ghl_message_id; (7) race condition 23505 capture em rep_identities insert. Teste stress 2026-05-03 validou todas (documentado em CLAUDE.md).
- ⚠️ Cada camada está dispersa entre webhook-handler, identity.ts, migrations. Sem teste end-to-end que dispara 2 webhooks idênticos concorrentes, é risco de regressão silenciosa. Documentação em código é fragmentada (comentários H8, Track 1 C3 em DECISIONS.md).
- 🔧 Criar script `scripts/test-idempotency-e2e.ts` que simula webhook duplo (Stevo + GHL race <100ms) e verifica INSERT uma vez, resposta uma vez. Adicionar ao CI. Manter camadas pois são defense-in-depth — remover umas qualquer mudança de schema quebra outra.

**Service Role Key Usage Scope — 5/10**
- ✅ Service role key é usado apenas em server-side (Next.js API routes + cron). Never exposed to client. Anon key está em NEXT_PUBLIC_ mas é never used at runtime (dead code per 00028). Repos centralizam acesso (createAdminClient sempre).
- ⚠️ **ARCHITECTURAL RISK**: 100% das queries usam service_role, que bypassa RLS. Não há gradation de privilege. Qualquer bug na app layer (forgetting location_id in WHERE) compromete toda a base de dados. Não há way to audit 'which routes read what data' sem log granular de Postgres.
- 🔧 MAJOR refactor (out-of-scope production): criar **view_role user + row-level policies** que app usa em place of service_role. Requires Supabase auth overhaul. INTERIM: (a) força compilação-time check de location_id in all SELECT/UPDATE (TypeScript static analysis); (b) audit log em app layer (middleware que logs all DB ops + location_id) para prod monitoring.

**Client Auth & JWT Verification — 6/10**
- ✅ sparkbot web endpoints (inbox, send, scheduling-prefs) verificam JWT via verifySparkbotWebToken. SSO route usa JWKS validation. API admin routes usam env-based API key checks (GHL_API_KEY). Rate limiting por IP + cost circuit breaker em webhook (inbound-message/route.ts).
- ⚠️ JWT verification retorna token object mas NÃO aparentemente vincula location_id ao token (token tem rep_id, sem location_id guarantee). verifySparkbotWebToken não mostrado em grep — pode aceitar qualquer JWT válido assinado (risco se JWKS upstream comprometido). Admin routes usam SIMPLE env key check (não JWT), vulnerável a key leak. Sem audit log de quem accessed o quê.
- 🔧 Auditar verifySparkbotWebToken signature — deve validar JWT issuer + audience. Admin API keys should be rotated (add created_at, rotated_at tracking, retirement warnings). Middleware pra log all auth+location access.

**Cross-Tenant Data Risk — Worst Case Scenario — 2/10**
- ✅ RLS deny-anon layer prevents naive attacks (misused anon key). Sparkbot messages indexed by (rep_id, hub_location_id) so direct iteration by rep_id alone won't leak (rep_id alone is UUID).
- ⚠️ **CRITICAL WORST CASE**: If a malicious actor or buggy code calls claimUnbilledBatch() for location A, they get ALL unbilled records (A, B, C, ..., Z). Then getCompanyId(location_id) lookup fails/succeeds wrong, leading to charge user Z instead of A. OR if findStaleUnbilledRecords is called in an admin page without filtering, page lists unbilled amounts of competitors. **SINGLE SHARED QUERY**: `SELECT ... FROM usage_records WHERE charged_to_wallet=false` (no location_id) returns gSLOB of data across all tenants.
- 🔧 EMERGENCY FIX: Add location_id filter to claimUnbilledBatch, findStaleUnbilledRecords before any production traffic. Add location_id to any query that returns numbers/costs. Consider rate-limiting billing cron to run per-location serially (slower but safer).

### Structural issues
- **[HIGH] Inconsistent location_id filtering across query types** — Some queries (sparkbot_messages, agents) consistently filter location_id. Others (admin_signals, usage_records cleanup, webhook samples) lack filtering. Creates maintenance burden — future devs must remember which table is safe and which isn't. No clear convention or type-safety enforcement. (/lib/repositories/*.repo.ts (inconsistent), /lib/account-assistant/inbound-webhook-capture.ts, /lib/billing/charge.ts)
- **[HIGH] RLS policies are 'security theater' — service_role bypasses all** — 50+ tables have RLS enabled + deny-anon policies. But service_role has RLS_BYPASS privilege. Every query in app is service_role. Policies are defense against accidental anon key use, not against app bugs. Creates false sense of security — developers may assume RLS protects them when it doesn't. (/supabase/migrations/00007_enable_rls.sql, 00028_rls_deny_anon.sql, 00088_rls_deny_anon_coverage.sql (all inert), /src/lib/supabase/admin.ts (service_role used everywhere))
- **[MEDIUM] No centralized location_id context injection** — Each query manually adds .eq('location_id', param). No middleware or context wrapper ensures location_id is ALWAYS present. Fragile to refactoring — if someone forgets .eq() in a new query, no compile error. (/src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts, /src/lib/account-assistant/webhook-handler.ts, /src/lib/repositories/*)
- **[MEDIUM] Admin/global queries mixed with location-scoped queries** — Functions like claimUnbilledBatch are called by cron (global context) but should filter per-location (or at least be explicit about global scope). Naming doesn't disambiguate (no 'Admin' or 'Global' prefix). Easy to misuse. (/src/lib/repositories/usage-records.repo.ts (claimUnbilledBatch, findStaleUnbilledRecords), /src/lib/billing/charge.ts (chargeUnbilledRecords calls these without location context))
- **[MEDIUM] Webhook samples (inbound_webhook_samples) housekeeping has no tenant scope** — Debug table for webhook payloads. Insert adds location_id. But cleanup DELETE has no WHERE location_id clause. Violates consistency pattern. Table grows unbounded if cleanup doesn't filter correctly. (/src/lib/account-assistant/inbound-webhook-capture.ts (captureInboundWebhookSample, ~line 140 cleanup DELETE))
- **[LOW] Admin signals table (admin_signals) is intentionally global** — Signals are for Pedro's dashboard (central admin). Schema has no location_id. This may be intentional, but creates risk if future admin APIs are added without checking. Should be explicitly documented in code or add CONSTRAINT that prevents misuse. (/supabase/migrations/00001_create_locations.sql (admin_signals table created, no tenant scope), /src/lib/admin-signals/recorder.ts (queries are global by design))
- **[MEDIUM] No static analysis or pre-commit check for location_id in queries** — Developers can add .select().eq('x', val).gt('y', z) without location_id and TS compiler doesn't complain. ESLint rule could enforce this (require location_id in WHERE for sensitive tables), but it's not implemented. (No pre-commit hooks defined; /src/lib is missing type-safe query builder)
- **[LOW] Dead code: NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY is never used** — Anon key lives in env + client.ts, but is never actually used in runtime (application uses service_role everywhere). Per 00028_rls_deny_anon.sql comment. Confuses future developers (is anon key meant to be used? why is it in NEXT_PUBLIC?). Should remove or document as 'reserved for future Supabase Auth migration'. (/src/lib/supabase/client.ts (createBrowserClient never called), env template)

### Production blockers
- **[REFUTED/LOW] CRITICAL: claimUnbilledBatch lacks location_id filter** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Function selects usage_records for billing without filtering by location_id. Can claim mix of records from multiple locations. Combined with getCompanyId() lookup, can charge WRONG location's GHL wallet. Discovered via code audit of /lib/repositories/usage-records.repo.ts line ~90. Risk: financial data leak + wrong customer charged.
  - Fix: Add locationId: string | null parameter to claimUnbilledBatch. If locationId provided, add .eq('location_id', locationId) before .select('id'). Update all call sites in charge.ts to pass locationId (can be null for global admin query, but document this is unsafe). Add test case that verifies billing only claims from correct location.
  - Veredicto: 
FUNCTION ANALYSIS:
/Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/src/lib/repositories/usage-records.repo.ts:226-257 - claimUnbilledBatch() selects usage_records without location_id filter (correct - global batch).

SAFETY MECHANISM - the fix is in the USAGE pattern in charge.ts:356-375:
- For EACH claimed record, line 358: const companyId = await getCompanyId(record.location_id) — uses record's own location_id (from DB row)
- Line 367: await chargeWallet(companyId, record.location_id, ...) — charges using that specific company+location pair
- Each record is processed independently with its own location context

DATABASE INTEGRITY:
/Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/supabase/migrations/00040_usage_records_and_drift_recovery.sql:27 - usage_records.location_id has FK constraint to locations(location_id) ON DELETE CASCADE
- Ensures every record references a valid location
- locations.location_id is UNIQUE (line 83)

CACHE SAFETY:
charge.ts:337-348 - getCompanyId() cache is keyed by locationId string, not global. Each location maps to its own company_id independently. No cross-location pollution.

TYPE SAFETY:
- usage_records.repo.ts line 20: location_id: string (TS)
- 00040.sql line 27: location_id TEXT (SQL)
- Consistent throughout

CONCLUSION: Not filtering by location_id is intentional design for global batch processing. The location context is preserved in each record and used correctly for each charge. No actual vulnerability.

- **[PARTIAL/LOW] CRITICAL: findStaleUnbilledRecords is global (all locations)** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Function queries usage_records without location_id filter. Used in chargeUnbilledRecords (billing cron) to find old unbilled records. Returns records from ALL locations mixed. Alert logs amount/count but could confuse ops teams (is alert for location A or B or sum?). Found /lib/repositories/usage-records.repo.ts.
  - Fix: Add locationId?: string parameter. Query should .eq('location_id', locationId) when provided (admin call with null = cross-tenant audit, add flag to enforce null must be admin). All callers in charge.ts must pass location context. Add audit log of which location's records were claimed to mitigate confusion.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/repositories/usage-records.repo.ts:108-120 — function selects from usage_records with filters on charged_to_wallet, uses_custom_key, total_charge_usd, created_at, but NO location_id filter. src/lib/billing/charge.ts:311-323 — alert logs "[Billing ALERT] {count} unbilled records... total ${amount}" without location breakdown. Usage is intentional: chargeUnbilledRecords (line 288) is a global admin function (uses createAdminClient/service role) that processes ALL locations in one cron run for efficiency. RLS policy exists (migration 00040:79) but is not applicable to admin client. The function is used for alerting on system-wide billing issues (>100 records OR >$10 total), not per-location reporting. Per-location visibility exists in parallel via /api/billing route (line 28) which filters by session.locationId.
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] HIGH: inbound_webhook_samples cleanup DELETE lacks location filter** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: captureInboundWebhookSample inserts with location_id, but cleanup DELETE in same file does .delete().lt('received_at', cutoff) with zero location check. Any code path could delete another location's samples. Found /lib/account-assistant/inbound-webhook-capture.ts. Risk: debug data loss.
  - Fix: Add location_id parameter to cleanup function. Change DELETE to include .eq('location_id', locationId). Update caller to pass locationId (from where? webhook context or from hubLocationId passed to captureInboundWebhookSample). Add integration test that verifies cleanup only deletes same-location samples.
  - Veredicto: /src/lib/account-assistant/inbound-webhook-capture.ts:40 inserts with location_id. Lines 49-54 select 100th oldest row GLOBALLY (no .eq("location_id", ...)). Line 59 deletes ALL rows .lt("received_at", cutoff) with ZERO location filter. Result: a webhook from Location B's 101st sample triggers deletion of Location A's oldest samples, regardless of Location A having fewer than 100 samples. Multi-tenant isolation broken: one location's data pruning affects another's. Schema /supabase/migrations/00078_inbound_webhook_samples.sql:12-19 shows location_id TEXT (nullable) but zero location-scoped RLS policies—only deny_anon_all (line 24). Function called from /src/app/api/webhooks/inbound-message/route.ts:181-192, shared webhook endpoint for all locations, so location_id is in the request but pruning discards it.
- **[PARTIAL/MEDIUM] HIGH: admin_signals table has no tenant scope column** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: admin_signals table globally accessible (no location_id or company_id). Future admin APIs that expose signals (ex: /api/admin/signals) could leak signal metadata from competitor's location to another admin. Found schema in 00001-00040 migrations (no location_id column). Risk: information disclosure.
  - Fix: Add OPTIONAL location_id TEXT column to admin_signals. Backfill all existing rows with NULL (admin context, not location-specific). New signals should set location_id if from location context (or NULL if system-wide). If signals are always admin-only (never expose via public API), document this assumption clearly. OR: accept global signals by design but add COMMENT explaining (not a bug, intentional design).
  - Veredicto: 00051_admin_signals.sql: admin_signals table schema has NO location_id or company_id column; metadata field stores location_id as JSONB only (lines 51-53, 81). /src/app/api/admin/signals/route.ts:26-31: GET endpoint queries all signals globally with zero location filtering (.select("*") with no .eq("location_id",...) filter). /src/middleware.ts:20-30: Single global ADMIN_PANEL_PASSWORD with no per-agency auth. 00088_rls_deny_anon_coverage.sql: Only deny-anon RLS policy; no tenant-isolation policy on admin_signals. README.md line 2: Confirms multi-tenant architecture ("Plataforma multi-tenant de agentes de IA...cada agência = companyId). CLAUDE.md: "Solo dev — bus factor = 1" and "ESTAO FINALIZANDO pra ir a producao agora" = currently single-admin deployment, not yet multi-agency admin.
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] MEDIUM: countMessagesByRole and dashboard metrics are cross-tenant** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Functions like countMessagesByRole in sparkbot-messages.repo query ALL sparkbot_messages (global count via 'gte created_at'). Used by admin dashboard to show metrics. Lacks location_id filter. Found /lib/repositories/sparkbot-messages.repo.ts. If exposed in /api/admin/dashboard without auth check, leaks competitor usage.
  - Fix: Audit all *dashboard* or *metrics* functions in repositories. Add locationId?: string param. Admin dashboard route /api/admin/dashboard must enforce: only admin can see global view, normal user only their location. Add integration test: verify /api/admin/dashboard?show_all_locations returns 401 if not admin.
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] MEDIUM: Service-role key bypasses RLS entirely** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Application uses service_role key in 100% of server-side queries via createAdminClient(). Service role has RLS_BYPASS privilege. RLS policies (deny-anon) are inert. Any app-layer bug (missing location_id in WHERE) compromises data. No per-row enforcement. Found: all of /lib/repositories/*, /lib/billing/*, /lib/account-assistant/*. Risk: regression when refactoring.
  - Fix: SHORT TERM: Add pre-commit hook / build-step TypeScript static analysis to force `location_id` or `hub_location_id` in WHERE of sensitive tables (usage_records, sparkbot_messages, bulk_message_*). LONG TERM: Migrate to Supabase Auth (not custom SSO) + RLS policies for service_role, or use view_roles with row security. Document current design decision + risk in SECURITY.md.
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] MEDIUM: No audit log of cross-location queries** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: If a bug allows query of location A's data while in location B context, no way to detect post-incident (no DB-level audit, no app-level logging of location_id per query). Postgres audit extension not enabled. Supabase doesn't provide free query logging. Risk: security breach goes undetected.
  - Fix: Add middleware in Next.js route handler (before createAdminClient) that logs: method + path + location_id context + user_id. Store in app log table or structured logging service (Vercel logs, Sentry, etc.). Minimum: console.warn('[AUDIT] op_type=SELECT table=sparkbot_messages user=X location=Y ip=Z'). This is 'defense in depth' not blocker, but highly recommended before prod.


---

## Agentes lead-facing — pipeline queue-processor

The queue-processor is the core execution engine for lead-facing agents (sales/recruitment/custom). It orchestrates a multi-stage message processing pipeline: deduplication and atomic claiming, multiple skip gates (pause/targeting/should-respond/human takeover), GHL data fetching with retry, prompt construction with lead history and carrier KB, LLM invocation with parse recovery, action execution (send_message/book/update fields), collected data sync, billing/charging, and automation triggers. The system includes 7 layers of idempotency (in-memory mutex → UNIQUE constraints → dedup gates), fail-open targeting, and comprehensive audit logging via execution_log.

### Funcionalidades

**Message Claiming & Deduplication (H11, H12) — 8/10**
- ✅ Atomic UPDATE...RETURNING claim prevents race conditions across concurrent workers. Reaper resets orphaned 'processing' messages >5min. Per-group error tracking ensures failed groups don't cause cascading status mismarks. Deduplication layer catches duplicate actions from LLM.
- ⚠️ Reaper window is fixed 5min—if a message gets reprocessed by duplicate worker exactly at 5:01, two concurrent executions can still occur before first marks it completed (race <100ms). No distributed lock per message_id across Vercel instances.
- 🔧 Use advisory locks (pg_advisory_xact_lock) keyed on message_id for true cross-lambda serialization, or implement distributed cache (Redis) for <100ms claims.

**Skip Gates (pause/targeting/should-respond/F52 handoff) — 7/10**
- ✅ Clean sequential gates prevent unnecessary work: ai_paused_at → max_messages cap → GU-6 manual resume override → targeting → should-respond. Fail-open targeting (GHL fetch error = assume match) preserves UX. F52 fallback handoff detection catches human takeover even without webhook. Clear audit trail via execution_log.
- ⚠️ GU-6 manual resume override logic uses only `ai_resumed_at` timestamp—if rep clicks 'resume' WHILE the last human message is being processed in parallel (2 workers claiming the same contact group), order of operations is undefined. F52 handoff check fetches last 30 execution_log rows sequentially to build anti-echo list—if contacts have >100 recent sends, performance degrades. No guard against race between F52 check and concurrent follow-up execution.
- 🔧 Lock conversation_state during resume-override check to serialize F52 logic. Cache aiSentTexts in Redis (5min TTL) to avoid sequential execution_log scans on each inbound. Add soft lock on conversation before F52 check.

**GHL Data Fetching (contact, messages, slots, opportunities) — 7/10**
- ✅ Parallel fetch via Promise.allSettled reduces latency (~500ms serial → 200ms parallel). withRetry on messages + slots (2 retries, 200ms base backoff) recovers transient GHL downtime. Graceful degradation: message fetch reject → conversationTurns=[]; slots reject → slotsFetchFailed=true + bot continues. Comprehensive error logging.
- ⚠️ Contact fetch has NO retry—single transient GHL error zeros contactData for entire turn (lead's name, email, etc lost from context). convId search is sequential (must succeed before messages fetch)—if search fails, messages fetch is skipped without fallback. No timeout per GHL call beyond Vercel's 30s global—if one endpoint hangs, entire request can timeout.
- 🔧 Add withRetry to contact fetch. Pre-cache convId in conversation_state to avoid search on every turn. Set explicit 5s timeout per GHL endpoint with early bailout.

**Lead History (F37) - Load & Should-Respond Decision — 7/10**
- ✅ Lead history loader (lead-history.ts) batches 4 parallel GHL fetches (contact/conversations/messages/notes). 5min in-memory cache per (location, contact, config-hash) avoids re-fetching same lead. should-respond evaluates heuristics (human_replied_recently, lead_requested_human, opp_closed) with configurable thresholds and notification. Clear decision enum + audit payload. Fail-soft: GHL error → empty LeadContext, bot responds anyway.
- ⚠️ Lead history cache is in-memory (Map) — lost on lambda restart. No cache invalidation hook when rep manually resumes (GU-6). should-respond uses simple substring regex for handoff keywords—false positives possible ('humano' matches 'inhumano'). Notification cooldown (4h) is hardcoded—no per-agent config. notifyRepViaSparkbot silently fails if rep unresolved (no error bubbled).
- 🔧 Migrate cache to Redis (5min TTL) for cross-lambda persistence. Call invalidateLeadHistoryCache on ai_resumed_at upsert. Use boundary-aware regex for keywords. Parameterize cooldown via agent_config. Bubble notify_rep failures to log/alert, don't swallow.

**AI Prompt Construction & Model Routing — 8/10**
- ✅ Unified motor via assembler.ts (Plataforma Modular) delegates to buildSystemPrompt for lead-facing agents—single source of truth for prompt. buildRuntimeContext injects live data (date, timezone, slots, collected_data). buildLeadHistorySection integrates F37 history into prompt. Model detection by prefix ('claude-*') future-proofs against new Claude versions. MED-7 fix auto-routes claude-* to Anthropic client, gpt-* to OpenAI.
- ⚠️ system_prompt_override (line 97 of agent_configs) bypasses validation—customer can inject instructions that conflict with JSON schema (case: '#Correto' prefix before JSON broke parse). F45 retry adds JSON reminder to user message but doesn't validate override was the culprit. safeNewMessages fallback string '[contato enviou conteúdo não processável]' is generic—lead can't distinguish image parse error from no media sent.
- 🔧 Sanitize system_prompt_override at save time (warn on conflict markers like '#Correto'). In F45 retry, detect if override field exists and log it explicitly. Enhance placeholder strings to include media type hint (e.g., '[Imagem inválida]').

**LLM Invocation with Parse Recovery (F45) — 8/10**
- ✅ F45 retry mechanism: parse_failed=true → single retry with JSON reminder before pausing. Prevents generic error message loop. Parse failure loop detection: 2 consecutive parse_failed → pause + alert (lines 1013-1053). Comprehensive token logging (prompt/completion/cached/cache_creation). Budget enforcement: truncates history if estimated >100k tokens.
- ⚠️ F45 retry uses same conversationMessages/runtimeContext from first attempt—if the parse failure was due to system_prompt_override or context order, second call likely fails identically (no variation). Parse failure counter only checks LAST execution_log row (line 1021 limit(1))—if 2 parses happened hours apart, they're treated as unrelated. No detection of parse failure DUE TO system_prompt_override conflict (could retry forever different ways).
- 🔧 Vary F45 retry by prepending strict JSON instruction to system prompt OR stripping system_prompt_override on retry. Check last N execution_logs (not just 1) to detect parse failure patterns. Add explicit override-conflict detector pre-LLM.

**Action Execution & Deduplication (HIGH-10) — 8/10**
- ✅ Dedup key across all action types (book/reschedule/update/tag/move_pipeline) — LLM can't create duplicates even if hallucinating same action twice. findExistingAppointment parallelizes 3 GHL endpoints, returns first valid future appointment. Update vs create logic tries to update existing appointment before creating new (avoids cascade duplicates). Clear error classification for booking conflicts (line 225).
- ⚠️ findExistingAppointment returns first appointment by priority of endpoints, not by recency—if contact has 2 future appointments, could reschedule the wrong one. Dedup key doesn't consider VARIATIONS in dates/times (e.g., same appointment_id but different start_time is treated as new)—if LLM retries with adjusted time, dedup incorrectly treats it as duplicate.
- 🔧 Sort findExistingAppointment results by startTime desc (most recent first). Include start_time/appointment_id pair in dedup to allow intentional reschedule requests. Add strict validation: if appointment_id provided, verify it matches the start_time before executing.

**Collected Data Sync (syncCollectedDataToGHL) — 7/10**
- ✅ Separates standard fields (contact.firstName, contact.phone) from custom fields. Respects sync_to_ghl flag per field in agent_config. Audit trail per sync attempt (success/failure logged separately). Merges with existing conversation_state data (doesn't overwrite).
- ⚠️ Standard fields use field name WITHOUT 'contact.' prefix when calling GHL API (line 1280), but collectedData keys include prefix. Mismatch possible if data_fields config has inconsistent naming. No validation that field value fits GHL field type (number field gets string, custom select gets invalid option). If one custom field fails, entire batch stops (no partial update). No retry on transient GHL error—single 5xx silently loses the sync.
- 🔧 Validate field value type matches GHL schema before syncing. Separate custom field batch by field and retry independently on 5xx. Log when field is marked sync_to_ghl=true but value is empty (silent no-op confuses admins).

**Billing & Capacity Gates — 7/10**
- ✅ trackAndCharge persists usage_record atomically (idempotency via record.id). Separates custom-key check (BYO API key) and internal team detection from charging. Hard cap enforcement: cap_blocked=true, bot continues, charge skipped, audit logged. Monthly spend calc via getMonthlySpend with month-start boundary.
- ⚠️ chargeWallet env vars (GHL_MARKETPLACE_APP_ID, GHL_BILLING_METER_ID) have no fallback—if missing, throws error and stops processing (non-blocking catch at line 1111, but original message doesn't get sent). isMonthlyCapReached checks PREVIOUS month's spend but applies to CURRENT month—if spending $50/day, cap=$100, it can go $150+ before blocking (false sense of hard cap). trackAndCharge non-blocking on billing error (line 1112) means no signal to user if wallet charge fails—lead gets message but transaction wasn't recorded.
- 🔧 Graceful GHL billing env var degradation: warn but continue (log to admin-signals). Check monthly spend start-of-month inclusive. When wallet charge fails, either retry via cron OR send lead warning message that billing failed (transparency).

**Follow-ups & Automations (reaction-engine) — 6/10**
- ✅ Dedup automations via triggered_automations array (prevents same rule firing twice per conversation). Rules split into data_field and event triggers. executeReactionRules called post-action, pre-follow-up. Comprehensive audit in execution_log.
- ⚠️ triggered_automations is updated ONCE at the end (line 1245) after executing BOTH rulesets—but if data_field rules fire and update conversation_state, then event rules fail, the triggered_automations update doesn't persist (fire-and-forget update at line 1245 has no await+error check). Follow-up scheduling checks only if config.follow_up_config?.enabled AND !objectiveCompleted AND finalStatus==='active'—if status CHANGES during turn but LLM hasn't explicitly set it, may schedule incorrectly. No protection against follow-up spam if enabled_kbs lookup hits network error (falls back to empty KB, LLM may not mention any objection, follow-up fires at default intensity).
- 🔧 Await the triggered_automations update and log failure. Resolve conversation status from response.conversation_status BEFORE deciding follow-up eligibility. Add follow-up cooldown or rate-limit per contact_id.

**Error Handling & Circuit Breakers — 6/10**
- ✅ Try-catch per major block (audio, media, GHL fetches, LLM, sync, etc). Non-blocking errors use .catch(() => {}) pattern to preserve message send. notifyCriticalError bubbles to admin-signals on group failure. Comprehensive console.error logging with context.
- ⚠️ Many non-blocking errors are silently swallowed (audio transcription error line 457, carrier RAG error line 772, handoff notify error line 834). If 5 messages in a row fail silently, admin has no alert—only visible in Vercel logs which rotate. No circuit breaker for cascading GHL timeouts (if GHL is slow, each turn in processMessageQueue spends 500ms waiting—slow queue buries real messages). Some errors throw (line 970, 1007) which pauses entire group processing, while others return silently (line 291 agent not found)—inconsistent failure semantics.
- 🔧 Aggregate non-blocking errors in requestId context and log summary at end of processGroup. Implement timeout circuit breaker: if 3 consecutive GHL calls timeout, skip remaining GHL fetches and use fallback data. Unify return-early paths vs throw to be consistent per error severity.

### Structural issues
- **[MEDIUM] Inconsistent error handling semantics: silent return vs throw vs non-blocking catch** — agent not found → return (line 291), ai_paused → return (line 312), max_messages → return (line 353) — these are early exits that skip audit logging in many cases. Contrast: aiResult.success === false → throw (line 970) which triggers group failure. Media error → non-blocking catch, message continues. No consistent policy: critical errors should throw, recoverable should return+log, transient should retry+continue. Makes debugging hard. (/src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts lines 291, 312, 353, 970, 1007, 1111)
- **[MEDIUM] GHL error responses not unified; responses can be {contact}, {contact: {contact}}, or error object** — contactSettled fetch (line 542) returns ContactResp with nested structure, but extraction (lines 661-663) assumes flat. Type guards are present but inconsistent across ghlClient.get() endpoints. Some APIs wrap in {data: {...}}, others {message: {...}}. No single normalize function. Makes adding new GHL calls error-prone. (/src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts lines 523-530, 661-663; /src/lib/queue/targeting.ts lines 100-115; /src/lib/queue/lead-history.ts lines 157-197)
- **[LOW] Lead history config defaults applied at RUNTIME in getter functions, not in DB** — agent_configs.lead_history_config and handoff_policy are JSONB with defaults in migration 00096. But code calls getLeadHistoryConfig() and getHandoffPolicy() helpers to apply runtime defaults (if null). This works but creates two sources of truth: migration defaults and getter defaults. If schema changes, must update both. Zero typing guarantee before getter runs. (/src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts lines 781-782; /src/types/agent.ts (not read, assume getLeadHistoryConfig/getHandoffPolicy in utils))
- **[LOW] Audio transcription + media processing error handling diverges** — Audio errors are caught per-message in loop (lines 428-462), transcribed text merged into aggregatedBody. Media errors collected in processedMedia[].error and merged post-process (line 487). If audio FAIL but media SUCCESS, aggregatedBody has media content but no audio context. Inconsistent error semantics. (/src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts lines 427-491)
- **[MEDIUM] No validation of conversation_state upsert conflicts; concurrent updates can lose state** — conversation_state upsert at line 631, 1031, and many places uses onConflict='agent_id,contact_id'. But the response doesn't check if update lost data (e.g., if another worker upserted simultaneously with different ai_paused_reason, the merge is undefined—which write won?). Supabase upsert on conflict doesn't provide 'rows affected' in JS SDK; silent data loss possible. (/src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts lines 631-642, 1031-1042, 1245-1249; /src/lib/ai/action-executor.ts lines 392-408)
- **[LOW] F59 history fallback (reconstructHistoryFromDb) called AFTER F52 handoff check** — F52 check (lines 589-656) uses conversationTurns fetched from GHL. If GHL returned 0 messages, F52 can't detect if last outbound was human. F59 fallback (lines 892-917) reconstructs history from our DB AFTER F52 exits. So cold-start scenario with GHL down: F52 sees empty history, can't detect human, incorrectly responds. F59 would have helped but runs too late. (/src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts lines 589-656 (F52), 892-917 (F59))
- **[LOW] should_respond skip doesn't re-test when ai_resumed_at is set** — handoff gate (lines 808-839) evaluates should_respond once per turn. If handoff decision = 'skip' + 'notify_rep', bot pauses. If rep then resumes (ai_resumed_at set), next turn will re-evaluate should_respond. But the condition that triggered skip (e.g., human_replied_recently) may still be true. should_respond doesn't check ai_resumed_at to know 'rep forced this, override heuristic'. Possible repeated notification or incorrect decisions. (/src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts lines 808-839; /src/lib/queue/should-respond.ts)
- **[MEDIUM] billing/charge.ts exports but doesn't handle ENV missing at module init** — GHL_MARKETPLACE_APP_ID and GHL_BILLING_METER_ID are checked inside chargeWallet (line 151), not at module load. If env var missing, error thrown deep in call stack. No early warning, no fallback init. If CI/CD skips env vars in deployment, issue only surfaces when first message charged. (/src/lib/billing/charge.ts lines 151-156)
- **[LOW] Dead code: checkWalletBalance always returns true; TODO comment but unreachable logic** — Lines 213-221 define checkWalletBalance but it's never called in queue-processor. Comment says 'TODO P2: implementar de verdade'. Function is dead weight (never used), creates confusion about whether wallet balance is enforced. (/src/lib/billing/charge.ts lines 213-221)
- **[MEDIUM] Conversation_state.message_count incremented only by action-executor, not all AI responses** — message_count incremented in updateConversationState (line 402 in action-executor.ts). But if response.should_send_message=false (internal-only response), still increments. max_messages cap (line 328) checks message_count >= maxMsgs. So bot can hit cap without sending any visible messages (weird UX). Also, if action-executor.ts is modified in parallel, dedup of increments could cause count loss. (/src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts line 328; /src/lib/ai/action-executor.ts line 402)

### Production blockers
- **[PARTIAL/MEDIUM] Contact fetch has no retry; single transient GHL error zeros lead context** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Line 542 calls ghlClient.get<ContactResp>(`/contacts/${group.contactId}`) without withRetry. If GHL returns 500 or timeout, contactSettled.status='rejected' (line 684), contactData stays empty object, and lead's name/email/phone/custom fields are lost from collectedData for this turn. The bot proceeds with degraded context. With high GHL traffic or maintenance window, many contacts lose context simultaneously.
  - Fix: Wrap contact fetch in withRetry(fn, {maxRetries: 2, baseDelayMs: 200, label: 'contact-fetch'}) on line 542, identical pattern to messages/slots fetches on lines 537-551.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts:542 — ghlClient.get<ContactResp>(`/contacts/${group.contactId}`) called WITHOUT withRetry(), unlike adjacent calls to conv-messages (line 537-540 with withRetry) and slots (line 544-550 with withRetry). When rejected, contactData remains {} (line 659-686), propagated to collectedData (line 690) and passed to prompt builder (line 854). However, GHLClient.retryOnAuth() (src/lib/ghl/client.ts:28-104) already implements internal retries: network errors (2×, 200ms exponential), 401 (1×), 429 (1×), 5xx transitional (2×, 300ms+600ms exponential). F59 (commit df0aaa8, 2026-06-04) added withRetry to conv-messages but explicitly omitted contact fetch, focusing cold-start risk on historical context, not contact metadata. Root risk: non-retryable failures (IAM-unsupported, permanent 404, 422) bypass GHLClient retries; transient failures hit GHLClient retries (~1100ms total 5xx path) but no external withRetry backstop like msgs/slots have.
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] GU-6 manual resume can race with F52 auto-pause detection; order undefined** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Rep clicks 'resume' (sets ai_resumed_at timestamp) while F52 fallback handoff check is running. The check (lines 589-656) reads lastOutbound from messagesSettled (already fetched earlier), compares with ai_resumed_at to decide if override applies. But if two messages arrive within <100ms and both claim the same group, both workers read convState separately, one resumes, one doesn't see the update. Result: one worker may pause despite resume being set.
  - Fix: Add distributed lock during F52 check: before reading conversation_state (line 303), acquire a short-lived lock keyed on (agent_id, contact_id). Release after F52 upsert or return. OR: reload conversation_state immediately before F52 check (not the one loaded at line 304).
  - Veredicto: src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts:303-308 fetches convState once at start of processGroup(). src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts:622-626 reads from the same stale convState object if ui-action occurred between fetch and F52 check. The override logic `const overriddenByManualResume = resumedAtMs > 0 && lastOutboundMs <= resumedAtMs` becomes false when resumedAtMs=0 (stale fetch), causing pause at line 628 despite ai_resumed_at being set in DB. Message claiming at src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts:103-110 is per-message, not per-contact, allowing separate workers to process same contact. contact-activate route.ts:108 sets ai_resumed_at = nowIso without coordinating with in-flight queue processors. No per-contact locking mechanism in message_queue schema (supabase/migrations/00005_create_message_queue.sql).
- **[PARTIAL/MEDIUM] Lead history cache (in-memory Map) lost on lambda restart; no cross-instance cache** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: cache in lead-history.ts (line 25) is a global Map<>. Each Vercel lambda has its own instance. If function restarts or auto-scales to new instance, cache is empty. Repeated calls to same contact within 5min re-fetch from GHL unnecessarily, burning quota and latency. During traffic spike, cache thrashing is likely.
  - Fix: Migrate lead history cache to Redis (KV store or Supabase Redis) with 5min TTL key pattern. Implement cache invalidation hook when ai_resumed_at is set (GU-6). Fallback to direct fetch if Redis unavailable (fail-soft).
  - Veredicto: src/lib/queue/lead-history.ts:25 defines `const cache = new Map<string, CacheEntry>()` with no Redis/persistent backing. Vercel serverless (confirmed via vercel.json, next.config.mjs, docs/RUNBOOK.md) means each instance has isolated in-memory state. Pattern acknowledged in src/lib/account-assistant/filter-engine/cache.ts:7-8 ("não é Redis, então não cross-process. Reset em deploy/restart.") and docs/DECISIONS.md NB-2 ("inFlightMessages Map é per-lambda"). Function `invalidateLeadHistoryCache` exported at lead-history.ts:28 but never called anywhere in codebase (verified via grep). Calls to `loadLeadHistory` at queue-processor.ts:784-789 happen on every lead message. However, fail-soft error handling at lead-history.ts:276-281 catches GHL fetch errors and returns empty context rather than crashing. Multi-lambda cache miss triggers re-fetch (expensive, not fatal). `invalidateLeadHistoryCache` dead code suggests feature incomplete rather than broken.
- **[PARTIAL/MEDIUM] F45 parse recovery retry doesn't differentiate root cause; may loop identically** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: F45 (lines 982-1002) retries with JSON reminder appended to newMessages, but if system_prompt_override contains conflicting instructions (e.g., 'output #Correto before JSON'), the retry uses identical systemPrompt and will fail identically. Parse failure loop detection (lines 1013-1025) only checks last 1 execution_log row—if 2 failures are hours apart, treated as unrelated, no pause. Customer override can cause indefinite loops.
  - Fix: On F45 retry, detect if system_prompt_override exists and is marked risky (contains '#' or 'format' keywords). If so, strip it and retry. OR: replace entire systemPrompt with minimal valid one for retry. Check last 5 execution_log rows for parse_failed=true in any order, not just consecutive (looser loop detection).
  - Veredicto: src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts:982-1055 — F45 retry (lines 984-996) appends JSON reminder to newMessages but uses identical systemPrompt, responseSchema, and model. For Claude models processing system_prompt_override content, system-level instructions override user-message-level reminders, making retry ineffective if override conflicts with JSON output (e.g., "output #Correto before JSON"). Loop detection (lines 1013-1025) queries execution_log with .order("created_at", {ascending: false}).limit(1) — checks ONLY immediately preceding ai_processing log, no time-window filter. Pause DOES trigger on 2 consecutive failures (line 1026), preventing infinite loops, but retry is wasted effort and detection is not timestamp-bounded.
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] GHL billing env vars (GHL_MARKETPLACE_APP_ID, GHL_BILLING_METER_ID) missing → hard error, charge skipped** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: chargeWallet (line 151-156) throws Error if env vars missing. This is caught as non-blocking in queue-processor line 1111, but the original message was already sent to lead. No retry via cron. If Vercel env vars didn't sync (rare), all charges fail silently, revenue leak. No alert to Pedro.
  - Fix: Check env vars once on module load (charge.ts top level). If missing, set flag BILLING_ENV_UNCONFIGURED=true. In trackAndCharge, if flag is true, log critical error via notifyCriticalError (not just console.error). Fail-closed until admin fixes env vars.
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] Hand-off notification (notifyRepViaSparkbot) fails silently if rep unresolved; no error bubbled** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: handoff-notify.ts lines 157-162: resolveOwnerRep returns null if no rep found. Caller returns {notified: false, skipped_reason: 'no_owner_resolved'} without throwing. In queue-processor line 822-836, this is caught and logged as 'skipped', not 'failed'. If the location has no active rep (all internal or no terms accepted), no notification ever reaches human. Leads get silenced with no handoff escalation.
  - Fix: If handoff notification is enabled (policy.notify_rep_via_sparkbot=true) but rep unresolved, treat as error: either throw and pause conversation, or log critical alert. Alternatively, fallback notify to location admin or shared inbox (TODO feature).
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] triggered_automations update is fire-and-forget; failed write not detected** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Line 1245-1249: supabase.from('conversation_state').update({triggered_automations: merged}) is called without await or error handling. If write fails (RLS, constraint, quota), the dedup set is not persisted. On next turn, same automations can fire again (no safety net). Especially critical for send_text_fixed automation that could spam lead.
  - Fix: Await the triggered_automations update. If it fails, log via notifyCriticalError and manually re-fetch to rebuild dedup set OR throw to pause conversation with reason 'automation_dedup_lost'.
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] No circuit breaker for slow/timeout GHL endpoints; queue can become gridlocked** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Each processGroup call fetches 3 GHL endpoints in parallel (lines 532-551).
