If GHL service is slow (200-300ms per call), but one endpoint hangs (>1s), allSettled waits for all 3 to finish. With 100 concurrent messages in queue, if 10% timeout, total time = 1s × 100 = 100s before queue processes anything. Queue backs up, messages age, retries accumulate. No backpressure or timeout override.
  - Fix: Set hard timeout per GHL endpoint: Promise.race([ghlClient.get(...), timeout(5000)]). If timeout, reject immediately, don't wait. OR: implement adaptive timeout: track p95 latency of each endpoint and set timeout = p95 + 2s. Skip fetch if endpoint has been timing out (open circuit breaker).
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] Distributed race condition: two workers claim same message group, both proceed to executeActions** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Atomic claim at line 103-110 marks messages as 'processing', but the claim + processGroup call is not atomic. Between claim (lines 103-110) and processGroup entry (line 192), another worker can claim the SAME group if grouped by (agent_id, contact_id) which was claimed but message_ids not in the second worker's batch. Result: same contact gets TWO simultaneous message responses (book two appointments, charge twice).
  - Fix: Include the claimed message IDs in the grouping key, not just agent_id+contact_id. OR: add a 'processing' lock on conversation_state (agent_id, contact_id) to prevent concurrent processGroup calls. OR: re-check message status inside processGroup before proceeding (early escape if another worker already marked processing).


---

## Agentes lead-facing — prompt motor & plataforma modular

O subsistema de agentes lead-facing (vendas, recrutamento, custom) implementa a Plataforma Modular em três camadas: (1) assembler de prompt que monta system_prompt a partir de templates + fragmentos de módulos; (2) registry de módulos que define comportamento/tools por tipo de agente; (3) entitlement gate que controla acesso via feature flags e liberações manuais. O fluxo é: wizard cria AgentSpec → builder/commit valida e persiste agent + agent_configs + agent_module_instances → queue-processor carrega agente e monta prompt via assembler ou builder legado conforme AGENT_MOTOR_UNIFIED flag. Lead history (F37) optionally injetada no prompt. O sistema está maioritariamente funcional em OFF-mode (flags desligadas, usa builders legados), mas crítico bloqueado em ON-mode quando custom_agent é ligado: queue-processor não carrega module_keys antes de chamar assembler, causando erro em runtime.

### Funcionalidades

**Entitlement Gate (AGENT_ENTITLEMENTS_ENFORCED) — 8/10**
- ✅ Flag-aware design (default OFF = log-first); SparkBot corretamente marcado como incluso/grátis; lead-facing (sales/recruitment/custom) bloqueado sem liberação ativa; admin bypass funciona; testes do gate em test-entitlement-gate.ts cobrindo matriz completa.
- ⚠️ UI admin pra liberação manual ainda não implementada (v1 é script CLI grant-entitlement.ts); confusão potencial: no /api/agents rota OLD, o schema rejeita custom_agent (correto pra aquela rota), mas admin poderia tentar via API debugando payload; entitlement não checa expiração no runtime (apenas na leitura no repo), pode servir agente expirado se a flag foi setada antes de expiração.
- 🔧 Implementar UI de liberação em /hub/admin antes de ligar AGENT_ENTITLEMENTS_ENFORCED. Validar expiração em checkAgentEntitlement retornando null pra expirados. Documentar que admin precisa usar /api/agent-platform/builder/commit pra custom agents, não /api/agents.

**Prompt Assembly — Seeds (sales_agent, recruitment_agent) — 9/10**
- ✅ Paridade perfeita entre motor unificado (assembler) e builders legados — test-sales-parity.ts cobre 5 variantes e passa. Assembler delega ao buildSystemPrompt, zero drift. Seções de prompt bem organizadas (behavior, identity, objective, recruitment rules, tones, qualification, booking, feedback, KB, custom instructions, response format). Lead history (F37) injetado naturalmente antes de admin instructions. Override de prompt respected com guardrails. Media handling (audio transcription, image analysis, PDF) mapeado com conditional rendering.
- ⚠️ Test-sales-parity é MANUAL (roda via tsx script, não em CI). Teste de recruitment específico (recruitment_agent NUNCA deve usar linguagem comercial) não isolado — corre junto com sales em matrix. Se future refactoring descompõe a prompt em módulos (fase futura), risco de reintroduzir drift — não há guard rail automático no build.
- 🔧 Integrar test-sales-parity em CI/CD (GitHub Actions). Criar test isolado específico pra recruitment (verificar ausência de 'contrato', 'venda', 'apólice'). Documentar a ordem das sections e dependências pra facilitar future modularization.

**Prompt Assembly — Custom Agents (CRÍTICO BLOQUEADO) — 2/10**
- ✅ Arquitetura conceitualmente correta: assembleLeadFromModules (linha 40-49 em assembler.ts) compõe prompt iterando moduleKeys e chamando LEAD_MODULE_FRAGMENTS[key]. Fragmentos lead-facing implementados para 6 módulos: behavior, qualification, scheduling, channel, knowledge, followup. buildLeadMetaInstruction() prepend automaticamente.
- ⚠️ CRÍTICO: queue-processor NÃO carrega agent_module_instances antes de chamar assembleSystemPrompt (linhas 871-877). Quando AGENT_MOTOR_UNIFIED está ON e agente.type === 'custom_agent', passa moduleKeys = undefined → assembler linha 100 throws erro. Isso quebra TODOS os custom agents assim que a flag liga. Nenhum teste de runtime pra custom_agent + AGENT_MOTOR_UNIFIED. Custom agents podem ser criados (wizard + builder/commit criam agent_module_instances), mas não podem responder em conversa com a flag ON.
- 🔧 IMMEDIATE FIX: Antes de linha 871, adicionar: const moduleKeys = agent.type === 'custom_agent' ? (await getAgentModuleInstances(supabase, agent.id)).map(i => i.module_key) : undefined; e passar moduleKeys no input. Testar: criar custom_agent via /builder/commit, simular conversa com AGENT_MOTOR_UNIFIED=1, verificar resposta. Adicionar test-custom-agent-motor.ts analogamente a test-sales-parity.

**Module Registry & Lead Fragments — 7/10**
- ✅ 6 módulos lead-facing têm fragmento implementado (behavior, qualification, scheduling, channel, knowledge, followup — linhas 152-173 em sales-prompt-builder.ts). Fragmentos reutilizam section functions privadas (source única, zero fork). Módulos sem fragmento (compliance, active_hours, crm_ops) silenciosamente skippados no assembler (linha 44). Registry em TypeScript (modules/registry.ts) mapeia módulos rep-facing (sparkbot). Migration 00075 seeds catálogo completo no DB.
- ⚠️ compliance, active_hours, crm_ops marcados como 'seed' e listados no default_modules dos templates sales/recruitment, mas NÃO têm fragmento lead-facing implementado. Quando esses módulos são ligados num custom agent, assembler continue (ignore) mas nenhum conteúdo é injetado — o agente nasce sem as regras anti-spam/janela de tempo, sem avisar ao admin. Processamento completo dos módulos (prompt + tools) ainda em Fase 2 — hoje é só prompt fragment. spec → moduleKeys derivação confusa: specToConfig linha 337 adiciona módulos 'derived' baseado na config, depois faz union com user-specified + baseline — risco de módulos multiplicarem silenciosamente ou ficarem orphans.
- 🔧 Implementar fragmentos para compliance, active_hours no lead-facing (Fase 2). Adicionar validação em assembleLeadFromModules: se um módulo na composição não tem fragmento, logar warning. Documentar em AgentModuleInstance schema quando um módulo é 'partially implemented'. Refatorar specToConfig pra clareza: separar 'derived' de 'user' em resultado estruturado.

**Tool Resolver (Module-based) — 5/10**
- ✅ Função pura resolveModuleToolKeys bem estruturada (linhas 20-35 em tool-resolver.ts), com deduplicação, ordenação, disabled set. Testável sem efeitos colaterais. Input é simples: moduleInstances[], disabledTools[], baseTools[].
- ⚠️ Não está integrada no queue-processor: tool selection ainda usa registry global completo (vendor legado) — resolveModuleToolKeys é dead code em runtime. Se um custom_agent liga só alguns módulos (ex: 'behavior' + 'scheduling'), o agente ainda pode chamar tools de módulos que não tem. Isto é menos crítico que prompt (porque executa ações permissionadas), mas viola o design intent de composição limpa. ResolveModuleToolKeys não foi testado com dados reais.
- 🔧 Integrar tool resolution no queue-processor: após carregar agent_module_instances, passar ao processWithAI como allowedTools. Criar test-tool-resolver.ts com 10+ cenários. Documentar em custom_agent creation que não há isolamento de tools hoje (Fase 2).

**Custom Agent Creation (wizard → builder/commit) — 8/10**
- ✅ Fluxo limpo: agent-wizard.tsx coleta Answers → /compose pré-processa (AI enriquece conteúdo) → /commit valida AgentSpec contra zod schema → specToConfig derivado módulos sensatos. Agent nasce pausado (inactive) — admin revisa antes de ativar. Todas as pieces criadas atômicamente: agent + agent_configs + agent_module_instances. Fallback de data_fields sensato.
- ⚠️ wizard.tsx complexo (700+ linhas), múltiplas etapas acopladas. Sem validação client-side de intakes. Builder /compose IA-enriquecido chama Claude — nenhum rate limit ou erro handling explicit. Timezone na config herdado do location sem NULL check — quebra em runtime se location.timezone é NULL. Teste de custom_agent creation end-to-end (wizard → activate → responder msg) não existe em CI — só scripts manuais.
- 🔧 Validação client-side de IntakeMode: tag mode precisa ≥1 tag; stage mode precisa stage_id; outreach mode precisa opening_message. Timeout + fallback em /compose (timeout 10s, volta default se AI falha). Validate location.timezone NOT NULL antes de criar config. Adicionar e2e test: create custom_agent, activate, enviar fake msg, verificar resposta.

**Paridade Motor Unificado (sparkbot rep-facing) — 9/10**
- ✅ test-motor-parity.ts cobre 7 variantes (default, confirmation modes, channels, tones, custom instructions, locales) — todos passam. Assembler delega 100% ao buildSparkbotSystemPrompt. Zero drift risk enquanto delega. Quando ON-mode future decompose modules, parity test garante safety gate.
- ⚠️ Teste roda via manual tsx script, não em CI. Variantes cobrem extremos mas não cobertura média (ex: nenhuma combo de [tones reais + custom_instructions + locale]). Sparkbot ainda NÃO é integrado no motor unificado (webhook-handler ainda chama prompt-builder direto). Flag AGENT_MOTOR_UNIFIED está wired pra queue-processor (lead-facing) mas não pro webhook-handler (rep-facing), inconsistência.
- 🔧 Rodar test-motor-parity em CI pré-deploy. Aumentar coverage: matriz cartesiana (tones × custom_instructions × locale). Integrar Sparkbot no motor via flag (quando pronto). Renomear flag pra AGENT_UNIFIED_MOTOR_ENABLED (mais claro que está para ambas as audiências eventualmente).

**Lead History Loading (F37 — Lead Awareness) — 7/10**
- ✅ loadLeadHistory() fetches contact history desde Spark Leads (tags, opps, recent msgs, notes). Injetado em PromptContext.leadHistory → buildLeadHistorySection() monta resumo legível. Opt-in via config.lead_history_config.enabled. Fail-soft: se fetch falha, continua sem histórico. F59 fallback implementado: se Spark Leads vem vazio mas conversação known, reconstructHistoryFromDb reclama histórico local.
- ⚠️ loadLeadHistory não testado com falhas de rede/timeouts reais. Se Spark Leads retorna truncado, agente fica com contexto incompleto sem saber. Tamanho do histórico no prompt não capped (só limita a 10 msgs recentes + 5 notas, mas opp + tags não limitados) — prompt pode inchar se contact tem 50+ tags/opps. LeadContext type não explicitamente exported em agent.ts.
- 🔧 Testar loadLeadHistory com Spark Leads API mocked (timeout, 500 error, empty result). Implementar cap em opp count (últimas 5 opps por stage status). Export LeadContext type in @/types/agent. Log warning se histórico truncado.

**Builder Spec & Validation (AgentSpecSchema) — 7/10**
- ✅ AgentSpec schema usa zod, validação forte (name ≥1 char, tone 0-100, modules checked contra allowed). Captura intake modes (inbound/tag/stage/keyword/outreach), objective variants, scheduling details, advanced targeting rules. specToConfig derivação sensata (moduleKeys deduped com baseline, fieldDefs slugged corretamente). Quiet hours (Fase 3.1) capturado.
- ⚠️ AdvancedTargetingRule schema há id (UUID string) mas specToConfig gera novo id cada vez (rid()) — possibilidade de duplicação se spec é re-committed. qualification_fields max 15 sem justificativa. Tone schema usa 'assertiveness' mas em TS codebase é 'aggressiveness' (naming mismatch). conversational_examples cap 8000 chars alinhado com validation.ts mas não centralizado. Nenhuma validação que modules estejam em allowedModuleKeys até depois de spec validar (race condition).
- 🔧 Remover id de AdvancedTargetingRule schema (generated server-side). Documentar hard limits. Rename tone.assertiveness → tone.aggressiveness em schema. Centralizar todos os caps em única const enum. Validação de moduleKeys contra catálogo dentro de specToConfig, não depois.

**Runtime Execution — Message Queue Processing — 7/10**
- ✅ Queue processor bem estruturado: agents grouped by (agent_id, contact_id) — sales + recruitment não mixam mesmo contato. Reaper logic reseta orphan 'processing' msgs após 5min. Atomic claim via UPDATE...RETURNING elimina race conditions. F59 (history reconstruction) implementado. F52 (targeting gate) antes do LLM. F37 (lead history loading) injected. Conversation status tracking funciona.
- ⚠️ CRÍTICO pra custom_agent: moduleKeys não carregadas. Se custom_agent + AGENT_MOTOR_UNIFIED=1, assembleSystemPrompt throws. Sem recovery — msg marcada failed. Entitlement check NÃO roda no queue — só na creation. Se admin revoga entitlement depois, agente continua respondendo. Media processing não integrado em leading fragments.
- 🔧 IMMEDIATE: Fix custom_agent moduleKeys loading. Adicionar entitlement check em processGroup (se capabilidade rativada, skip e log, não fail msg). Integrar media context naturalmente em prompt.

### Structural issues
- **[MEDIUM] Dead code: resolveModuleToolKeys in tool-resolver.ts** — Function é well-written e testable, mas nunca chamada em runtime. queue-processor não invoca. Bloqueia tool resolution part da modular platform (Fase 2). Atualmente benign, mas indica incomplete integration. (src/lib/agent-platform/tool-resolver.ts (lines 20-35); NOT invoked em src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts)
- **[LOW] Naming mismatch: tone.assertiveness in schema vs tone.aggressiveness in code** — AgentSpecSchema (builder-spec.ts) define tone como {creativity, formality, naturalness, assertiveness}. Mas em sales-prompt-builder.ts e agent types, field é 'tone_aggressiveness'. Maintainability risk: confusão futura se alguém adiciona tone variant. (src/lib/agent-platform/builder-spec.ts:195 (assertiveness) vs src/lib/ai/sales-prompt-builder.ts:530 (tone_aggressiveness))
- **[LOW] Prompt size caps scattered across 3 files sem central definition** — CUSTOM_INSTRUCTIONS_CAP = 8000 (sales-prompt-builder.ts:920), CONVERSATION_EXAMPLES_CAP = 8000, max em AgentSpecSchema = 8000, max em validation.ts = 8000. Single source of truth needed. (src/lib/ai/sales-prompt-builder.ts, src/lib/agent-platform/builder-spec.ts, src/lib/utils/validation.ts, src/types/agent.ts)
- **[LOW] Advanced targeting rules (AdvancedTargetingRule) generates UUID on each specToConfig call** — Em builder-spec.ts linha 318-324, novo UUID (rid()) é gerado cada vez que specToConfig processa mesmo spec. Se spec é re-submitted, targets ganham duplicate IDs. Server-side ID generation seria cleaner. (src/lib/agent-platform/builder-spec.ts:318 (rid() call), schema definition linha 47-55)
- **[MEDIUM] Timezone inheritance bug: location.timezone pode ser NULL** — Em builder/commit (builder/commit/route.ts:101-104), timezone é setado de location.timezone sem NULL check. Se location não tem timezone, agente nasce com NULL em working_hours/active_hours/quiet_hours timezone field — breaks runtime calculations. Fix existe em specToConfig mas não bulletproof. (src/app/api/agent-platform/builder/commit/route.ts:103-104; src/lib/agent-platform/builder-spec.ts:398)
- **[LOW] Media context not integrated into lead-facing prompt fragments** — buildMediaInstructionsSection existe em sales-prompt-builder.ts (linhas 638-665) e é included em buildSystemPrompt(), mas NÃO em LEAD_MODULE_FRAGMENTS['behavior'] ou 'channel'. Quando custom agent + AGENT_MOTOR_UNIFIED usa assembleLeadFromModules, media instructions faltam. (src/lib/ai/sales-prompt-builder.ts:152-173 (LEAD_MODULE_FRAGMENTS); media section NOT em channel fragment (line 170))
- **[MEDIUM] No validation que moduleKeys em spec existem em allowed catalog** — specToConfig (builder-spec.ts:344) filtra module contra allowedModuleKeys, mas allowedModuleKeys vem de listModules() no create time. Se catalog muda entre UI submit e backend validate, spec pode ser processado com stale module list. (src/app/api/agent-platform/builder/commit/route.ts:75 (listModules call timing); src/lib/agent-platform/builder-spec.ts:344)

### Production blockers
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] Custom agent runtime crash when AGENT_MOTOR_UNIFIED=1** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: queue-processor.ts linha 871-877 chama assembleSystemPrompt com moduleKeys undefined para custom agents. assembler.ts linha 100 throws error 'moduleKeys (custom) exige...'. Nenhum recovery — msg marcada failed. Qualquer custom agent + unified motor flag = conversas quebradas.
  - Fix: Load agent_module_instances antes de assembleSystemPrompt: const moduleKeys = agent.type === 'custom_agent' ? (await getAgentModuleInstances(supabase, agent.id)).map(i => i.module_key) : undefined; linha 869. Add moduleKeys to assembleSystemPrompt input. Test: create custom_agent, activate, send message, verify response. Adicionar test-custom-agent-motor.ts test suite.
  - Veredicto: assembler.ts:100-105 throws error when audience='lead' && leadArgs && !moduleKeys for custom agents. queue-processor.ts:870-875 never passes moduleKeys when calling assembleSystemPrompt. assembler.ts:111-122 templateKeyForAgentType('custom_agent') returns 'custom_agent' (default case), which doesn't match known seed templates in switch at line 82-97. Test coverage gap: test-sales-parity.ts only tests sales_agent and recruitment_agent, not custom_agent.
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] Incomplete module implementation — compliance, active_hours, crm_ops sem lead-facing fragments** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: Migration 00075 seeds 9 módulos. Apenas 6 têm LEAD_MODULE_FRAGMENTS implementados. Quando custom_agent liga compliance/active_hours/crm_ops, assembleLeadFromModules silenciosamente ignora. Agente nasce sem anti-spam rules, janela de tempo, ou integração CRM — sem avisar ao admin.
  - Fix: Implementar fragmentos lead-facing pra compliance (opt-out language, rate limits), active_hours (janela de funcionamento), crm_ops (se applicable) em sales-prompt-builder.ts. Ou, se intenção é deixar incomplete: adicionar validação que warn em assembleLeadFromModules se module não tem fragment.
  - Veredicto: supabase/migrations/00075_modular_agent_platform.sql:136-146 (9 módulos seeded) + src/lib/ai/sales-prompt-builder.ts:152-173 (apenas 6 LEAD_MODULE_FRAGMENTS implementados; compliance/active_hours/crm_ops ausentes) + src/lib/agent-platform/assembler.ts:40-49 (assembleLeadFromModules faz continue silencioso para módulos sem fragmento) + _planning/plataforma-modular/PLANO.md:91 (confirms compliance precisa conteúdo) + sem testes validando se catálogo tem fragmentos implementados
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] No runtime tool resolution — custom agents can call tools from modules they don't have** (conf: medium)
  - Porquê: resolveModuleToolKeys (tool-resolver.ts) é pure function, nunca chamada em queue-processor. Tool selection usa global registry. Custom agent com só 'behavior' + 'scheduling' pode invocar update_field, add_tag, move_pipeline tools (de outros módulos) porque LLM vê full registry.
  - Fix: Load module_instances → extract allowed tools via resolveModuleToolKeys → pass allowedTools to processWithAI. Guards against tool leakage em custom agents. Menos crítico que prompt (tools são permissioned), mas viola modularity design.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/agent-platform/tool-resolver.ts:34-48 — function defined but never imported/called in production. src/lib/ai/sales-prompt-builder.ts:1041-1154 — buildResponseJsonSchema() hardcodes all action types in anyOf schema (lines 1083 update_field, 1093 add_tag, 1108 book_appointment, 1123 reschedule_appointment, 1133 move_pipeline) without filtering by agent modules. src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts:878 — responseSchema = buildResponseJsonSchema(promptCtx) called without resolveModuleToolKeys. Grep shows resolveModuleToolKeys never imported anywhere except test script.
- **[PARTIAL/MEDIUM] No CI integration for sales/recruitment prompt parity tests** (conf: medium)
  - Porquê: test-sales-parity.ts e test-motor-parity.ts são manual tsx scripts (não rodam em GitHub Actions). Se future refactoring decompose prompt modules, drift pode passar review. Sem automated regression gate.
  - Fix: Add npm script npm run test:parity → run both parity tests em série, fail se qualquer variante drifta. Integrate into pre-deploy CI check. Add test-custom-agent-motor.ts para custom agent composition.
  - Veredicto: scripts/test-sales-parity.ts:1-7 (manual tsx script, no CI); scripts/test-motor-parity.ts:1-8 (manual tsx script, no CI); package.json:6-10 (no test script in npm); vercel.json:1-12 (no build hooks); next.config.mjs:1-57 (no test integration); .github/: zero workflows exist (confirmed via `curl api.github.com/repos/pedropoleza/spark-ai-platform/actions/workflows`); CLAUDE.md Guard rail section explicitly states tests are manual prerequisite before flag activation; src/lib/agent-platform/assembler.ts:7-11 documents parity tests as "guard rail"; PLANO.md Fase 1 exit criterion: "paridade 7/7 + tsc/build verdes ✅"


---

## Agentes lead-facing — sistema de follow-up

The project implements TWO separate follow-up systems running in parallel: (A) OLD "scheduled_followups" system for lead-facing agents (sales/recruitment) triggered per-message from queue-processor.ts, using flat FollowUpConfig JSONB and a cron-driven scheduler; (B) NEW "followup_sequences" system designed for SparkBot (rep-facing) with sophisticated spam scoring, approval gating, and modular core service. Both exist in the same codebase, targeting different audiences, but neither is fully production-ready. System A has a 3-week critical bug (F46, fixed 2026-06-04), a fundamental duplicate-sequence issue (F47, unfixed), and dangerous silent error handling. System B is feature-rich but incomplete (spam recheck stub, webhook placeholders, lead-facing implementation planned but not done).

### Funcionalidades

**System A (Old): scheduled_followups scheduling — 5/10**
- ✅ Cancels previous pending follow-ups before creating new batch (line 31-36 follow-up-scheduler.ts). Has DND/opted-out checks before sending. Integrates retries into processWithAI. Logs execution to execution_log for thumbs/handoff detection.
- ⚠️ CRITICAL: Creates entire new sequence (N follow-ups) on every message turn without deduplication across turns (F47 migration comment 'observado: 80 follow-ups pra 1 contato após 8 turnos'). Silent error handling: supabase-js returns {error} not throw, code doesn't check—F46 bug silenced failed UPDATEs for 3 weeks (May 12—June 4, 2026). No validation that follow_up_config matches agent type (sales vs recruitment). Hardcodes SMS/WhatsApp routing logic (line 273-295) duplicated from bulk-messages. No idempotency key on sent messages—double-send possible if runner crashes.
- 🔧 (1) Deduplicate: contact_id+location_id should have at most 1 ACTIVE sequence (pending/scheduled/running). Store ONE set of attempts, advance timer on silence, not restart. (2) Error handling: wrap supabase updates in `if (result.error)` checks per CLAUDE.md anti-pattern #1. (3) Type safety: validate follow_up_config.mode against agent.type. (4) Extract sendFollowupMessage logic to shared util (DRY vs bulk-message-runner). (5) Test: add integration test verifying 8+ silent turns produce only 1 sequence per contact, not 8.

**System A: processScheduledFollowUps (cron runner) — 6/10**
- ✅ Atomic claim via UPDATE...RETURNING (line 122-129). Checks conversation completion status + stale + ai_paused_at gates (line 142-167). Detects lead reply post-scheduling (line 206-224) and cancels sequence. Retries GHL fetch with withRetry + fallback to DB history reconstruction (F59 fix 2026-06-04). Billing tracked per follow-up attempt.
- ⚠️ Limited to 20 per tick (line 129 MAX_PER_TICK in follow-up-scheduler; hardcoded, no tuning per location). If conversation_state doesn't exist (new contact), doesn't fallback gracefully. No poison pill handling—if GHL get() fails consistently, follow-up gets marked 'failed' but not retried later (stuck in failed state). No metrics/instrumentation on pause-on-reply working vs missing. LIMIT 20 means with 100+ backlog follow-ups might never clear at 30s tick rate.
- 🔧 (1) Make MAX_PER_TICK configurable per agent or based on backlog size. (2) Add metrics: counters for claim failures, send errors by reason, reply-detected vs timeout-completed. (3) For 'failed' status, implement exponential-backoff retry (like message_queue does) rather than permanent stuck. (4) Add observation: if runner consistently returns {sent:0, errors:N}, alert admins (poison pill detector).

**System B (New): followup_sequences feature completeness — 7/10**
- ✅ Well-structured modular core (followup/core.ts, types.ts, 8 separate service modules). Sophisticated spam scoring with LLM refinement (spam-score.ts). Robust approval flow: auto/manual per risk (adaptive mode). Safety checks include opt-out, duplicate active sequence dedup (countActiveSequences), wallet blocking. History reconstruction (F59) backed in. Tools layer with 8 chat functions (create, approve, cancel, pause, resume, edit, list, progress). Atomic claim in followup-runner (line 106-118). Contact disambiguation + error handling in core.
- ⚠️ INCOMPLETE for production: (1) Spam recheck on message send is stubbed—line 172 'TODO MVP v2 — pra MVP skip' (requires_final_check never evaluated). (2) Webhook trigger entry point designed (source_metadata prepared) but NOT IMPLEMENTED (migration says 'futuro'). (3) LEAD-FACING not done: designed for SparkBot (rep-facing), but has NOT been wired into queue-processor for sales/recruitment agents. (4) Lead-history loading + should-respond checks from F37 (2026-05-29) NOT connected to followup/core (separate concern but architectural drift). (5) No persistence of approval decisions in execution_log (createFollowupRequest→persistSequence doesn't log approval event). (6) sequence-notifier (line 233 dynamic import in runner) might fail silently. (7) Settings loader (line 66 loadFollowupSettings) tries agent_id first but NO FALLBACK if agent deleted—returns hardcoded defaults without warning.
- 🔧 (1) Implement requires_final_check in followup-runner (recalc spam_score pre-send, skip if 'high'). (2) Design + implement webhook trigger entry (stage_changed event from GHL pipeline). (3) DECISION: keep followup_sequences ONLY for SparkBot OR migrate sales/recruitment TO followup_sequences (unify both systems). (4) Wire lead-history + should-respond checks into followup core if skipping is desired. (5) Add execution_log entries for create/approve/reject/pause events (audit trail). (6) Test sequence-notifier is async-safe (import + await pattern is resilient). (7) Add explicit warning when agent_id lookup fails in settings-loader.

**System A+B Coexistence: Configuration drift — 3/10**
- ✅ Both systems use agent_configs table (no data duplication). System B has clean column names (followup_feature_enabled, etc.) per SQL patterns. System A's follow_up_config JSONB is self-contained (schema versioning possible via { version: 1 }).
- ⚠️ CRITICAL CONFUSION: (1) Agent can have both follow_up_config (old) AND followup_feature_enabled (new) set simultaneously. Runtime doesn't enforce mutual exclusion. (2) FollowUpConfig.mode='ai_auto|manual' completely different from followup_approval_mode='adaptive|always_ask|auto_low_risk|auto_all'—code mixing these is a bug waiting to happen. (3) agent_configs columns are flat (followup_feature_enabled BOOLEAN) but old system uses JSONB structure—schema mismatch risk. (4) No migration path documented: if admin enables new system, does old system auto-disable? Unknown. (5) Default values inconsistent: System A defaults follow_up_config.enabled=true (CLAUDE.md missing), System B defaults followup_feature_enabled=true—both on means double-scheduling. (6) Tools in /lib/account-assistant/tools/followup.ts reference agent type but no guard against sales_agent accidentally using SparkBot-only config.
- 🔧 (1) Add explicit mutual-exclusion gate: if followup_feature_enabled && follow_up_config.enabled, log error + disable System A. (2) Create migration: backfill legacy agents (follow_up_config.enabled=true) with followup_feature_enabled=false. (3) Add UI validation in agent-configs: radio button 'Follow-up system: Disabled | Legacy (scheduled_followups) | Modern (followup_sequences)', enforce one-only. (4) Rename: System B columns s/followup_approval_mode/sequence_approval_mode/ to distinguish. (5) Add config load test: verify only one system active per agent_id + location_id combo.

**Error handling: silent failures — 4/10**
- ✅ F52 (2026-06-04) implements history fallback when GHL fetch fails—cold-start now safe. F59 implements history reconstruction from DB. withRetry() wrapper used for GHL calls. execution_log insertion is wrapped try-catch with non-blocking semantics (line 358-380 follow-up-scheduler).
- ⚠️ CRITICAL: supabase-js update() doesn't throw on error—returns { error: {...} }, which code silently ignores throughout (F46 bug—silent failure for 3 weeks). Line 31-36 (follow-up-scheduler.ts) cancels previous: no error check. Line 44-76 (insert): no error check. Line 425 (mark sent): no error check. EVERY update/insert in both systems vulnerable. (2) processScheduledFollowUps returns {sent, errors} without distinguishing error types (claim failure vs send failure vs GHL timeout)—admin can't diagnose. (3) contactRepliedAfter (line 305-343) returns false on ANY error (fail-open), which means pause-on-reply silently broken if GHL is down.
- 🔧 (1) Audit all supabase calls: wrap in explicit `if (result.error)` checks (per CLAUDE.md). Create lint rule / pre-commit hook. (2) Use typed error enums instead of boolean returns: { ok: true, messageId } | { ok: false, reason: 'ghl_timeout' | 'claim_collision', retryable: boolean }. (3) For pause-on-reply, fail-CLOSED: if can't verify reply, assume contact replied (pause conservatively). (4) Return detailed error breakdown from runner: { sent, errors, errorBreakdown: { claim_failed, send_failed, ghl_timeout, ... } }.

**Idempotency: duplicate sends — 5/10**
- ✅ System B (followup_runner) claims via atomic UPDATE with claim_token + claimed_at (line 106-118). Execution_log insertion includes ghl_message_id deduplication. System A checks DND per contact before sending (line 169-203).
- ⚠️ System A (scheduled_followups): no ghl_message_id stored—if runner claims msg and crashes after send but before DB update, next runner tick re-sends (duplicate on retry). No unique constraint on (agent_id, contact_id, scheduled_at, attempt_number) so if claim fails race-condition-style, two processes might send same attempt. (2) System B stores ghl_message_id but only AFTER successful send—if send succeeds but process dies before UPDATE, next tick re-sends. (3) Neither system uses idempotency key in GHL API call—GHL /conversations/messages endpoint likely doesn't deduplicate client-side, so backend must. (4) Claim token expires only implicitly (marked 'processing' forever if process dies)—no lease timeout.
- 🔧 (1) For System A: insert ghl_message_id BEFORE send via GHL, use ghl_message_id as UNIQUE key in scheduled_followups. OR store sentAt + ghl_message_id returned from GHL then do INSERT...ON CONFLICT UPDATE. (2) Implement claim lease timeout: reaper should reset 'processing' > 2min (not 5min) to be conservative. (3) Add test: send scheduled follow-up, kill process before DB update, restart—verify no duplicate send to GHL. (4) For GHL calls, pass idempotency key in request (if API supports—check GHL docs).

**Billing integration (follow-up messages) — 6/10**
- ✅ System A tracks follow-up cost via trackAndCharge() (line 356-380 follow-up-scheduler.ts). Checks for custom OpenAI API key and skips charge if present. Billings are tagged action_type='follow_up'. Cached tokens tracked (result.cached_tokens).
- ⚠️ System B has NO billing integration—createFollowupRequest → generateSequence calls processWithAI but never calls trackAndCharge. Follow-ups generated by System B LLM consume tokens but don't increment usage_records—invisible to billing dashboard. (2) System A's billingtracking happens AFTER message is sent but skipped on error (line 381: non-blocking catch). If trackAndCharge fails, message was sent but not charged—no audit trail of cost. (3) cap_blocked enforcement not checked in either system—can generate/send follow-ups even if location hit monthly spend cap. (4) Estimator comment (line 356) says '30% leads × 5 follow-ups × $0.005 = $22.50/mês/location' but no validation that follow_up_config.max_attempts <= reasonable limit (could config 100 attempts = $7.50/lead if unlucky).
- 🔧 (1) System B: add trackAndCharge call in core.ts generateSequence or runner on send (decide if cost at generation or send—send is safer). (2) For System A: move trackAndCharge BEFORE send, fail message if billing fails (critical cost control). (3) Add hard cap: max_attempts = min(config.max_attempts, 10) at config validation time (already done line 57 follow-up-scheduler, good). (4) Add monthly cost estimate UI: follow_up_config shows projected cost based on config × expected lead count. (5) Test: fill cap, try create follow-up, verify it's blocked with message 'monthly spend cap reached'.

**Pause-on-reply logic (stop_on_reply) — 6/10**
- ✅ System B (followup-runner line 145-161): checks sequence.stop_on_reply flag, calls contactRepliedAfter() with started_at boundary, marks sequence 'skipped_reply' + cancels remaining messages. Dispatches completion notifier. Event logged (line 364-368).
- ⚠️ contactRepliedAfter (line 305-343) is resilient but slow (queries GHL conversations twice, iterates all). Fail-open means if GHL is down, pause-on-reply is disabled silently. (2) System A's scheduled_followups has NO stop_on_reply equivalent—scheduler only checks if lead replied AFTER scheduled_at (line 206-224), not triggered after first message sent. So if lead replies to first follow-up, System A continues with follow-ups 2-5. (3) System B's started_at is set when sequence transitions scheduled→running (line 165-170), but if first message fails to send, started_at is NOT reset—subsequent reply detection will use wrong boundary. (4) No test coverage visible: smoke-test-followup.ts doesn't cover pause-on-reply scenario.
- 🔧 (1) For System A: add stop_on_reply flag to follow_up_config (currently not in FollowUpConfig type). Check after each send: if message sent, poll for reply, cancel remaining if found. (2) For System B: only set started_at when FIRST message SUCCESSFULLY sends (move line 165-170 into success branch of line 184-200). (3) For contactRepliedAfter: add timeout + cache (fail-closed: assume replied if >1s timeout). (4) Add integration test: schedule 3-msg sequence, send msg 1, inject inbound reply, verify sequence pauses and messages 2-3 marked skipped.

**Testing and observability — 4/10**
- ✅ Smoke test exists (smoke-test-followup.ts) covering settings, safety, spam score, parseRequestedAt. Helper functions (countActiveSequences, decideFlow, calculateCumulativeDelay) have clear logic. execution_log provides audit trail.
- ⚠️ System A has NO test coverage—no smoke test, no E2E test for send. Impossible to verify critical path (queue-processor → scheduleFollowUps → processScheduledFollowUps). (2) System B's smoke test doesn't cover: pause-on-reply, approve_sequence race condition, runner claim collisions, billing integration, handoff notifier. (3) No observability: no metrics exported (no emit('followup_scheduled'), 'followup_sent', 'followup_failed'). Admin dashboard (hub) has no follow-up metrics pane. (4) Logs are console.log (line 323-326 follow-up-scheduler)—doesn't emit structured trace IDs, hard to correlate across lambdas. (5) No alerting: if runner tick returns {sent:0, errors:N} consistently, no automatic alert to ops. (6) processScheduledFollowUps is called by cron but no visibility into cron health—could be silently disabled.
- 🔧 (1) Add E2E tests: create contact → trigger follow-up schedule via queue-processor → advance clock → verify runner sends → verify execution_log entry → verify message in GHL. (2) Export metrics: follow_up.scheduled, follow_up.sent, follow_up.failed, follow_up.claimed, follow_up.claim_failed, pause_on_reply.detected, pause_on_reply.failed. (3) Add structured logging with request ID correlation (already done for queue-processor, apply to follow-up). (4) Dashboard: add 'Follow-ups' tab showing (sent this week / failed / pending / avg time-to-send). (5) Add health check: /api/health includes {followup_cron_last_tick: ISO, followup_pending_count: N, followup_claimed_age_seconds: N}. (6) Alert: if claimed_age_seconds > 300, trigger PagerDuty (runner stuck).

**Production readiness: F47 duplicate-sequence bug — 2/10**
- ✅ Bug is documented in migration comment (F47 2026-06-04). Cause is understood: scheduleFollowUps() is called per-message turn, creates NEW full sequence without merge/dedup.
- ⚠️ BLOCKER: This is a critical production bug UNFIXED. Evidence: (1) Migration 00097 line 38-39 comments 'Follow-up rastreado: o scheduler cria uma sequência NOVA... observado: 80 follow-ups pra 1 contato após 8 turnos. Deduplicar/substituir no follow-up-scheduler é tarefa separada.' (2) No follow-up task created (no issue link, no _planning/ doc with action). (3) If a contact goes silent for 8 turns (unlikely but possible), 80 follow-ups queue up. When runner starts, it sends 20/tick—4 ticks = 2 minutes of spam to this contact. If second-order amplification (contact has 100 such cases), system sends 8000 messages to GHL in 2 minutes = potential DDoS/rate-limit. (4) No safeguard: follow_up_config.max_attempts=5 is OVERRIDDEN every turn (line 57 calculates max_attempts each call, but creates NEW set). (5) No dedup gate: no check for `existing pending+scheduled for this contact` before creating new batch.
- 🔧 MUST FIX before production: (1) Change scheduleFollowUps() logic: instead of cancel-all-then-create-new, check if ACTIVE sequence exists. If yes, return early (do nothing). If no, create one. (2) Add query: `SELECT id FROM scheduled_followups WHERE contact_id=? AND agent_id=? AND status IN ('pending','processing','completed')` with TTL=7 days. If found, skip scheduleFollowUps entirely. (3) OR: add follow_up_config.skip_if_active_sequence_exists flag (default true). (4) Test: silence contact 8 turns, verify only 1 sequence created, not 8. (5) For legacy data: add cleanup migration `DELETE FROM scheduled_followups WHERE created_at < 2026-06-04 AND status='pending'` (clear backlog).

**Transition/deprecation path — 2/10**
- ✅ Schema exists for both systems (clear separation). Code comments document which system is used where (// follow_up_config vs // followup_feature_enabled).
- ⚠️ NO TRANSITION PLAN: (1) No decision documented: is System A deprecated after System B ships, or do both persist? (2) If migrating, no tooling: no script to convert follow_up_config JSONB → followup_sequences. (3) Ops doesn't know: _planning/ docs don't clarify which system is for whom ('SparkBot rep-facing' vs 'lead-facing agents' distinction not in CLAUDE.md). (4) No feature flags: if System B has a critical bug, can't rollback without code deploy. (5) UX confusion: if admin UI shows both config sections, users don't know which applies. (6) Test collision: smoke tests don't prevent regression where old code changes System A but System B tests pass anyway.
- 🔧 BEFORE production deploy: (1) Add explicit decision to CLAUDE.md: 'System A (scheduled_followups) is for lead-facing agents (sales/recruitment). System B (followup_sequences) is for SparkBot (rep-facing). At-most-one active per agent.' (2) Add mutual-exclusion gate in queue-processor (line 1171-1182): if both enabled, log warning + disable System A. (3) Create migration + script to backfill: SET followup_feature_enabled=false WHERE follow_up_config IS NOT NULL (preserve legacy behavior, require manual opt-in to System B). (4) Add feature flag: `ENABLE_FOLLOWUP_SEQUENCES` (default false until stable). (5) Deprecation notice: System A will be removed 2026-Q4, migrate to System B by 2026-09-30. (6) For System B pre-launch: test against realistic 5-agent + 1000-contact load to verify runner doesn't bottleneck.

### Structural issues
- **[CRITICAL] Two parallel follow-up systems with overlapping intent but different architectures** — System A (scheduled_followups, migration 00040/00097) designed for lead-facing agents, triggered from queue-processor on every message turn. System B (followup_sequences, migration 00067) designed for SparkBot rep-facing. Both share intent (schedule follow-up messages) but use different DB tables, different config columns, different approval logic (FollowUpConfig.mode vs followup_approval_mode), different runners. Codebase has no clear boundary—docs don't state which-for-whom. Files: /src/lib/queue/follow-up-scheduler.ts (System A), /src/lib/account-assistant/followup/ (System B, 11 files). (src/lib/queue/follow-up-scheduler.ts, src/lib/account-assistant/followup/*, supabase/migrations/00040_*.sql, 00067_*.sql)
- **[CRITICAL] Critical bug unfixed 3 weeks (F47): duplicate sequence generation** — scheduleFollowUps() called per-message creates ENTIRE NEW sequence every turn. Contact with 8 silent turns = 8 sequences queued. Migration 00097 documents: 'observado: 80 follow-ups pra 1 contato após 8 turnos. Deduplicar/substituir é tarefa separada.' No task created, bug never fixed. Code has zero dedup: cancel-all at line 31, then create-new loop. No gate checking existing sequences per contact. (src/lib/queue/follow-up-scheduler.ts:31-76, supabase/migrations/00097_fix_scheduled_followups_updated_at.sql)
- **[CRITICAL] Silent error handling pattern: F46 bug replicated throughout** — F46 (Jun 4, 2026) exposed silent supabase-js error handling: update() doesn't throw, returns {error}. Code ignored error field, UPDATE silently failed for 3 weeks. SAME PATTERN exists in follow-up-scheduler.ts line 31 (cancel), 44 (insert), 425 (mark sent), and followup/core.ts & sequence-scheduler.ts—zero error checks. Every supabase call vulnerable. Violates CLAUDE.md anti-pattern #1. (src/lib/queue/follow-up-scheduler.ts:31-36, 44-75, 425, src/lib/account-assistant/followup/sequence-scheduler.ts (entire file))
- **[HIGH] No mutual exclusion between System A & B: double-scheduling possible** — Agent can have follow_up_config.enabled=true AND followup_feature_enabled=true simultaneously. queue-processor checks follow_up_config at line 1171, schedules System A. No gate preventing System B from also scheduling. Both systems could create follow-ups for same contact. Defaults: migration 00015 sets follow_up_config default enabled, migration 00067 sets followup_feature_enabled=true. Ops doesn't know which system is canonical per agent. (src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts:1171-1182, supabase/migrations/00015_recruitment_agent_support.sql, 00067_followup_feature.sql)
- **[HIGH] System B incomplete: spam recheck, webhook, lead-facing stubs not implemented** — followup-runner.ts line 172 comment 'TODO MVP v2' indicates requires_final_check field is stubbed. Schema has stage_triggers JSONB but no webhook listener/executor. Core service is designed as 'source-agnostic' (source='chat|proactive_rule|webhook') but webhook=future (per migration comment). Lead-facing integration NOT wired—sales/recruitment agents can't trigger System B (only rep can via chat tools). (src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/followup-runner.ts:172, src/lib/account-assistant/followup/types.ts:8, supabase/migrations/00067_followup_feature.sql (stage_triggers))
- **[HIGH] Idempotency gap: no ghl_message_id stored pre-send (both systems)** — System A scheduled_followups table has no ghl_message_id column. Runner sends to GHL, stores nothing until after. If process crashes post-send, next tick re-sends. System B followup-runner stores ghl_message_id AFTER send succeeds (line 189), same window. No unique constraint prevents duplicate inserts. Message could be sent to lead 2x. (src/lib/queue/follow-up-scheduler.ts:273-401, src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/followup-runner.ts:184-191)
- **[HIGH] System B missing billing integration** — createFollowupRequest() → generateSequence() → processWithAI() consumes tokens but never calls trackAndCharge(). No usage_records inserted. Cost invisible to billing dashboard. If location has spend cap, can generate unlimited follow-ups for free (cap not checked before generation). (src/lib/account-assistant/followup/core.ts (no trackAndCharge call), src/lib/account-assistant/followup/sequence-generator.ts (processWithAI called but not charged))
- **[HIGH] No test coverage for System A critical path** — smoke-test-followup.ts tests System B only. System A (queue-processor → scheduleFollowUps → processScheduledFollowUps) has ZERO E2E test. Can't verify send works, pause-on-reply works, or F47 duplicate bug is actually fixed. (scripts/smoke-test-followup.ts (System B tests only), no tests for src/lib/queue/follow-up-scheduler.ts)
- **[HIGH] Zero observability: no metrics, no alerting for follow-up runner** — processScheduledFollowUps called by cron but no metrics emitted. If runner fails, admin has no alert. No health check. No dashboard pane. If runner crashes and logs aren't checked, follow-ups silently pile up for hours/days. (src/lib/queue/follow-up-scheduler.ts (console.log only), src/app/api/health/route.ts (no followup metrics))
- **[MEDIUM] No transition/deprecation plan documented** — CLAUDE.md doesn't clarify: is System A deprecated after System B ships? Do both persist? If migrating, no tooling to convert. Ops doesn't know which system to use for new agents. No feature flag to rollback System B if critical bug found. (CLAUDE.md (missing Systems A/B decision), no _planning/deprecation-follow-up.md)
- **[MEDIUM] Pause-on-reply logic incomplete and asymmetric** — System B implements pause-on-reply (followup-runner line 145-161). System A has no equivalent—if lead replies to 1st follow-up, System A continues with 2-5. System B's fail-open (contactRepliedAfter returns false on error) means pause-on-reply is silently disabled when GHL is down. No test coverage for pause-on-reply scenario. (src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/followup-runner.ts:145-161 (System B only), src/lib/queue/follow-up-scheduler.ts (System A has no pause-on-reply))

### Production blockers
- **[PARTIAL/HIGH] F47: Duplicate follow-up sequences (unfixed 3-week bug)** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: scheduleFollowUps() called per-message turn creates ENTIRE NEW sequence (max_attempts follow-ups) without deduplication. Evidence: contact going 8 silent turns generates 8 sequences = 40 follow-ups queued (if max_attempts=5). When runner starts, sends in bursts. Observed in production: '80 follow-ups pra 1 contato após 8 turnos' per migration 00097 comment. Code has zero dedup gate—scheduler just calls cancel() then insert().
  - Fix: Add early-return gate in scheduleFollowUps() (line 17-77 follow-up-scheduler.ts): query scheduled_followups for (agent_id, contact_id, status IN pending/scheduled/processing) with TTL. If found, return without creating new batch. Test with 8 silent turns, verify only 1 sequence created. Also: add max_attempts cap enforcement at config-load time (not per-turn).
  - Veredicto: src/lib/queue/follow-up-scheduler.ts:31-36 attempts deduplication via UPDATE to cancel pending follow-ups, BUT lines 31-36 and 44,66 do NOT check Supabase result for errors (anti-pattern documented in CLAUDE.md). If UPDATE fails, old follow-ups remain and new ones are added, causing duplicates. Migration 00097 (2026-06-04) fixed underlying DB schema bug (missing updated_at column) that was causing these UPDATE failures silently. Migration comment (00097_fix_scheduled_followups_updated_at.sql:36-39) acknowledges "80 follow-ups pra 1 contato após 8 turnos" bug and marks deduplication as "separate task". scheduleFollowUps() IS called per message turn in queue-processor.ts:1175 (when conversation active, objective not completed). Each call creates maxAttempts new rows (lines 62-75 show loop inserting N follow-ups). Root cause (missing column) fixed in 00097, but error handling on UPDATE/INSERT operations still missing as of latest commit df0aaa8.
- **[CONFIRMED/CRITICAL] F46 pattern: Silent supabase-js errors throughout both systems** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: F46 (2026-06-04) found scheduled_followups table missing updated_at column → trigger failed silently. supabase-js doesn't throw, returns { error: {...} }. Code doesn't check error field. Result: processScheduledFollowUps marked rows 'processing' but UPDATE silently failed, runner returned {sent:0} for 3 weeks (May 12–Jun 4), follow-ups never sent. Same pattern exists throughout: follow-up-scheduler.ts line 31 (cancel), line 44 (insert), line 425 (mark sent)—ZERO error checks. Every update/insert vulnerable.
  - Fix: Audit all supabase calls in both systems (follow-up-scheduler.ts, followup/core.ts, followup-runner.ts, followup/sequence-scheduler.ts). For every update()/insert()/upsert(), wrap: `if (result.error) { throw new Error(...) }` or return typed error. Create pre-commit lint rule to flag unhandled .error. Test: inject bad migration (drop column), run, verify error is thrown not silenced.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/queue/follow-up-scheduler.ts:31-36 (await without { data, error } destructure), line 44-53 (insert without error check), line 425 (update without error check); supabase/migrations/00097_fix_scheduled_followups_updated_at.sql:7-10 documents the root cause — scheduled_followups table created without updated_at column but trigger tries to set it, causing all UPDATE ops to fail silently via supabase-js { error } field that code never checks. Timeline: runner activated 2026-05-19, bug discovered 2026-06-04 (23 days), 86 follow-ups stuck in pending status, zero sent. Pattern also evident in queue-processor.ts:91-96 (orphan reaper without error check), handoff-notify.ts, webhook-handler.ts, summary-note-generator.ts. Anti-pattern explicitly documented in CLAUDE.md as "Try/catch in supabase-js insert: does NOT throw, returns {error}. Use if (result.error?.code === ...)"
- **[PARTIAL/MEDIUM] System B incomplete for production: spam recheck, webhook, lead-facing not done** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: followup-runner.ts line 172 has TODO comment: 'Recheck spam_score se requires_final_check (TODO MVP v2 — pra MVP skip)'. Feature is designed (requires_final_check field exists, schema ready) but NOT implemented. Webhook trigger system is designed but marked 'futuro' in migration 00067. Lead-facing integration is NOT wired into queue-processor—System B is only callable via chat tools (SparkBot), can't be triggered by lead inbound messages. Migration 00067 has 'stage_triggers' JSONB field but no executor written.
  - Fix: For MVP: (1) Either implement spam recheck in runner (recalc score from sequence context, skip if 'high') OR remove requires_final_check flag + simplify. (2) Document: 'Webhook triggers + lead-facing planned for Phase 2 (2026-Q4), not in MVP.' Add issue + feature flag ENABLE_WEBHOOK_TRIGGERS=false. (3) If shipping with System B, wire sales/recruitment agents to use followup_sequences NOT follow_up_config (requires config migration + testing).
  - Veredicto: src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/followup-runner.ts:172 — TODO comment confirmed but is INTENTIONAL MVP scope exclusion ("pra MVP skip"). Not a bug—design allows adding later. src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/event-router.ts (F27.D) — webhook system DOES exist for CONTACTTAGUPDATE/OPPORTUNITYSTAGEUPDATE but serves lead-facing reactive dispatch, not System B. src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts:1169-1182 — uses legacy scheduled_followups table, separate from followup_sequences. System B and lead-facing are two PARALLEL systems, not one incomplete.
- **[REFUTED/LOW] Configuration drift: mutual exclusion not enforced** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: Agent can have BOTH follow_up_config (System A) AND followup_feature_enabled (System B) enabled. Runtime has no check—both schedulers may run, creating double follow-ups for same contact. Settings loader (loadFollowupSettings) defaults followup_feature_enabled=true, defaults don't auto-disable System A. queue-processor line 1171 checks follow_up_config?.enabled independently of System B, no AND NOT followup_feature_enabled guard.
  - Fix: Add mutual-exclusion gate in queue-processor (before scheduleFollowUps call, line ~1170): if (config.followup_feature_enabled && config.follow_up_config?.enabled) { log.warn(...); config.follow_up_config.enabled = false; } Document decision in CLAUDE.md: 'Only one system per agent.' Create backfill migration: UPDATE agent_configs SET followup_feature_enabled = false WHERE follow_up_config IS NOT NULL (preserve System A as default for existing agents).
  - Veredicto: src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts:283 filters agents with `in("type", ["sales_agent", "recruitment_agent", "custom_agent"])` — only lead-facing agents reach line 1171 where follow_up_config is checked. src/lib/account-assistant/webhook-handler.ts processes ONLY account_assistant agents (SparkBot), which is a different agent type. These types are mutually exclusive per supabase/migrations/00002_create_agents.sql:14 UNIQUE(location_id, type) constraint. System A uses scheduled_followups table, System B uses followup_sequences table. There is no code path where both systems execute for the same agent because they operate on different agent types via different entry points.
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] Idempotency: System A has no duplicate-send protection on retry** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: scheduled_followups table has no ghl_message_id stored. Runner claims follow-up and sends via GHL, but if process crashes between GHL send (which succeeds) and DB UPDATE status='sent', next runner tick re-claims and re-sends same message (duplicate). No unique constraint to prevent. System B stores ghl_message_id but only after send succeeds, same window exists.
  - Fix: For System A: before calling GHL, insert placeholder with ghl_message_id=UUID + status='sending'. After GHL returns messageId, UPDATE to store returned ID + status='sent'. This makes (agent_id, contact_id, attempt_number, ghl_message_id) effectively unique, preventing replay. For System B: same pattern in followup-runner (line 184-191 currently doesn't store ID pre-send). Test: crash runner mid-message, restart, verify GHL doesn't receive duplicate message.
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] System B: No billing integration (tokens consumed but not charged)** (conf: med)
  - Porquê: createFollowupRequest() calls generateSequence() which calls processWithAI() and consumes tokens. No trackAndCharge() call. Generated follow-ups use LLM cost but it's invisible to billing dashboard. If admin has spend cap, can create unlimited free follow-ups because no usage_records inserted.
  - Fix: In followup/sequence-scheduler.ts persistSequence() or followup-runner.ts sendFollowupMessage(): after LLM call, call trackAndCharge() (model name, tokens, actionType='generate_followup'). Store in usage_records. Test: generate sequence with 3 messages, query usage_records for that agent/location, verify total_charge_usd > 0.
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] No health check or alerting for follow-up runner (cron-driven)** (conf: med)
  - Porquê: processScheduledFollowUps is called by cron but has no visibility—if cron job is disabled or timing drifts, follow-ups silently pile up. No metrics emitted. No alert if runner consistently returns {errors:N, sent:0}. Admin dashboard has no 'Follow-ups' tab to show pending count or health. If runner is broken for 24h, no one notices until escalation.
  - Fix: Add /api/health check including: {followup_last_runner_at: ISO, followup_pending_count: N, followup_claimed_older_than_2min: count}. Emit metrics: followup_scheduled, followup_sent, followup_failed, runner_ticks. Add dashboard 'Follow-ups' tab with (sent this 24h, failed, pending, avg time-to-send). Set up alerting: if pending_count > 100 OR claimed_age > 300s, page on-call.


---

## Agentes lead-facing — awareness, handoff & targeting

F37 and F27 enable lead-facing agents (sales/recruitment/custom) to understand conversation context and make intelligent routing decisions. F37 loads historical lead data from GHL, evaluates whether the bot should respond or hand off, and notifies the rep. F27 enforces targeting rules (tags, custom fields, pipeline stages) to ensure agents only respond to eligible contacts. Both are gated by configuration flags (default OFF for safety) and use fail-open semantics to avoid silencing the agent on errors. The implementation spans queue-processor (orchestrator), four specialized modules (targeting, lead-history, should-respond, handoff-notify), type definitions, and a migration adding schema columns.

### Funcionalidades

**F27 Targeting Rules Enforcement — 7/10**
- ✅ Fail-open design (GHL fetch errors = agent responds). AND logic correctly gates responses. Three rule types (tag, custom_field, pipeline_stage) properly extracted from GHL contact/opps. Cache-aware pipeline stage resolution via GHLClient.get(). Audit trail in execution_log action_type='targeting_skip' with reason. Manual override via ai_resumed_at respected (GU-6).
- ⚠️ No rate limiting on GHL API calls during targeting check — each response triggers 2 parallel GHL requests (contact + opportunities search). High-volume contacts (100+ messages) could DDoS GHL API. Custom field matching is case-insensitive but uses String() coercion which could silently fail on non-string types (e.g., numbers). Pipeline stage resolution doesn't cache pipelines across contacts in same location/call — refetches on every check.
- 🔧 Add memoization for pipeline lookups within a 5-minute window (reuse across multiple contacts in queue batch). Rate-limit or batch GHL targeting checks (defer non-critical validations to batch job). Test custom field type coercion edge cases (null, undefined, boolean, numeric IDs). Document the AND semantics clearly for admin UI — some may expect OR.

**F37 Lead History Loading — 6/10**
- ✅ Fail-soft design (GHL fetch errors return empty context instead of throwing). In-memory cache with 5min TTL + configurable hash key. Parallel Promise.all for contact + conversations fetch. Handles both customFields and customField array keys (GHL API inconsistency). Normalizes message direction ('inbound'/'outbound'). Filters empty message bodies. Distinguishes human outbound from bot via source !== 'api'. Cache entry includes fetch_ms for observability.
- ⚠️ CRITICAL CACHE BUG: cache key doesn't include include_tags flag (line 147). If one request sets include_tags=false then another sets true, both get same cached result (tags missing on 2nd request). No explicit invalidation hook despite exporting invalidateLeadHistoryCache — function is exported but never called from any webhook/queue handler. Cache is in-memory per Lambda container; no cross-container invalidation (cold-start on new requests may miss recent updates). Conversation truncated to first 5 (line 160) but stored all in array then sliced (wasteful). No timeout guard on .catch() handlers — could hang indefinitely if GHL is slow.
- 🔧 URGENT: Add include_tags to cache key (1 line fix, high impact). Add explicit invalidation calls in queue-processor webhook handlers when new inbound arrives. Consider Redis cache or DB-backed cache for cross-container coherence if cold-starts matter. Set explicit timeout on GHL client calls (e.g., 5s abort). Limit conversation query to exactly what's needed, not fetch-then-truncate.

**F37 Should-Respond Decision Logic — 8/10**
- ✅ Policy-disabled safety default (enabled=false). Clear priority order: human_replied_recently > lead_requested_human > opp_closed. Normalized string matching with NFD accent stripping (handles 'falar com alguém' → matches 'falar com alguem'). minutesBetween() handles NaN gracefully. Test suite (12 scenarios) covers happy path + edge cases. Matches against each rule until first match (fail-fast). Audit trail includes reason in execution_log.
- ⚠️ Substring keyword matching (line 76: bodyNorm.includes(k)) is too loose — 'humanoide' matches 'humano' keyword, causing false handoff (test line 144-151 documents this as intentional but risky). No configurable keyword boundaries/word-boundary regex. Lead said 'você é humano?' gets skipped (substring match). Case study: rep installs agent with default custom_keywords_handoff, lead says 'esse bot é humanizado demais' → skip happens incorrectly. Test explicitly says this is a 'limitation current', implying it's known but unresolved.
- 🔧 Switch from includes() to word-boundary regex for keywords (e.g., \b + escape special chars). Provide UI hint: 'Keywords are matched as substrings; add 'humano' carefully'. Add length guard (skip if < 3 chars, too prone to false matches). Consider 2-word minimum for custom keywords to reduce noise.

**F37 Handoff Notification via SparkBot — 6/10**
- ✅ Non-blocking design (NEVER throw; always returns NotifyResult). Fallback rep resolution cascade: contact.assignedUserId > fallback rep_identities. Idempotency check with 4-hour cooldown via handoff_notifications table or execution_log fallback. Graceful fallback when handoff_notifications table doesn't exist (migration 00096 hasn't run yet). DeliveryResult captures ok/error/via for audit. Double-inserts execution_log + handoff_notifications (redundancy for durability).
- ⚠️ CRITICAL ISSUE: rep resolution MISSING opp.assignedTo (line 45-47 in code comment says 'fica pra fase 2'). Contact may not be assigned, fallback to 'any rep of location' — could notify wrong rep. Idempotency race condition: two concurrent handoff decisions for same (location, contact, reason) in 4h window both pass cooldown check, both notify (race-check-set, not atomic). If deliverProactiveMessage fails silently, execution_log still marks notified=false but handoff_notifications NOT inserted → inconsistent state (cooldown check will pass on next try, no dedup). NotifyResult.skipped_reason could be undefined (not all paths set it), leading to confusing audit logs.
- 🔧 Add opp.assignedTo lookup (F37.D follow-up, make issue). Use UNIQUE constraint or SELECT FOR UPDATE to prevent race condition on idempotency check (make it atomic). If deliverProactiveMessage fails, DON'T insert handoff_notifications (only insert if delivery succeeded or system persisted it). Always set skipped_reason (add 'unknown' default). Add retry logic for rep lookup failures (transient DB issue).

**Targeting + Handoff Integration in Queue Processor — 7/10**
- ✅ Correct sequencing: targeting check (F27) BEFORE load-history (F37). leadHistory only loads if lead_history_config.enabled=true (no waste). handoffPol.enabled AND leadHistory both required for decision (safe AND gate, not OR). Manual resume override (ai_resumed_at) properly checked before targeting gate (GU-6). Audit in execution_log with action_type='should_respond_skip' + reason. Log messages clear and contextual (req ID, contact ID prefix).
- ⚠️ CRITICAL PRODUCTION BLOCKER: Line 808 condition `if (handoffPol.enabled && leadHistory)` means if admin enables handoff_policy but disables lead_history_config, handoff gate is silently SKIPPED (never runs). Bot ignores handoff policy entirely. Lead says 'quiero hablar con alguien' but no history loaded → skip not evaluated → bot responds anyway. This is especially bad because DEFAULT_HANDOFF_POLICY has enabled=true in code but gets merged with DB NULL via getHandoffPolicy(), so enabling one without the other is a foot-gun. No warning logged when this condition fails.
- 🔧 Change condition to `if (handoffPol.enabled)` and load minimal history if needed (at minimum last human outbound timestamp). Or require both config flags to be enabled together in UI (single cat toggle 'Lead Awareness + Handoff'). Add warning log if handoff enabled but history not loaded. Document dependency clearly.

**Cache Invalidation for Lead History — 3/10**
- ✅ Function exported (invalidateLeadHistoryCache). 5-minute TTL prevents stale data forever. In-memory cache per container is fast.
- ⚠️ CRITICAL: Cache invalidation function defined but NEVER CALLED from anywhere. Exported but unused. If rep updates contact tags in GHL, agent's next response uses stale tags (from cache, up to 5 min old). If contact moves pipeline stage, bot doesn't know until cache expires. No webhook/queue handler calls invalidate when new inbound arrives. This is a major awareness bug — bot makes decisions (handoff, history section) based on potentially stale data.
- 🔧 URGENT: Call invalidateLeadHistoryCache(contactId) when new inbound message arrives (in queue-processor after inserting msg to queue, or in webhook). Add test to verify cache is cleared on inbound. Consider making cache key include config hash so different configs get different cache entries (currently missing include_tags in key, which compounds this bug).

**Edge Cases: Closed Opportunities & Lead Awareness — 7/10**
- ✅ Lead with won/lost/abandoned opportunity correctly triggers skip (has_closed_opp flag works). Silent skip (no rep notification) correct for closed opps. Test suite covers won/lost/abandoned status values. EMPTY_CONTEXT provides sensible defaults when load fails (fetch_ms=0, empty arrays).
- ⚠️ has_closed_opp is boolean but logic looks for FIRST closed opp to display in message (line 89-90 in should-respond.ts). If contact has 5 opps (3 open, 2 closed), algorithm reports the first closed one found, not the most recent. Could report 'Opp X lost' for a 3-month-old deal when the contact is actually in an open deal with another product. Opportunities array not sorted by date (loaded from GHL in no particular order). Lead with multiple opps: 1 won, 1 in negotiation — bot skips, rep gets 'Opp [won] closed'. Rep confused because they're actively negotiating the other opp.
- 🔧 Sort opportunities by status (open first) or date (most recent). Display status of most recent opp, not first match. Consider skipping ONLY if the ACTIVE opp is closed (unclear from current logic). Add test case: contact with mixed open+closed opps → verify correct opp is reported.

**Fail-Open vs Fail-Closed Trade-offs — 8/10**
- ✅ Consistent design principle: GHL fetch errors → fail-open (agent responds, graceful degradation). targeting.ts (line 161-168), lead-history.ts (line 276-281), should-respond implicitly (returns default 'respond' if no context). This prevents silent failures and customer-facing 'agent never responds' issues.
- ⚠️ Fail-open can mask real bugs (GHL API contract changed, auth failed, network issue). No separate handling for 'auth failed' vs 'network timeout' vs 'contact not found' — all treated same (respond). If GHL API key is rotated and no one notices, agent responds normally but missing all contact context (silent degradation). Targeting check fails silently; admin thinks rules are working but they're not (agent responds to everyone). Could benefit from alerting thresholds ('if 10% of targeting checks fail in 5min window, alert admin').
- 🔧 Add differentiation in error handling: timeouts/transients → fail-open with warning, auth/permission errors → fail-open with error alert (separate signal), 404 contact not found → respond (contact is new). Add metrics: 'targeting_check_error_rate', 'lead_history_fetch_error_rate'. Alert on unexpected error spikes. Log GHL error details (status code, message) for debugging without exposing to user.

### Structural issues
- **[CRITICAL] Cache key incomplete — include_tags not hashed** — lead-history.ts line 147: cache key is `${locationId}:${contactId}:${config.messages_count}:${config.include_notes ? 1 : 0}:${config.include_opportunities ? 1 : 0}` but missing `${config.include_tags ? 1 : 0}`. If admin toggles include_tags for a contact that's already cached, both requests get same cached result → tags missing on one path. (src/lib/queue/lead-history.ts:147)
- **[CRITICAL] Cache invalidation function exported but never called** — invalidateLeadHistoryCache(contactId) is exported from lead-history.ts but grep shows zero callers anywhere in src/. When new inbound arrives, cache is not cleared → agent uses stale contact data (old tags, old opp stage, old notes) for up to 5 minutes. (src/lib/queue/lead-history.ts:28 (defined but unused))
- **[CRITICAL] Handoff policy enabled without lead history loads nothing** — queue-processor.ts line 808: condition `if (handoffPol.enabled && leadHistory)` means if handoff_policy enabled but lead_history_config disabled, the entire should-respond gate is skipped. Admin enables handoff but not history → no decisions made. Lead says 'hablar con humano' → bot responds anyway because evaluateShouldRespond() never called. (src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts:808)
- **[HIGH] Rep resolution for handoff missing opp.assignedTo** — handoff-notify.ts lines 45-47 explicitly note 'opp.assignedTo — não temos no LeadContext; fica pra fase 2'. If contact is unassigned, fallback resolves 'any rep of location' which could be wrong person. Should load opp owner from GHL when contact has no direct assignment. (src/lib/queue/handoff-notify.ts:45-47 (todo not implemented))
- **[HIGH] Idempotency check race condition in handoff notify** — handoff-notify.ts lines 90-120: alreadyNotified() checks cooldown but doesn't prevent two concurrent requests from both passing the check. No SELECT FOR UPDATE or atomic upsert. If 2 lead messages arrive within 100ms, both evaluate shouldRespond, both want to notify → both pass cooldown check → both send notification (duplicate). (src/lib/queue/handoff-notify.ts:90-120)
- **[MEDIUM] Substring matching for handoff keywords too permissive** — should-respond.ts line 76: uses bodyNorm.includes(k) for keyword matching. 'humanoide' matches 'humano' keyword. Test at line 144-151 documents this as known limitation but it causes false handoffs. No word boundary enforcement. (src/lib/queue/should-respond.ts:76)
- **[MEDIUM] Opportunities array not sorted; reports wrong closed opp** — lead-history.ts loads opps unsorted from GHL. In should-respond.ts line 89-90, if contact has 5 opps (3 open, 2 closed), finding first closed opp could be the oldest one, not most recent. Bot reports stale closed deal instead of currently-active one. (src/lib/queue/should-respond.ts:89-90, src/lib/queue/lead-history.ts:234-247 (opps not sorted))
- **[MEDIUM] Targeting check makes 2 GHL API calls per message with no rate limiting** — targeting.ts line 87-98: Promise.all([contact, opportunities]) makes 2 GHL API calls. High-volume contact (100+ messages) triggers 200+ GHL API calls without batching or rate limiting. No caching of pipelines across contacts in same batch. (src/lib/queue/targeting.ts:87-98)
- **[LOW] Dead code: deliverProactiveMessage imported but delivery metadata not validated** — handoff-notify.ts imports and calls deliverProactiveMessage but extraMetadata may contain arbitrary keys (agent_id, lead_contact_id, handoff_reason) that aren't validated against DeliveryOptions interface. If schema changes, no type safety. (src/lib/queue/handoff-notify.ts:174-189)

### Production blockers
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] BLOCKER: Cache key missing include_tags flag — silent data loss** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: lead-history.ts cache key doesn't hash config.include_tags. If two requests hit the same contact with different include_tags settings, both get same cached result. Second request gets tags stripped even though it asked for them. Bot makes decisions based on incomplete lead context (missing tags → missing targeting logic).
  - Fix: Add `${config.include_tags ? 1 : 0}` to cache key on line 147. Retest with scenarios: (1) load with include_tags=true, cache hit with include_tags=false → verify tags present. (2) Reverse. Add unit test.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/queue/lead-history.ts:147 — cache key construction is `${locationId}:${contactId}:${config.messages_count}:${config.include_notes ? 1 : 0}:${config.include_opportunities ? 1 : 0}` — missing `include_tags` flag. LeadHistoryConfig interface (src/types/agent.ts:140) defines `include_tags: boolean`. The result at line 261 conditionally includes tags: `tags: config.include_tags ? extractTags(contact) : []`. Since config.include_tags is not hashed in cache key, two requests with same location/contact/messages_count/notes/opportunities but different include_tags values will hit same cache entry. Second request gets cached result with tags stripped (line 261 executed as [] due to first request's config.include_tags=false), even if second request has include_tags=true. This breaks buildLeadHistorySection (src/lib/ai/sales-prompt-builder.ts:953-962) which relies on leadHistory.contact.tags and uses it for prompt decisions. Root cause: queue-processor.ts:122 groups messages by `agent_id:contact_id`, allowing multiple agents in same location to process same contact independently, each with different lead_history_config values. No test coverage for cache-key collisions with include_tags variance (scripts/test-lead-awareness.ts does not test this scenario).
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] BLOCKER: Cache invalidation never called — stale lead data until timeout** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: invalidateLeadHistoryCache() exported but never invoked. If contact gets re-tagged in GHL, agent's next 5 responses use old tags (cache TTL). Targeting rules evaluated against stale data. Lead added to 'hot' tag, bot doesn't know until 5min expires.
  - Fix: Call invalidateLeadHistoryCache(contactId) in queue-processor when new inbound is queued (after line 808 or earlier in webhook). Or add to queue message handler. Must test: update contact tags in GHL, send inbound to agent within 1s → verify new tags seen (not cached old ones). Track cache hit rate to ensure invalidation is working.
  - Veredicto: 
1. src/lib/queue/lead-history.ts:27-32 — `invalidateLeadHistoryCache()` is exported and documented to be called when inbound arrives
2. src/lib/queue/lead-history.ts:12-13 (comment) — "Cache in-memory 5min por contactId (invalidado quando webhook recebe novo inbound do mesmo contato)"
3. _planning/F37-lead-awareness/PLAN.md:57 (Decision D2) — Design decision states: "5min memória + invalidate em new inbound"
4. grep results across src/app/api/webhooks/inbound-message/route.ts, src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts, src/lib/account-assistant/webhook-handler.ts — function is never imported or called (only test-lead-awareness.ts imports it for unit test)
5. git show 907e94b (F37 commit) — original feature implementation contains no calls to invalidateLeadHistoryCache
6. scripts/test-lead-awareness.ts:155-158 — test only verifies function doesn't throw, doesn't verify it's invoked on inbound
7. No TODOs, FIXMEs, or follow-up commits address this gap

Real impact: If contact is re-tagged in GHL at T=10s after first inbound (T=0), second inbound at T=2min loads cache from T=1s without new tag. Targeting rules and handoff policies evaluate against stale data for up to 5 minutes.

- **[CONFIRMED/CRITICAL] BLOCKER: Handoff policy ignored when lead_history_config disabled** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: Line 808 in queue-processor: `if (handoffPol.enabled && leadHistory)` treats leadHistory undefined as false. If admin enables handoff_policy but disables lead_history_config, no decision is made, handoff gate is completely skipped. Bot responds to everything, ignoring 'quero hablar con humano' keywords.
  - Fix: Change condition to `if (handoffPol.enabled)` and load minimal context if needed (only last_human_outbound timestamp + opp closed status). Or add logic: if handoffPol.enabled but leadHistory undefined, populate minimal LeadContext from execution_log/conversation_state. Document in UI that both must be enabled together.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts:783-805 (leadHistory only loaded if leadHistoryCfg.enabled); line 808 requires BOTH handoffPol.enabled && leadHistory truthy; src/lib/queue/should-respond.ts lines 73-84 show "lead requested human" heuristic uses only currentMessageBody—does NOT need leadHistory; CLAUDE.md lines 160-173 describe F37 as two independent toggles both defaulting to OFF, indicating intent that handoff_policy should work independently
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] BLOCKER: Rep resolution missing opp.assignedTo — wrong notification recipient** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: handoff-notify.ts resolveOwnerRep() checks contact.assignedUserId but code comment says opp.assignedTo 'fica pra fase 2'. If contact unassigned but opp has owner, wrong rep gets notified (or no one if location has multiple reps).
  - Fix: If contact.assignedUserId not found, load opp from leadContext.opportunities and check assignedTo (may not be in schema yet, check GHL API). If GHL opp doesn't have assignedTo, fallback current logic. Add test: contact unassigned, opp assigned to rep X → verify rep X notified.
  - Veredicto: 
/Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/src/lib/queue/handoff-notify.ts:47-50 — Comment explicitly states "opportunities[0].assignedTo — não temos no LeadContext; fica pra fase 2"

/Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/src/lib/queue/lead-history.ts:84-93 — GhlOppResp interface missing assignedTo field in opportunity response

/Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/src/types/agent.ts:201-210 — LeadContext.opportunities array structure omits assignedTo field

/Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/src/lib/queue/handoff-notify.ts:52-85 — resolveOwnerRep() function only checks contact.assignedUserId (line 57) and falls back to any rep in location (line 71-82), never checks opportunity.assignedTo

/Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/_planning/ghl-api-reference.md — GHL API POST/PUT /opportunities endpoints confirm assignedTo is a standard field, implying GET response includes it

Root cause: assignedTo is fetched from GHL opportunities API response but NOT extracted in lead-history.ts GhlOppResp interface, NOT propagated to LeadContext type, and NOT consulted in handoff-notify.ts resolveOwnerRep() cascata

- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] BLOCKER: Race condition in idempotency check — duplicate notifications possible** (conf: med)
  - Porquê: alreadyNotified() is a check-then-set, not atomic. Two concurrent handoff decisions for same (location, contact, reason) both see cooldown expired, both pass check, both send notify. 4-hour cooldown becomes 0 in high-concurrency scenarios.
  - Fix: Use database UNIQUE constraint or SELECT ... FOR UPDATE to serialize the check. Or change to: insert into handoff_notifications with ON CONFLICT (location_id, contact_id, reason) DO UPDATE to get atomic upsert. Test with parallel requests to same contact within 1s → verify only 1 notification sent.
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] BLOCKER: Substring keyword matching causes false handoffs** (conf: high)
