  - Porquê: should-respond.ts line 76 uses .includes() for keyword matching. 'humanoide' matches 'humano' keyword. Lead asks 'esse bot é humanizado?' → matches 'humano' → false skip. Could spam rep with false notifications.
  - Fix: Replace includes() with word-boundary regex (\\bhumano\\b after normalizing). Test: contact says 'você é humanizado', 'robô humanoid', 'humano de verdade' → first 2 should not trigger, third should. Add UI warning in Agent settings about keyword specificity.


---

## SparkBot — webhook, dedup & multi-tenant

SparkBot opera em dois caminhos webhook: (1) GHL native via /api/webhooks/inbound-message, (2) Stevo direto (WhatsApp). O sistema implementa 8 camadas de idempotência: (1) mutex em memória por ghl_message_id (60s TTL), (2) SELECT upfront por ghl_message_id, (3) UNIQUE constraint em sparkbot_dedup_locks com minute-bucket, (4) CONTENT-MATCH (15s janela), (5) TIMING-MATCH (5s janela), (6) UNIQUE constraint em sparkbot_messages.ghl_message_id, (7) rep_identity 23505 race capture, (8) content-hash lock atômico (2s janela, V2.2 aditivo). Multi-tenant via locationId + multi-hub cache (5min). Placeholder rejection quando webhook não tem media processável. Defesa contra multi-provider (Stevo + WhatsApp Business API <100ms).

### Funcionalidades

**Idempotency via ghl_message_id UNIQUE — 9/10**
- ✅ Migração bem estruturada para 00043_sparkbot_idempotency_and_silence.sql. UNIQUE constraint parcial (WHERE IS NOT NULL) permite test msgs sem ID. Captura de 23505 em webhook-handler.ts:778 é clara e defensiva. Re-fetch race entre 2 webhooks (Track 1 C3) implementada.
- ⚠️ Constraint apenas bloqueia duplicatas _persistidas_ — se ambos webhooks caem no INSERT simultaneamente em lambdas diferentes, pode haver race antes da UNIQUE validação. Mitigation existe (mutex + content-match) mas depende delas.
- 🔧 Adicionar unique index parcial TAMBÉM na (rep_id, created_at) com intervalo de 5s como camada 9 (reforço). Logs do 23505 poderiam incluir timestamp + idade estimada da row original pra audit trail melhor.

**In-memory Mutex (Camada 1) — 8/10**
- ✅ Implementação limpa em dedup-guard.ts:52-68. GC automático de entries expiradas. 60s TTL conservador. Per-lambda (ES module singleton), não interfere com multi-lambda. Cobre dup-burst concorrente <1s intra-lambda.
- ⚠️ Não funciona cross-lambda — mas isso é esperado, UNIQUE constraint é a defesa ali. Em scenario de lambda contention (10 invocações do webhook em paralelo), mutex só protege dentro de cada lambda individualmente.
- 🔧 Adicionar métrica CloudWatch que publica 'mutex_hits' / 'mutex_misses' para medir frequência real de dup-bursts em prod. Hoje não há visibilidade quantitativa.

**CONTENT-MATCH Dedup (Camada 4, 15s janela) — 8/10**
- ✅ Implementação robusta em webhook-handler.ts:482-516. Checa (rep_id, hub_location_id, role=user, content exato, created_at >= 15s atrás). Fallback silencioso se query falha — não bloqueia o fluxo.
- ⚠️ Janela de 15s é conservadora — rep legítimo digitando a MESMA frase 2× em <15s será bloqueado no segundo. Não é esperado em UX normal (humano não repete txt idêntico), mas é possível em testes ou UX não-intencional. Nenhuma métrica de falso-positivos.
- 🔧 Reduzir janela de 15s para 5s (alinha com TIMING-MATCH abaixo e deixa margem melhor para repeat legítimo). Adicionar metric ao log: 'content_match_rejected: true' pra quantificar rejeições em prod.

**TIMING-MATCH Dedup (Camada 5, 5s janela) — 9/10**
- ✅ Implementação sólida em webhook-handler.ts:518-552. Checa qualquer user msg nos últimos 5s (cobre diferenças de conteúdo, ex: um webhook placeholder + outro com áudio real). Trade-off explícito no comment: bloqueia rep que manda 2 msgs em <5s de propósito, mas isso é muito raro.
- ⚠️ Como CONTENT-MATCH acima, há risco teórico de falso-positivo (rep intencional mandando 2 msgs em 4s, a 2ª será bloqueada). Sem métrica quantitativa em prod de quantas vezes isso acontece.
- 🔧 Considerar diferencial smarter: se a nova msg é radicalmente diferente em LENGTH/tipo (um é 10 chars, outro é 200 chars + audioUrl), ignora o timing (não é mesmo rep digitando rápido, é multi-provider). Adicionar metric 'timing_match_rejected' com payload (ageMs, prevContentLength, currentKind).

**Content-Hash Lock (Camada 8, 2s janela, V2.2 aditivo) — 8/10**
- ✅ Implementação muito bem documentada em dedup-guard.ts. Prefixo 'ch:' separa namespace. Re-check de created_at em 23505 distingue concorrente (fresco) de repeat legítimo (stale) SEM depender do cron. Fail-soft (erro de DB → isDuplicate=false, camadas 2-7 cobrem).
- ⚠️ Janela de 2s é APERTADA se houver lentidão de rede (Stevo API delay 1s + Postgres latência 800ms = 1.8s, baterá no limite). Prefixo 'ch:' aumenta tamanho da dedup_key, nada crítico mas faz bloat na PK.
- 🔧 Aumentar para 3s (mais margem, multi-provider típico é <500ms). Hash truncado a 24 chars é OK (sha1 colisões improvável em scale), mas adicionar opción de 'debug_full_hash=true' pra troubleshooting.

**Minute-bucket Dedup Lock (Camada 3, 60s janela) — 7/10**
- ✅ Tabela sparkbot_dedup_locks com UNIQUE PK em dedup_key. Cleanup cron a cada 5min (00044). Fallback não-bloqueante se insert falha.
- ⚠️ Key inclui minuteBucket (Math.floor(Date.now() / 60000)) — se 2 webhooks chegam em ms diferentes mas no mesmo minuto natural, MESMO content, ambos ganham a lock (race de <1s não é coberto, mutex deve pegar). Não documen risco de colisão em edge case: se msg é exatamente igual mas chega em 2 minutos naturais diferentes (00:00:59 e 00:01:01), ambos passam pois buckets diferentes. Improvável em prática.
- 🔧 Considerar trocar minuteBucket por finer granularity: 'decimalBucket = Math.floor(Date.now() / 5000)' (5s em vez de 60s) pra mais cobertura. Cron cleanup continua a 5min (TTL 60s auto-expira anyway). Adicionar índice em (rep_id, expires_at) pra queries de limpeza ficarem mais rápidas.

**Multi-hub Sparkbot Detection (isSparkbotHub) — 9/10**
- ✅ Implementação bem estruturada em /api/webhooks/inbound-message/route.ts:37-60 + hub-resolver.ts. Cache 5min em memória. Query DB: agents WHERE type=account_assistant AND status=active. Multi-hub ready. Fallback env ASSISTANT_HUB_LOCATION_ID documentado. Parity test pra migração simples.
- ⚠️ Cache em memória Map<string, {isHub, expiresAt}> é per-process (cada lambda tem sua cópia). Em scale com 100+ locations, 5min cache pode estar stale se agente é desativado/ativado freq. Cache não tem cache-busting mecânico.
- 🔧 Considerar adicionar webhook listener (ou cron) pra invalidar cache quando agents.status muda. Ou usar Redis pra cache distribuído entre lambdas (mais complexo, só pra scale >1000 locations).

**Placeholder Rejection (Audio Message./Image) — 8/10**
- ✅ Implementação robusta em webhook-handler.ts:366-410. PLACEHOLDER_TEXTS SET com 12 valores. Rejeita APENAS se texto é placeholder E NÃO tem attachment processável (audioUrl ou mediaAttachments). Aguarda webhook irmão com conteúdo real. Defensivo pra Stevo que manda 'Audio Message.' + audio_url juntos.
- ⚠️ Se um webhook chega com body='Audio Message.' + audio_url válida, o sistema reprocessa como áudio (linha 417-452) — mas se o transcribe falha, o rep vê mensagem de erro genérica em vez de claro 'áudio inválido'. Transcript failure codes (quota_exceeded, invalid_key, rate_limited) têm mensagens boas (lines 457-477), mas transcrição silenciosamente falhando ainda cai numa resposta genérica.
- 🔧 Se audioUrl existe mas transcribe falha com code=null (desconhecido), em vez de continuar como antes, retorne erro explícito tipo '__TRANSCRIBE_FAILED__: <ageMs>ms, retry'. Adicionar flag na config pra habilitar 'strict_audio_mode' que rejeita qualquer msg com áudio se transcribe falhar.

**Rep Identity Race Capture (Track 1 C3, 23505) — 9/10**
- ✅ Implementação excelente em identity.ts:207-213. Race entre 2 webhooks Stevo+GHL <100ms → ambos INSERT rep_identities → UNIQUE phone constraint salva segundo com 23505. Código re-fetches e retorna a row criada pelo competidor. Sem deadlock.
- ⚠️ Re-fetch pode teoricamente falhar (network blip, row was deleted miraculously) — código volta null nesse caso. O webhook que criou o rep segue normal, o que recebeu 23505 e não conseguiu refetch vai pedir phone novamente ao rep na próxima msg. Improvável mas não é zero-risk.
- 🔧 Adicionar 1 retry na re-fetch (max 3 attempts com 100ms backoff). Ou, mais defensivo, se re-fetch falha, sleep 200ms e tentar createAdminClient() nova vez (pode ser lock temporário). Adicionar metric 'rep_identity_race_detected' + 'rep_identity_race_refetch_failed' pra observabilidade.

**Stevo Handler Debounce & Burst — 7/10**
- ✅ Implementação criativa em stevo-handler.ts:306-360. Debounce pré-LLM (espera janela se STEVO_DEBOUNCE_MS > 0) + pré-envio (descartar resposta vazia se msg nova chegou durante geração). Filtra texto/interativo (áudio/imagem continuam na hora). resolveBurstTurn junta rajada num input só. Évita fragmentação de respostas.
- ⚠️ Debounce depende de timing absoluto (setTimeout) — se lambda tem GC/CPU contention, a 'janela esperada' pode estourar. Exemplo: STEVO_DEBOUNCE_MS=4000, mas lambda toma 200ms pra processar antes de chamar setTimeout → a nova msg chega em 3.8s (antes da espera), mas a janela real foi só 3.8s, msg mais nova não é capturada. shouldStillRespond re-checa DB, mas nada garante que a nova msg foi PERSISTIDA ainda (pode estar em memória, ainda não no DB). shouldStillRespond query pode falhar silenciosamente (erro catch → 'segue processando') — respostas duplicadas aí.
- 🔧 Em vez de setTimeout, usar um distributed lock (Redis SET NX + TTL) pra janela de debounce — evita timing issues. Ou, mais simples, adicionar coluna em sparkbot_messages 'is_burst_primary' marcando qual turno do burst é o que respondeu (previne duplicação mesmo se DB checks falharem). Reforçar shouldStillRespond: se query falha, BAIL (fail-closed) em vez de 'segue'.

**Silence & Proactive Pausing — 8/10**
- ✅ Implementação sólida em webhook-handler.ts:788-801. Qualquer inbound reseta silence counter + limpa flags proative_paused_at/proactive_warned_at. Silent fail-soft (não bloqueia webhook se update falha). Thresholds bem documentados em CLAUDE.md: 0/1=normal, 2=warning, 3=pause, ≥4 bloqueado.
- ⚠️ Update em rep_identities é async + non-blocking (segue processamento). Se o UPDATE não confirma antes do webhook terminar, o rep pode receber MULTIPLE proativos consecutivos mesmo tendo respondido (próximo cron tick não sabe que respondeu). Fix audit observou isso em stress test 2026-05-03 mas resolvido com `waitUntil` no webhook route (linha 285-295 em inbound-message/route.ts).
- 🔧 Adicionar transaction flag na update (ou advisory lock) pra garantir que silence reset é visível antes de proativo-runner ver o rep. Ou, mais simples, adicionar columnread-cache na proativo-runner (5min TTL local) pra não bater DB a cada tick — vai puxar o silence status em batch.

**Early Returns & Cleanup Guarantee — 9/10**
- ✅ Implementação muito boa em webhook-handler.ts:185-898. Try/finally wrapping o bulk do handler. cleanupInFlight() callback garante liberação em QUALQUER saída (early return, exception, error branch). Muito difícil vazar mutex lock.
- ⚠️ Se uma exceção é lançada FORA do try {} (ex: import() statement antes do try falha, ou createAdminClient() line 170 lança), mutex não é liberado. Improvável, mas possível em error edge cases (module resolution failure, admin client misconfiguration).
- 🔧 Mover createAdminClient() call para DENTRO do try {} block. Ou refactor pra factory function que sempre retorna um client válido (com fallback). Adicionar invariant check logo após mutex claim (line 165-168) pra garantir que try está setado.

### Structural issues
- **[MEDIUM] Dedup Layers 2-7 Are Interleaved with Flow** — Layers 2-7 (SELECT ghl_message_id, CONTENT-MATCH, TIMING-MATCH, dedup_locks INSERT, UNIQUE 23505, rep_identity 23505) não foram extraídas pra dedup-guard.ts porque estão **interleavadas** com o main flow (linhas 163-820 do handler). Movê-las quebraria control-flow e arriscaria alterar ingestão. Isso é defensivo do ponto de vista 'não mexe se tá funcionando', mas torna o webhook-handler um god-file de 900 LOC difícil de testar isoladamente. Quando Pedro precisa debugar dedup, precisa ler as 800 linhas inteiras. (src/lib/account-assistant/webhook-handler.ts (163-553))
- **[MEDIUM] No Unified Dedup Test Harness** — Cada camada é testada indiretamente via stress-test.ts ou smoke tests manuais. Não há script pra simular race conditions specific (2 webhooks <100ms, content-identical, messageId diferente). Stress test 2026-05-03 encontrou bugs, mas sem test automation, a próxima refactor pode reintroduzir bugs. Falta fixture 'race-scenario-simulator.ts' que coloca 10 webhooks em paralelo e valida que APENAS 1 resposta é enviada. (scripts/ (nenhum script de race-test encontrado))
- **[LOW] Placeholder PLACEHOLDER_TEXTS Set is Hardcoded** — Lista de placeholders (Audio Message., Image, Document, etc.) é hardcoded em webhook-handler.ts:377-390. Se GHL ou Stevo adicionarem novo tipo de placeholder, fica ignorado. Não há DB table ou config pra manter essa lista dinâmica. Se Pedro quer adicionar 'Voice Note' ou 'Arquivo', requer deploy. (src/lib/account-assistant/webhook-handler.ts (377-390), nenhuma config table)
- **[LOW] Hub Cache TTL Não É Configurável** — HUB_CACHE_TTL_MS = 5 * 60 * 1000 é hardcoded em webhook-handler.ts:34 e hub-resolver.ts:25. Não há env var. Se no futuro multi-hub scale requer cache invalidation mais agressivo (ex: 1min), precisa deploy. Não há admin UI pra invalidar cache manualmente. (src/lib/account-assistant/webhook-handler.ts:34, src/lib/account-assistant/hub-resolver.ts:25, src/app/api/webhooks/inbound-message/route.ts:34)
- **[MEDIUM] Stevo-only path doesn't have feature parity with GHL handler** — Stevo handler (stevo-handler.ts) implementa debounce, burst resolution, e pre-send check. GHL handler não tem esses. Se Stevo é declarado primário (SPARKBOT_INBOUND_PRIMARY=stevo), GHL fica fallback, mas se há bugs no Stevo debounce, não há fallback pro 'comportamento simples do GHL'. Inversamente, se GHL é primário e Stevo é fallback, Stevo nunca roda (nunca descobre bugs). Feature parity checklist não existe em docs. (src/lib/account-assistant/webhook/stevo-handler.ts vs webhook-handler.ts (falta parity matrix em _planning/))
- **[LOW] Rep Identity Phone Normalization has edge cases** — normalizePhone() em identity.ts:32-47 usa generatePhoneCandidates() — suporta BR (+55) e US (+1). Se rep tá em outro país (México +52, Arg +54), será normalizado como +1 (default US). Em scale com clientes multipaís, essa heurística falha. Não há way pra passar país explícito (seria via location.country_code, não implementado). Será problema em prod quando tem cliente no México. (src/lib/account-assistant/identity.ts:32-95)
- **[LOW] In-flight Mutex TTL Hardcoded** — IN_FLIGHT_TTL_MS = 60_000 em dedup-guard.ts:53 é constante. Se dup-burst é muito lento (lambda contention, rede lenta, ghl api latência), 60s pode expirar antes da 2ª call chegar. Não há env var. Falta documentação pra Pedro saber quando aumentar. (src/lib/account-assistant/webhook/dedup-guard.ts:53)

### Production blockers
- **[PARTIAL/MEDIUM] CRITICAL: Placeholder rejection race com Stevo + GHL** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Quando Stevo + WhatsApp Business API estão ambos ativos, webhook do GHL pode chegar com body='Audio Message.' (placeholder) sem attachment. Código atual rejeita (line 404-409), esperando webhook irmão. Mas se webhook irmão (Stevo) chega ANTES da rejeição ter sido persistida, Stevo vê a msg do rep como 'não processada ainda' e processa. GHL vira fallback. Dois webhooks tentam processar, mutex/dedup pode falhar em race <100ms (mutex é per-lambda). Resultado: duas respostas possíveis.
  - Fix: Antes de rejeitar placeholder, inserir row em sparkbot_messages com flag 'is_placeholder_stub=true'. Stevo dedup SELECT vai ver a row e sabe que GHL já iniciou (dedup by ghlMessageId já existe). Ou mais simples: NO PRODUCTION até que Stevo + GHL não rodem simultâneos (use SPARKBOT_INBOUND_PRIMARY=stevo pra designar primário).
  - Veredicto: src/lib/account-assistant/webhook-handler.ts:366-410 (placeholder rejection) — código rejeita por retorno simples sem persistência; src/lib/account-assistant/webhook-handler.ts:298-331 (CONTENT DEDUP LOCK, camada 4) — chave é rep_id|minuteBucket|content, logo GHL placeholder e Stevo real com conteúdos diferentes conseguem locks distintos; src/lib/account-assistant/webhook-handler.ts:518-552 (TIMING-MATCH) — SELECT não encontra nada se GHL foi rejeitado, logo não bloqueia Stevo; _planning/_review-2026-05-19/B2-tools-loop.md:130-149 (P0 #2) — documenta race real comprovada em prod com "Oi" (texto idêntico), E menciona áudio com placeholder mas com conteúdos diferentes ("contexto atualizado" vs "Não consigo processar áudio"), confirmando que há janela onde ambos podem tentar processar. PORÉM: (a) placeholder rejection retorna sem processar/inserir, logo não gera resposta (diferente de P0 #2 onde ambos geram respostas); (b) se GHL retenta no MESMO minuto (0-60s), CONTENT DEDUP LOCK (camada 4) bloqueia via minuteBucket-based key UNIQUE constraint; (c) se retenta em minuto diferente, content-hash lock (camada 8, 2s janela) em dedup-guard.ts:125-216 bloqueia concorrentes reais (<2s).
- **[CONFIRMED/MEDIUM] CRITICAL: Content-Hash Lock (Camada 8) não cobre Stevo-only race** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Content-hash lock é desligado por padrão em Stevo (apenas GHL usa, linha dedup-guard.ts:348). Mas stevo-handler.ts faz dedup upfront APENAS por ghlMessageId (line 219-232), não pelo content-hash. Se Stevo dispara DOIS webhooks com messageId DISTINTOS (improvável mas teoricamente possível em network retry), ambos passam no SELECT upfront e vão pro INSERT simultaneously. UNIQUE constraint em ghl_message_id não pega (IDs diferentes). Se o conteúdo é idêntico, nenhuma das 7 camadas bloqueia porque stevo-handler não implementa CONTENT-MATCH ou TIMING-MATCH (apenas webhook-handler faz).
  - Fix: Adicionar em stevo-handler.ts after line 244 (após buildRepInput), mesma lógica de TIMING-MATCH: SELECT sparkbot_messages WHERE rep_id, created_at >= 5s atrás, role=user. Ou usar tryContentDedupLock (camada 8) também no stevo-handler. Recomendação: alinha ambos os handlers.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/account-assistant/webhook/stevo-handler.ts:219-232 — findByGhlMessageId(parsed.messageId) é o ÚNICO dedup antes do INSERT. Linhas 254-276 fazem INSERT direto em sparkbot_messages sem chamar tryContentDedupLock, sem INSERT em sparkbot_dedup_locks (camada 3), sem CONTENT-MATCH check (camada 4), sem TIMING-MATCH check (camada 5). Comparar com src/lib/account-assistant/webhook-handler.ts que implementa: (1) tryClaimInFlight linha 165, (2) SELECT ghl_message_id linhas 171-175, (3) sparkbot_dedup_locks insert linhas 307-331, (4) CONTENT-MATCH 15s linhas 492-516, (5) TIMING-MATCH 5s linhas 529-552, (6) UNIQUE constraint na insert linha 778, (7) rep_identity 23505 via identifyRep, (8) tryContentDedupLock linha 348-359. Stevo-handler ausente de 1, 3, 4, 5, 8. src/lib/account-assistant/webhook/dedup-guard.ts linhas 20-26 documentam que camada 8 é "blindagem pra quando a API voltar" (i.e., quando multi-provider Stevo/GHL). Sem implementação em stevo-handler, exposição é real.
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] CRITICAL: Timing-Match (Camada 5) pode bloquear intencionais** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Se rep manda 2 msgs legítimas em 4s (ex: 'Quero...' / '...atualizar'), a 2ª será bloqueada por timing-match (line 518-552). Sem feedback ao rep que msg foi descartada. Rep nunca recebe confirmação, fica esperando resposta, envia a 2ª msg novamente em 10s (agora passa), mas o histórico perde a mensagem original. Se isso acontece ao vivo em prod, não temos métrica pra detectar ('timing_match_rejected' log existe mas não tá em admin-signals). Pedro pode não saber que 5% das respostas foram perdidas por timing-match falso-positivo.
  - Fix: Adicionar signal admin_signals: { feature: 'sparkbot-timing-match-rejected', rep_id, ageMs, prev_content, current_kind }. Query esse signal em admin-panel / metrics. Ou reduzir de 5s para 3s janela + monitor. Considerar excluir multi-media (áudio/imagem/doc) da timing-match (esses casi são raros em rajada <5s).
  - Veredicto: src/lib/account-assistant/webhook-handler.ts:518-552 — TIMING-MATCH bloqueia com return silencioso em linha 548 se rep tem qualquer msg nos últimos 5s. Sem recordSignalAsync/admin_signals trigger. Msg bloqueada não é persistida (return ANTES do INSERT em linha 760). console.warn em linha 544 é único log, não integrado em admin-signals.ts que é o painel visível para Pedro. Verificação exaustiva: grep -r "timing_match\|TIMING.*MATCH" retorna apenas webhook-handler.ts e dedup-guard.ts (comments). Nenhum recordSignalAsync em webhook-handler.ts para dedup rejeições. src/app/admin/signals/signals-client.tsx não inclui filtro ou métrica para "timing_match_rejected".
- **[CONFIRMED/MEDIUM] MEDIUM: Stevo Handler doesn't persist ghl_contact_id in metadata** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: GHL handler persists ghl_contact_id em metadata (line 772 + 852). Stevo handler não adiciona isso (stevo-handler.ts line 263-276). Quando proativos (reminder-runner) querem contactar o rep via Stevo, não conseguem mapear rep_id → ghl_contact_id (usado pra enviar msgs no GHL). A aba de conversas no Web UI (painel SparkBot) filtra por ghl_contact_id para achar a conversa certa. Sem isso, histórico fica perdido / desincronizado.
  - Fix: Adicionar lookup: stevo-handler.ts line 234-241 após identifyRep, query GHL /users/search para puxar ghl_contact_id do rep nessaLocation. Armazenar em metadata. Ou docum pra Pedro que Stevo setup requer location_id do rep ter contato_id já mapeado (nem sempre verdade — Stevo é channel separado).
  - Veredicto: stevo-handler.ts:263-275 (user msg metadata SEM ghl_contact_id) vs webhook-handler.ts:769-771 (GHL user msg metadata COM ghl_contact_id). Idêntico em agent msgs: stevo-handler.ts:523-540 SEM vs webhook-handler.ts:846-852 COM. Impacto confirmado em sparkbot-messages.repo.ts:115 que usa .filter("metadata->>ghl_contact_id") e webhook-handler.ts:247 (REACTION recency check). Histórico: commit 8226033 (2026-05-03) fixou problema similar para GHL agent msgs ("ghl_contact_id também em role=agent" pois "só user msgs tinham")
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] MEDIUM: No metrics on actual dedup effectiveness** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Sistema tem 8 camadas de dedup, mas ZERO observabilidade quantitativa. Não há gauge pra 'quantas msgs foram bloqueadas por dedup' vs 'quantas passaram'. Stressor tests em 2026-05-03 encontraram bugs, mas sem produção dados, não sabemos se o sistema está **realmente** protegido. Se um novo bug de race aparecer (ex: cache TTL muito curto, 5min desincroniza hub list), ninguém detecta até que Pedro reporte múltiplas respostas duplicadas.
  - Fix: Adicionar instrumentation: cada dedup layer (mutex, SELECT, content-match, timing-match, content-hash, UNIQUE) publica CountMetric ('sparkbot_dedup_hit', tags ['layer']). Dashboard mostra % de hits por layer. Setup alert: 'timing_match_rejected > 10/min' (indica muita perda de msg legítima).
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] MEDIUM: Placeholder rejection loses audio if extraction fails** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Lines 396-399 extraem audio/media para decidir se rejeita placeholder. Se extractAudioUrl falha (timeout, network, corrupted attachment), hasUsableAttachment=false, placeholder é rejeitado. Mas quando webhook irmão (real content) chega, eles são processados independentemente — nada garante que o audio_url real que o webhook irmão traz é o MESMO que foi tentado aqui. Se ambos webhooks têm audio mas um falha extract, pode haver 2 inserts (msg perdida no caminho).
  - Fix: Não confiar em extractAudioUrl == null como prova de 'placeholder'. Verificar body.attachments array directly: se > 0 items com type audio/*, há audio mesmo se URL extraction falhou. Ou mais defensivo: só rejeitar placeholder se bODY.attachments está completamente vazio OU não contém mime-type compatível.


---

## SparkBot — processor, loop LLM & guardas

SparkBot is the rep-facing conversational agent powered by Claude (primary) with Haiku (secondary) and GPT-4.1 (fallback). The processor (processor.ts) orchestrates inbound messages through a complex pipeline: terms validation → location resolution → LLM with tools via runWithTools → coherence gate (F53, F54) → anti-repeat guard (F57) → billing. The loop is multi-iteration (max 10 turns), with fallback chain (Sonnet 4.6 → Haiku 4.5 → GPT-4.1, STRICT_CLAUDE_ONLY flag stops OpenAI). Multiple loop-breakers exist but have edge cases and coordination issues that could trap reps in repeat loops or fail silently.

### Funcionalidades

**LLM Fallback Chain (3-tier) — 8/10**
- ✅ Correct implementation: Claude Sonnet 4.6 primary, Haiku 4.5 secondary (same provider, different pool), GPT-4.1 tertiary. STRICT_CLAUDE_ONLY=1 flag blocks OpenAI. Detects rate limits, credit issues, API down. Signals admin when both Claude layers fail (F49 in prod, reportError via Sentry). LLMFailureMidLoop exception prevents double-execution of side-effects after tools have run. Cache control applied to system prompt + last tool (30% token economy).
- ⚠️ Fallback happens ONLY at iteration 0 (before any tools). If Claude fails after executing tools in iteration N, no fallback—returns error stub immediately. Haiku fallback doesn't inherit the same `max_tokens=2500` config (uses DEFAULT_MODEL constant). If admin misconfigures fallback_model (e.g., invalid OpenAI key), OpenAI error is caught but error message not traced back to the config. Tertiary fallback to GPT-4.1 still happens even if STRICT_CLAUDE_ONLY=1 flip happens mid-request (env read via function, not cached).
- 🔧 (1) Document that mid-loop Claude failures are non-recoverable and expected (reps see honest error). (2) Add visibility: if BOTH Claude primary and secondary fail, log which one was chosen as fallback (currently both failures log, but fallback choice not explicit). (3) Add metric for 'secondary fallback used' to distinguish from tertiary. (4) Validate fallback_model config at startup (cache in memory, not per-request).

**Coherence Gate (F53 / F54 Loop-Breaker) — 6/10**
- ✅ Correctly separates violations into specific (family-based patterns) and generic (1st-person write verbs). Distinguishes 'rerun' (safe when no write succeeded) vs 'rewrite' (when write already happened, don't duplicate). Detects opportunity CREATE vs MOVE/UPDATE (case Henry). Has loop-breaker: if fallback 'still not consegui concluir' already sent last turn, doesn't repeat it (prevents N-turn trap). Negation/preview detection eliminates false-positives ('não tenho nota' not flagged). F54 (false-positive reduction) uses 8 heuristics.
- ⚠️ isNegatedOrPreviewContext() heuristics are regex-based and brittle. Example: 'Sem nenhuma nova tarefa criada' might not match all negation patterns in Portuguese (NER would be more robust). The loop-breaker detection (alreadyWarnedLastTurn) checks for exact substring 'ainda não consegui concluir isso aqui' — if bot uses slightly different wording, it won't detect the previous fallback. Violations array includes duplicates if match same text via both specific and generic patterns (dedup not happening). analyzeCoherence() called AFTER billing but BEFORE sending, meaning re-run tokens not counted in usage_records.charged_at (audit trail wrong).
- 🔧 (1) Add NER/semantic check for negation (not just regex). (2) Parameterize fallback text so loop-breaker detection is robust. (3) Deduplicate violations by matched_text. (4) Move coherence re-run BEFORE billing or explicitly track re-run tokens separately in usage_records. (5) Log coherence.action (rerun vs rewrite) to understand gate distribution in prod.

**Anti-Repeat Guard (F57 Sieder / Soraia Fix) — 7/10**
- ✅ Detects when bot will send near-duplicate of recent assistant message (lookback=2 covers A-B-A pattern). normalizeForRepeat() removes accents, punctuation, emojis, whitespace (good catch for ' Confirma? ✅' vs 'confirma'). MIN_REPEAT_LEN=25 prevents killing legitimate short acks ('ok', 'feito'). isNearDuplicate() handles both exact match and 80% containment (for msgs with minor additions). Re-run uses no-tools directive to avoid side-effects. If re-run still repeats or returns empty, hard fallback 'Opa, acho que acabei te respondendo...' guaranteed different. Signal logged when guard fires.
- ⚠️ Guard runs AFTER billing (line 762) — re-run tokens not in usage_records.charged_at (same issue as coherence). If re-run itself returns empty string, logic doesn't check and may return empty `broke` variable, which becomes finalText=''→'Não consegui gerar resposta. Tenta de novo?' (fallback in return statement, but loses interactive payload). The echo detection uses `history` from messages passed to LLM — if coherence gate already mutated result.text once, the history still has old assistant message, so second echo check might miss it. Test mode exempt (no re-run in tests) but tests can't validate the behavior.
- 🔧 (1) Move anti-repeat re-run BEFORE billing or track tokens separately. (2) If re-run returns empty, explicitly log and use hard fallback (don't rely on outer return logic). (3) Document that coherence gate mutates result.text first, so echo check sees the old historical message, not the rewritten one. (4) Enable guard in test mode (or create separate test for it). (5) Add metric: 'anti_repeat_guard_fired' to measure loop frequency in prod.

**Conversation History Handling (Empty Message Vulnerability) — 4/10**
- ✅ stevo-handler.ts (line 348) filters empty messages: filter((m) => (m.content || '').trim().length > 0). webhook-handler.ts also filters (line comment 'FILTRA mensagens com content vazio'). processor.ts correctly explains why: Claude rejects with 400 'user messages must have non-empty content'. CLAUDE.md (line 100) documents the rule.
- ⚠️ CRITICAL: processor.ts (line 436-439) does NOT filter conversationHistory after receiving it:

const history = (input.conversationHistory || []).map((t) => ({
  role: t.role,
  content: t.content,  // ← could be ''
}));

Both callers (stevo-handler, webhook-handler) filter BEFORE calling processor, BUT processor doesn't validate input—if conversationHistory comes from anywhere else or if a caller misses the filter, empty messages go to LLM. This is a safety-net failure. If any empty message sneaks in, llm-client.ts (runWithClaude, runWithOpenAI) will pass it directly without validation → Claude returns 400 → stopped_reason='error' → fallback chain. Empty messages are rare (filtered at source) but possible under edge cases (import via API, test mode, future refactors).
- 🔧 (1) Filter conversationHistory in processor.ts before building the messages array (add .filter((m) => (m.content || '').trim().length > 0)). (2) Add unit test that sends empty ConversationTurn and validates it's rejected gracefully. (3) Document in ProcessInput interface that conversationHistory MUST have non-empty content (contract enforcement). (4) Consider validating in buildUserMessage() as well for defense-in-depth.

**Tool Call Deduplication (F58) — 9/10**
- ✅ Prevents duplicate write (create_task, create_note, etc.) with identical args in same turn. stableArgs() produces stable JSON signature. writeCache Map tracks by name::args. If repeat detected, returns previous result with deduped_in_turn=true flag (idempotent). Only for idempotent create tools, not send_message (2 sends may be intentional). Catches case Soraia (7 duplicate reminders from 1 re-call in iteration 2). Executor wrapped cleanly (dedupExecutor).
- ⚠️ Signature is stable JSON but doesn't account for field order (though JSON.stringify of sorted keys should be stable). If tool result changes structure (e.g., first call returns {id:'X'}, second call returns {id:'X',created:true}), both considered 'same result' (content equality not checked). Tests unclear—no visible test-dedup-f58.ts script. Integration with coherence gate unclear: if a tool is deduped, does the result count as 'succeeded' for the coherence family? (Assumption: yes, because code marks it .status='ok' implicitly).
- 🔧 (1) Add unit test for F58 dedup (scripts/test-f58-dedup.ts). (2) Document deduped_in_turn flag and how it affects coherence/billing. (3) Consider deep equality check for tool results (not just caching by signature). (4) Log when dedup fires (currently only .warn in console, not tracked in metadata).

**Max Iterations Limit (10 turns) — 7/10**
- ✅ MAX_ITERATIONS=10 set in llm-client.ts. Prevents infinite loops. Bumped from 6→10 in H30.3 to support multi-action chaining (rep sends 1 msg, bot executes N tools in one turn). Both Claude and OpenAI paths enforce it. Clear fallback message when reached: 'Executei várias ações mas preciso parar aqui.' Signal logged in processor when stopped_reason='max_iterations' (F49).
- ⚠️ Max iterations is PER CALL TO runWithTools, but processor may call runWithTools TWICE: (1) initial turn, (2) coherence re-run. If initial turn hits max_iterations and re-run also hits max, tokens not aggregated—result shows only 1st turm's iteration count. iterationsCompleted in LLMFailureMidLoop exception not used to distinguish iteration 0 (fallback OK) vs N>0 (no fallback). If MAX_ITERATIONS = 10 and rep sends msg with 11 separate tool calls needed, bot silently fails (stopped_reason='max_iterations', not 'error').
- 🔧 (1) Document that max_iterations is per-call, not per-turn (coherence re-run is separate). (2) Track total iterations across initial + re-run and log when exceeded. (3) Dynamically adjust MAX_ITERATIONS if new tools with lower token cost added (currently constant, not tuned to model/tools). (4) Add test case: rep requests 11 actions, verify graceful degradation.

**Debounce (Latest-Wins Strategy) — 8/10**
- ✅ stevo-handler implements latest-wins correctly: waits debounceMs, then checks shouldStillRespond() — if msg more recent or agent already responded, bails (early-out). Combines text-burst via resolveBurstTurn() — rajada não-respondida collapses into 1 input. Media (audio/image/doc) excluded from debounce (processed on arrival). Pré-LLM AND pré-envio checks prevent stragglers arriving during generation. Idempotent by message ID (double-invocation from Stevo same-ID deduped upfront).
- ⚠️ STEVO_DEBOUNCE_MS=0 by default (OFF), so debounce is opt-in via env. If not set, each msg instant-reply → fragmented output (observed in 15:34 EDT flow). resolveBurstTurn() combines text but MUTATES the input.input (creates new RepInput)—if caller holds reference to old input, confusion. No dedup of text msgs themselves (if rep sends 'hi' twice in quick burst, both might get combined into 'hi\nhi' if debounce just missed).
- 🔧 (1) Change STEVO_DEBOUNCE_MS default to 4000 (4s) instead of 0—better UX with minimal latency. (2) Document the default is OFF for compatibility; need explicit flag to enable. (3) Add integration test for debounce (verify rajada collapses). (4) Clearly return NEW RepInput, don't mutate caller's input.

**Interactive Mode (Buttons/Lists) & Backstop Fallback — 8/10**
- ✅ extractInteractiveFromToolCalls() looks for present_options tool, extracts payload. Auto-chooses buttons vs list based on #options and label length. interactiveFallbackText() generates text with numbered options (1. Option, 2. Option) for fallback (web/GHL). detectNumberedOptionsFallback() (BACKSTOP) converts numerically-listed text to InteractivePayload if LLM forgot present_options but wrote list—catches 'LLM sees but forgets present_options' (adoption boost without 100% compliance). Footer/title support. Striping em-dashes (—) to prevent AI aesthetics.
- ⚠️ BACKSTOP only triggers if CUE (qual/escolha/preferir/opção or ends '?') detected, MISSING if bot wrote list without cue (false-negative). Interactive payload size cap is 10 options per WhatsApp spec, silently truncates beyond. If present_options is called MULTIPLE times in 1 turn, only LAST one extracted (earlier prompts ignored—could be bug if bot presented 2 separate choice points). stripDashes() runs AFTER interactiveVia determined, so metric doesn't know if dashes caused stripping.
- 🔧 (1) Add BACKSTOP detection for lists without explicit CUE if item count ≥4 and numeric pattern clear. (2) Log when >10 options detected and truncated (audit metric). (3) Document: only LAST present_options is used (or change to support sequential prompts). (4) Test en-dashes (–) and em-dashes (—) both stripped correctly.

**Confirmation Gate & Tool Input Validation — 7/10**
- ✅ H8 pattern: tools with risk='medium'|'high' require confirmed_by_rep:true input. getAllToolDefinitions() injects param dynamically based on agent_configs.confirmation_mode. executeTool() enforces at tool-level (reads confirmed_by_rep flag before executing). LLM is instructed to ask 'Confirma?' and wait. Re-call with confirmed_by_rep=true proceeds. Prevents accidental send/delete operations.
- ⚠️ Confirmation gate enforced in executeTool() AFTER the tool is called—if tool's first action fires before the check (rare, shouldn't happen with proper tool design), confirmation would come too late. Waits for rep's response: if rep says 'ok' but LLM interprets as REFUSAL and rephrases WITHOUT re-calling tool, the tool was never executed → bot lies ('feito') with coherence gate as backup. Confirmation mode 'always' means EVERY tool needs confirm, potentially freezing rep. No UI indicator that tool is pending confirmation (LLM must remember and ask).
- 🔧 (1) Add pre-execution validation in executeTool() to verify confirmed_by_rep=true BEFORE any side-effect. (2) Log confirmation flow (rep asked, confirmed, executed) for audit. (3) Add metric: % of tools requiring confirmation vs completed without gate blocks. (4) Document: if rep refuses confirmation, tool NOT executed but LLM may still claim it (coherence gate fallback).

**Test Mode Gate (Idempotent, No Billing) — 9/10**
- ✅ testSessionId !== null + risk !== 'safe' → tool returns {simulated:true}. Read-only tools (search, get, list, analyze_tabular_data) always execute (preserve analysis). Test mode persists to agent_test_messages table, has separate history track. Prevents accidental charges or side-effects in synthetic tests. Matches strategy: full execution for info-gathering, mock for mutations.
- ⚠️ Distinction between 'safe' and non-safe tools is in tool definitions (hardcoded). New tools default to 'safe' (benign) if not explicitly marked. If risk field missing, defaults to safe (permissive). Calling code doesn't validate risk field exists. Test mode gate is BEFORE execution, but billing happens AFTER—if billing fails, test run might still charge (mitigation: usesCustomKey flag for internal/test, but not automatic).
- 🔧 (1) Validate all tools have explicit risk field (no defaults). (2) Log test mode execution separately (test_token_usage vs real_token_usage). (3) Add admin dashboard widget: test runs per agent, cost if charged, simulated vs real. (4) Document: test mode executes search/get/list fully (not simulated) for realistic AI learning.

**Error Handling & Fallback Text Generation — 6/10**
- ✅ Multiple fallback messages: parse error → 'Tive problema técnico...pode tentar de novo'; max_iterations → 'Executei várias ações...'; no response → 'Não consegui gerar resposta. Tenta de novo?'. LLMFailureMidLoop distinguishes mid-loop failures (no fallback, honest error). reportError() signals admin when both Claude primaries fail (F49). Billing failure is non-blocking (console.error, continues).
- ⚠️ Fallback messages are generic and don't indicate ROOT CAUSE to rep (max_iterations looks same as parse error to rep). If parser fails (JSON malformed from Claude), error string not trimmed—may expose internal error to rep. Fallback stub (llmFailureStub) always uses DEFAULT_MODEL even if primary was custom model (confusing for audit). No distinction in fallback between 'rate limit' (transient) vs '401' (config issue) vs '5xx API down'—all get same 'problem técnico' message. Test mode LLM failures not surfaced (tests see error stub, no retry signal).
- 🔧 (1) Generate fallback text based on stopped_reason (parse vs timeout vs max_iter): 'Tive problema com a parsing...' vs 'Executei ações demais...'. (2) Sanitize error messages before returning (remove stack traces, API keys). (3) Use correct model in fallback stub. (4) Log specific failure reason to admin signal (rate limit vs API down vs auth) for faster triage. (5) In test mode, surface LLM failures so test developer can debug.

### Structural issues
- **[HIGH] Empty Message Vulnerability in Conversation History** — processor.ts line 436-439 builds LLM messages without filtering empty content. While stevo-handler and webhook-handler filter BEFORE calling processor, processor.ts doesn't add a defensive filter. If conversationHistory is supplied from any other source (API, future refactor, test), empty messages bypass validation and cause Claude 400 error, triggering fallback chain. CLAUDE.md line 100 says this should be filtered everywhere. (/src/lib/account-assistant/processor.ts (line 436-439), /src/lib/account-assistant/llm-client.ts (no validation))
- **[MEDIUM] Coherence & Anti-Repeat Re-Run Tokens Not in Billing Audit Trail** — Both coherence gate (line 612) and anti-repeat guard (line 770) call runWithTools for recovery, adding tokens to result.prompt/completion_tokens. BUT billing happens at line 690, BEFORE these re-runs. So usage_records.charged_at shows only original tokens, not recovery tokens. Auditing token costs per agent is inaccurate (+10-20% undercount if re-runs frequent). (/src/lib/account-assistant/processor.ts (billing line 690 vs coherence/anti-repeat lines 612, 770))
- **[MEDIUM] Loop-Breaker Detection Relies on Exact String Match** — Coherence gate loop-breaker (line 594-598) checks if last assistant message includes 'ainda não consegui concluir isso aqui' (exact substring). If bot uses any variation ('ainda não consegui fazer', 'não consegui completar isso'), the breaker won't detect prior fallback and may repeat fallback N turns (case Sieder already observed). This is fragile maintenance burden. (/src/lib/account-assistant/processor.ts (line 594-598), /src/lib/account-assistant/core/coherence-gate.ts (line 230))
- **[MEDIUM] Negation Detection Heuristics Are Regex-Based & Brittle** — isNegatedOrPreviewContext() in coherence-gate.ts uses 8 regex patterns to filter false-positives (lines 127-142). Patterns are English-aware but Portuguese negation is rich (não, nem, nenhum, nunca, sem, etc.) and context-dependent. Example: 'Sem nenhuma tarefa criada agora' might not match negation lookbehind. NER or semantic understanding would be more robust. (/src/lib/account-assistant/core/coherence-gate.ts (lines 124-142))
- **[LOW] Max Iterations Per-Call, Not Per-Turn** — MAX_ITERATIONS=10 is enforced in each runWithTools call. If processor calls runWithTools twice (initial + coherence re-run), each gets 10 iterations independently. This is correct behavior but implicit—documentation and logging don't make it clear. If future code adds a 3rd re-run (e.g., after anti-repeat fails), iteration budgets could fragment unexpectedly. (/src/lib/account-assistant/llm-client.ts (line 16, 366-519, 570-650))
- **[MEDIUM] Debounce Disabled by Default (STEVO_DEBOUNCE_MS=0)** — debounce defaults OFF (line 62 of stevo-handler.ts). Rep sending msg burst gets N instant responses (fragmented output, seen in prod 15:34 EDT case). Turning it ON requires explicit env config. Better default would be 4000ms (4s), with explicit OFF flag if needed. Current design risks prod surprises on new deployments. (/src/lib/account-assistant/webhook/stevo-handler.ts (lines 61-64))
- **[MEDIUM] Tool Result Truncation (12KB) Can Silently Lose Data** — MAX_TOOL_RESULT_CHARS=12000 (line 48, llm-client.ts) truncates tool results with OMITTED notice. Some tools (get_conversation_history, bulk_analysis) can return MB. Truncation preserves head+tail but removes middle. If tool result includes critical middle data (contact name in middle of list), bot gets corrupted data without knowing it. LLM sees '[TRUNCATED: X chars]' but may ignore and hallucinate. (/src/lib/account-assistant/llm-client.ts (lines 48-57))
- **[LOW] Duplicate Violations in Coherence Analysis** — analyzeCoherence() (coherence-gate.ts line 197-240) can generate duplicate violations if the same text matches both a specific pattern (e.g., 'note_create') AND the generic verb pattern. Violations array not deduplicated, so signal might report same issue twice. (/src/lib/account-assistant/core/coherence-gate.ts (lines 197-240))

### Production blockers
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] Conversation History May Contain Empty Messages Under Certain Paths** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: processor.ts doesn't validate ConversationTurn.content after receiving it from caller. While primary callers (stevo-handler, webhook-handler) filter, if ANY code path supplies conversationHistory without filtering, empty messages reach LLM → Claude 400 error → fallback chain triggered. This is silent degradation, not obvious failure.
  - Fix: Add .filter((m) => (m.content || '').trim().length > 0) in processor.ts line 436-439 before building history. Add unit test: ProcessInput with empty ConversationTurn should pass after filtering.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/account-assistant/processor.ts:436 — The critical vulnerability:
```
const history: LLMMessage[] = (input.conversationHistory || []).map((t) => ({
  role: t.role,
  content: t.content,
}));
```
NO VALIDATION of content before sending to LLM. Empty strings pass through.

Three production paths bypass the filter:

1. /api/sparkbot/send/route.ts:90 — Web UI (PRODUCTION):
```
const conversationHistory: ConversationTurn[] = priorMsgs.reverse().map((m) => ({ role: m.role === "user" ? "user" : "assistant", content: m.content }));
```
No filter. Empty content strings from DB reach processor.ts line 436.

2. /api/agents/account-assistant/test/route.ts:174 — Test endpoint:
```
const conversationTurns: ConversationTurn[] = priorMessages.map((m) => ({
  role: m.role === "user" ? "user" : "assistant",
  content: m.content,
}));
```
No filter. Empty content strings reach processor.ts line 436.

3. /api/agents/account-assistant/synthetic-test/route.ts:152 — Synthetic test:
Same pattern, no filter.

LLM consumption chain (src/lib/account-assistant/llm-client.ts:350):
```
const messages: AnthropicMessage[] = input.messages.map((m) => ({
  role: m.role,
  content: typeof m.content === "string" ? m.content : (m.content as AnthropicBlock[]),
}));
```
Messages sent directly to client.messages.create() at line 383 without validation.

Consequence: Empty-content message triggers 400 "user messages must have non-empty content" error at Anthropic API. Caught at llm-client.ts:400 as generic error, triggers fallback chain (Haiku→OpenAI) which is silent degradation.

Webhook-handler (src/lib/account-assistant/webhook-handler.ts:719) DOES filter:
```
const conversationHistory: ConversationTurn[] = priorMsgs
  .reverse()
  .filter((m) => (m.content || "").trim().length > 0)
  .map(...)
```

Stevo-handler (src/lib/account-assistant/webhook/stevo-handler.ts:346) DOES filter:
```
const chrono = prior.reverse().filter((m) => (m.content || "").trim().length > 0);
```

But processor.ts itself has NO defensive validation. Thus any future caller or configuration drift leaves the system vulnerable. Schema allows empty strings (content TEXT NOT NULL allows "" ≠ NULL).
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] Coherence Loop-Breaker Can Fail If Bot's Fallback Text Changes** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: Loop-breaker (processor.ts line 594-598) detects prior fallback by exact substring match 'ainda não consegui concluir isso aqui'. If that text is updated (typo fix, localization), loop-breaker breaks. Sieder/Soraia cases (repeated fallback) would recur.
  - Fix: Parameterize fallback text in coherence-gate.ts line 230 as a const. Import it in processor.ts line 594 and match against it. Add test: two consecutive coherence gates on same violation → 2nd doesn't repeat fallback.
  - Veredicto: processor.ts:594-598 uses `.includes("ainda não consegui concluir isso aqui")` as hardcoded literal string match. coherence-gate.ts:230-231 defines `safeRewrite = "Na real, ainda não consegui concluir isso aqui — não quero te dizer que fiz algo que não foi feito. Pode confirmar pra eu tentar de novo?"`. The substring is embedded in exactly one fallback message. If either text is modified (typo correction, pt-BR/en-US localization, rewording), the `.includes()` check will fail to detect prior warnings, breaking the loop-breaker logic. The detector appears at lines 594-598 (exact match): `(lastAssistantMsg.content as string).toLowerCase().includes("ainda não consegui concluir isso aqui")`. If the fallback text at coherence-gate.ts:231 is changed to e.g. "Na real, ainda não consegui concluir — não quero..." (dropping "isso aqui"), the detector breaks. No constant defined, no parameterization, substring hardcoded in two separate locations. This is confirmed as a real vulnerability by the CLAUDE.md memory referencing the Sieder/Soraia cases where the coherence gate caused repeated fallback loops that required the loop-breaker to activate.
- **[PARTIAL/HIGH] STEVO_DEBOUNCE_MS Disabled by Default—Prod Risk** (conf: medium)
  - Porquê: Debounce OFF (=0) means rapid text bursts → N instant replies. Observed in prod (15:34 EDT, case mentioned in stevo-handler comment). When STEVO_SEND_ENABLED=1 flips on, debounce should default ON to avoid surprising message fragmentation.
  - Fix: Change getDebounceMs() line 62 default from 0 to 4000. Document in env schema. Add integration test: send 3 msgs in 100ms, verify 1 response combining all 3.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/account-assistant/webhook/stevo-handler.ts:58-64 — getDebounceMs() returns 0 by default via `parseInt(process.env.STEVO_DEBOUNCE_MS?.trim() || "0", 10)`. Comment at 58-60 states: "Default OFF (0) — ligar via STEVO_DEBOUNCE_MS=4000 no go-live supervisionado. Assim deployar NÃO muda o timing das respostas até a gente validar junto" (intentional conservative default).

Burst fragmentation WAS OBSERVED: stevo-handler.ts:307-308 references "fluxo 15:34 EDT" where "2 msgs em 3s viravam 2 respostas fragmentadas" — matches claim.

Code has defensive safeguards: stevo-handler.ts:314-339 (pre-LLM check when debounceMs > 0) and stevo-handler.ts:402-423 (pre-send reprocessing check) prevent duplicate sends. Pre-send works for text-only, no-side-effects; confirmations/tools still fire.

The actual risk: STEVO_SEND_ENABLED and STEVO_DEBOUNCE_MS are independent gates. No validation enforces they work together. When admin turns on STEVO_SEND_ENABLED=1 without setting STEVO_DEBOUNCE_MS=4000, rapid bursts will each process independently (4s pre-LLM gate skipped), and each may send separately if they have side effects.
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] Re-Run Tokens (Coherence, Anti-Repeat) Not in Usage Records** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: Billing happens before coherence/anti-repeat re-runs (processor.ts line 690 vs 612, 770). usage_records shows undercounted tokens. Long-term: cost per agent, billing accuracy, scaling predictions all wrong. If 20% of turns need recovery re-runs, cost tracking is 20% low.
  - Fix: Move billing AFTER anti-repeat guard (line 816 final text), or track recovery tokens separately in usage_records.recovery_tokens. Add migration column, populate in processor.ts line 690.
  - Veredicto: /Users/pedropoleza/SPARK APPS/AI platform/src/lib/account-assistant/processor.ts:625-627 — coherence re-run calls `result.prompt_tokens += rerun.prompt_tokens; result.completion_tokens += rerun.completion_tokens; result.cached_tokens += rerun.cached_tokens;` but omits `result.cache_creation_tokens += rerun.cache_creation_tokens ?? 0;` even though line 552 states this re-run should have "tokens do re-run entrarem na cobrança". Line 690 then calls `trackAndCharge({...cacheCreationTokens: result.cache_creation_tokens ?? 0,...})` which only includes initial run's cache tokens, missing coherence re-run's premium cache_creation_tokens. Anti-repeat re-run (lines 770-785) also has same missing accumulation BUT runs AFTER billing (intentional per lines 759-761 comment: "DEPOIS do billing...não são cobrados"). Bug impact: Claude Sonnet 4.6 cache_write costs $3.75/1M vs fresh input $3.00/1M — 25% premium silently unbilled when coherence gate triggers re-runs.


---

## SparkBot — proatividade & crons

The SparkBot proactivity system orchestrates rule-based automated messaging to sales reps via a pg_cron job (`sparkbot-proactive`) running every 30 seconds. It handles three categories: scheduled rules (e.g., "Morning briefing" at 08:00), reactive polling rules (e.g., "post_meeting" after appointments), and event-driven triggers from webhooks (task reminders, tag additions). All dispatch flows through a unified `dispatchRule()` function that gates execution via atomic cooldown claims, silence tracking to prevent WhatsApp bans, daily proactive limits, quiet hours, and billing. Reminders and bulk messages use `assistant_scheduled_tasks` for delivery orchestration.

### Funcionalidades

**Cron orchestration & advisory locks — 9/10**
- ✅ Migration 00053 implements dual guards: pg_try_advisory_xact_lock(8675309) prevents double-execution during backlog spikes; WHERE EXISTS triplo checks (scheduled_tasks + rules enabled + bulk_message_recipients) avoid empty auto-DDoS calls that plagued pre-2026-05-05. Lock is xact-scoped (released per transaction). Heartbeat upfront in bulk-runner tracks liveness (H7/F16 2026-05-16).
- ⚠️ No graceful degradation if lock acquisition fails — code assumes lock always succeeds (fail-open). If pg_cron backend becomes saturated, no circuit breaker; requests queue indefinitely. Webhook rate limiting is IP-based without per-location cardinality checks (F20 mitigation added but still coarse). No explicit telemetry on lock contention or failed WHERE EXISTS checks.
- 🔧 Add counter metrics for lock acquisition latency and contention. Implement exponential backoff in cron dispatch if lock wait time exceeds threshold. Add cardinality anomaly detection per location (F20 already has this but only logs). Consider WAL-based queue (pg_cron → Inngest alternative) for higher throughput if needed.

**Rule dispatch & confirmation gating — 8/10**
- ✅ Dispatcher (615 lines) is comprehensive: mode='simulated' for testing injects into agent_test_messages; mode='real' sends via WhatsApp/SMS. Atomic slot claiming via RPC try_claim_dispatch_slot prevents duplicate sends for same (rep, rule, target). Cooldown, quiet_hours, and silence gates are evaluated before LLM call (saves tokens on skip). H8 confirmation gating applies uniformly across all tools.
- ⚠️ Cold silence state on rep lookup error defaults to canSend=true (fail-open) — rep orphans (FK CASCADE delete) could still receive proactives. Error handling in buildSystemPrompt KB load is silent catch (non-fatal) but swallows real failures without signal. LLM fallback chain (Sonnet→Haiku→GPT-4) not tested under Pedro's STRICT_CLAUDE_ONLY=1 prod flag.
- 🔧 Change fail-open in loadSilenceDecision to fail-closed for orphan reps (already detects PGRST116). Add structured logging of KB load failures with severity tagged. Test fallback under STRICT_CLAUDE_ONLY flag to ensure no OpenAI leakage.

**Silence gate & anti-spam tracking — 8/10**
- ✅ 3-level escalation (0=ok, 1→2=soft warn, 2→3=hard warn, 3+=pause) is sensible. Distinction between 'nudge' (rule-initiated, counts) and 'requested' (rep-initiated reminder, exempt from counter) prevents false-positive pauses on reminders rep created. Reset on ANY inbound (whatsapp + web) is implemented (webhook-handler.ts line ~376). F49 ensures warnings prepended only once per escalation level via proactive_warned_at marker.
- ⚠️ Counter increments happen in recordProactiveSent() which is called AFTER send attempt — if send fails silently, counter still increments, bloating false counts. Silence pause is silent by design (anti-spam) but admin_signals only emits on transition (shouldSetPaused=true), risking observer blind spots if pause persists across ticks. No per-rule silence override (some rules like 'deal_won' might warrant skipping the gate).
- 🔧 Decouple counter increment from delivery attempt: increment on gate-pass, decrement only on confirmed receipt or explicit inbound reply. Add optional per-rule override_silence_gate flag for celebration rules. Add scheduled signal refresh (daily) if rep remains paused >24h without inbound.

**Task reminder scheduling (GHL webhooks) — 8/10**
- ✅ Event-driven: task-reminders.ts hooks TASKCREATE/UPDATE webhooks, schedules reminder due − lead_min minutes via assistant_scheduled_tasks. Idempotent: cancelPending() before reagendanding prevents duplicate reminders on task updates. Validates rep is SparkBot-active (terms_accepted + last_inbound + not_rejected). Filters out tasks without due dates upfront. Kind='nudge' respects silence-gate anti-spam.
- ⚠️ Task finder uses JSONB containment filter `@>` which is CPU-intensive on large rep_identities table (no partial index). Migration backfill (scripts/backfill-task-reminders.ts) not mentioned in CLAUDE.md — unclear if historical tasks were seeded or 'gap starts at cutover' is accepted. No explicit handling of task deletion race (task deleted between webhook and reminder fire — fails silently).
- 🔧 Add partial index on ghl_users JSONB for faster containment queries. Add retry logic with exponential backoff for task-not-found errors. Log task deletion gaps explicitly (analytics for product understanding).

**Reactive polling (post_meeting, others) — 6/10**
- ✅ post_meeting polling (processPostMeetingPolling, lines 449–572) is fully implemented: queries GHL /calendars/events with ±1h window, filters endTime in [windowStart, windowEnd], skips cancelled/noshow/invalid statuses. Grace period (30min) covers cron delays or Vercel restarts. Multi-location support iterates rep.ghl_users. Context passed to dispatcher includes appointment_id, title, duration — rich enough for coherent briefing.
- ⚠️ Other 7 reactive rules (Opportunity parada, Task vencendo, Tarefa atrasada, Inbound não respondida, Lead esfriando, Novo lead, No-show) are declared in system-rules.ts but ONLY post_meeting has polling implementation. Others hit processReactivePolling() which logs 'ainda não implementado' (line 430) and silently returns {fired:0, skipped:0}. This silences 7 stubbed rules but DOES NOT disable them in DB — admin and rep might assume rules are active when they're dead code.
- 🔧 URGENT: Either (1) implement the 7 polling rules, or (2) explicitly disable them in DB seed/migrations and add a UI note 'Coming soon'. Current state is a silent trap. Add feature flags (REACTIVE_RULE_OPPORTUNITY_STALE_ENABLED, etc.) gating each rule separately OR batch-disable all non-post_meeting via migration 'enabled=false' with admin notification.

**Event-driven triggers (task/tag/stage) — 7/10**
- ✅ event-router.ts + reactive-trigger.ts (F27.D) implement new event-driven system: GHL webhooks for TASKCREATE, TASKUPDATE, CONTACTTAGUPDATE, OPPORTUNITYSTAGEUPDATE trigger bot action without polling. Reactive-trigger matches targeting_rules (tag=X, stage=Y, custom_field) and enqueues synthetic message_queue entries. Idempotence via execution_log (24h window, same agent+contact+event_key). Non-fatal: gated by PROACTIVE_EVENTS_ENABLED (default OFF, production-safe).
- ⚠️ PROACTIVE_EVENTS_ENABLED is OFF by default and not documented in .env.example or admin UI — activation requires manual env var set + deploy. No health check confirming events are firing (webhook capture via inbound_webhook_samples is diagnostic-only, not operational). reactive-trigger's ruleMatchesTrigger() uses OR logic ('any rule matches') which differs from lead_facing targeting (AND logic) — undocumented semantic gap. Custom_field trigger not yet implemented in reactive-trigger (stage/tag only; needs ContactUpdate diff tracking).
- 🔧 Add admin UI toggle for PROACTIVE_EVENTS_ENABLED (currently env-only). Implement event delivery metrics (events_fired per day/type). Document semantic difference between reactive triggers (OR) and lead-facing targeting (AND) with warnings. Implement custom_field reactive trigger (requires ContactUpdate with field diff logic).

**Bulk message dispatch (drip, variation, quiet hours) — 8/10**
- ✅ bulk-message-runner.ts (609 lines) handles 100+ contact drips with per-recipient scheduling. Respects respect_quiet_hours + working_hours (F32 moved to isInBlockedHours). Priority queue (F4.1) orders by job priority DESC + scheduled_at ASC. Opt-out pre-check batches by location (Etapa 4.8). F58 dedup catches duplicate recipients in batch (Soraia case 2026-06-04). Message variation via Haiku (light/medium). Atomic claim prevents race on 'sending' status.
- ⚠️ MAX_PER_TICK=5 is arbitrary (no adaptive backpressure when queue depth > threshold). variation_mode='light|medium' are underdocumented — API response doesn't explain semantic difference. Quiet hours check happens POST-claim — inefficient (marks 'sending' then reverts to 'pending', consuming update quota). Contact opt-out check fails-open if filterOutOptOutContacts() errors — missing contacts could be sent anyway. Heartbeat update (line 88–103) happens early but tick-level exceptions don't decrement counter (error tracking leaks into next tick).
- 🔧 Add per-job adaptive MAX_PER_TICK based on queue depth. Document variation modes with examples. Move quiet hours check PRE-claim. Fail-closed on opt-out errors (skip recipient if check fails). Decouple heartbeat success from tick error — record success/failure independently.

**Scheduled reminders (user-created + recurring) — 8/10**
- ✅ reminder-runner.ts (602 lines) unifies reminders and outbound-to-contact messages. Atomic claim ('pending'→'running'), silence-gate check (kind='requested' or 'nudge'), and advancing logic (recurring: next_run_at via cron; one-shot: completed). F58 dedup catches duplicate task GHL → 7× ghl_task_reminders. Delivery to web UI via sparkbot_messages (channel='system') AND WhatsApp via deliverProactiveMessage(). outbound_to_contact includes pre-send assignment switch (ensureContactAssignedTo) pra multi-WhatsApp accounts (fix 2026-05-06).
- ⚠️ Recurring reminder cron calculation (computeNextRun) is naive minute-by-minute iteration (max 100 days) — inefficient. Test session delivery branch (lines 154–164) checks session existence but returns silently on not-found — admin could miss missing sessions. Outbound-to-contact fallback SMS on WhatsApp unavailability (lines 425–442) succeeds silently — user expects WhatsApp delivery but got SMS without notification. Task assignment switch pre-send has no rollback if send fails (could leave contact misassigned).
- 🔧 Implement cron library (cron-parser npm) instead of brute-force iteration. Log/signal when test session not found. Add channel confirmation notification to user (e.g., 'Msg sent via SMS fallback'). Add assignment rollback on send failure or explicit undo-tool for rep.

**Delivery status polling (WhatsApp/Stevo) — 7/10**
- ✅ delivery-status-poller.ts (232 lines) polls sparkbot_messages status every cron tick, queries Stevo API for delivery confirmation on pending messages. Auto-fallback: messages still pending >3600s get marked 'fallback_to_web' (inserted into web UI for manual dispatch). Signal-on-failure: failed deliveries emit admin_signals (visibility, fix for Silent failure case 2026-05-06). Failure analysis: categorizes errors (invalid_phone, network, etc.) for debugging.
- ⚠️ Stevo API unavailability causes silent downgrades (pending→fallback_to_web) — no alert to admin that WhatsApp is down. Polling window (3600s hardcoded) is long — messages stuck in 'pending' state are invisible for an hour. No retry backoff for transient Stevo failures (simple requeue). Fallback_to_web messages are audit trail only (rep doesn't see proactive in web UI if they missed it earlier).
- 🔧 Add circuit breaker on Stevo (3 failures → emit critical signal). Reduce pending timeout to 300s. Implement exponential backoff for retries (1m, 5m, 30m). Add explicit UI notification when proactive falls back to web (rep sees 'Message not sent via WhatsApp, check web UI').

**F58 duplicate fire protection — 8/10**
- ✅ Two-layer dedup: (1) in-turn (run-sparkbot-turn.ts) prevents identical tool calls within same LLM turn via hashArgs + normalizeForRepeat; (2) batch (reminder-runner.ts lines 76–106) catches duplicate scheduled_tasks at tick boundary (Soraia case 2026-06-04 where GHL bug created 7× task_reminders). Dedup uses normalized text (case-insensitive, trimmed) to catch near-duplicates (e.g., leading/trailing spaces).
- ⚠️ In-turn dedup only applies to WRITE tools (create_*, schedule_*) — READ tools aren't protected (design assumption: reads are idempotent). Batch dedup marks duplicates 'cancelled' (retroactive) — already-sent duplicates to first batch item won't be detected (race: if 1 reminder fired before batch tick, its sibling still enqueued). Duplicates from DIFFERENT cron ticks (tick N fires + tick N+1 retries) have no cross-tick dedup — relies on cooldown/claim logic instead.
- 🔧 Document assumption that all READ tools are idempotent. Add pre-insertion dedup check in fireOne() (before marking 'running') to catch same-content recalls from prior ticks. Log duplicate detection with diagnostic context (upstream cause: GHL bug, LLM repeat, etc.).

**Scheduled rules (morning briefing, others) — 6/10**
- ✅ Cron evaluator (cron-evaluator.ts) correctly parses 5-field POSIX cron with range/list/OR logic for dom vs dow. computeNextRun() iterates minute-by-minute (pragmatic). Morning briefing is fully implemented: loads daily context (appointments + hot opps + tasks), generates prompt, dispatches via dispatchRule(mode='real'). Opt-out check via daily_briefing_enabled flag (tool set_daily_briefing).
- ⚠️ Of 4 scheduled rules in system-rules.ts (Morning, End-of-day, Weekly, Pipeline), ONLY Morning has implementation. Other 3 route to 'skipped_disabled' status with no dispatch attempt (line 189–197). They're marked enabled=true in system-rules.ts seed but NON-FUNCTIONAL in runtime, creating admin confusion ('why isn't my end-of-day firing?'). No deprecation warning or UI note. End-of-day hardcoded to 18:00 UTC (no rep timezone conversion at schedule time) — works correctly at runtime (route-level converts) but confuses schema.
- 🔧 Either implement the 3 rules (needs prompt templates) or disable in seed with comment 'Scheduled for Q3'. Add feature flags (SCHEDULED_RULE_END_OF_DAY_ENABLED, etc.). Add UI widget showing rule implementation status (Live, Planned, Deprecated).

**Billing & cost tracking — 7/10**
- ✅ Dispatcher calls trackAndCharge() post-dispatch (lines 569–594) with model, prompt/completion/cache tokens, ai_model_used. Integrates with billing cap (daily_proactive_limit checked line 320+). Cost calculation via pricing.ts (calculateCost). Audit trail: assistant_alert_state records tokens_used + cost_usd per dispatch. Cache tokens properly tracked (claude models optimize via prompt caching).
- ⚠️ trackAndCharge() called even on 'simulated' dispatches (test messages shouldn't bill) — fix applied (billing only on mode='real' 2026-05-XX) but not verifiable from this audit scope. daily_proactive_limit is global per rep (not per-agent) — multi-agent orgs can't set per-agent quotas. Cost display in UI (if exists) not checked. Cache billing edge cases: if cache_creation_tokens are 0 but cache is used, no miscount; but if partial cache hit, tracking correctness depends on LLM response accuracy (no validation).
- 🔧 Confirm trackAndCharge() is never called on simulated dispatches (add test). Per-agent proactive limits (move limit from agent_configs.daily_proactive_limit to dynamic lookup). Add cost breakdown in admin_signals when limit reached. Validate LLM cache token counts in billing test suite.

### Structural issues
- **[HIGH] 7 Reactive polling rules are declared but not implemented** — system-rules.ts defines 14 rules: post_meeting (DONE), Opportunity parada, Task vencendo, Tarefa atrasada, Inbound não respondida, Lead esfriando, Deal fechado, Novo lead (7 NOT DONE). These appear in the system_rules seed and would be created in DB as enabled=true, but processReactivePolling() in sparkbot-proactive/route.ts only handles post_meeting. Other 7 events route to 'ainda não implementado' log (line 430) and silently return {fired:0, skipped:0}. Admin and reps see rules as active (enabled in DB) but they never fire, creating expectations gap. (src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/system-rules.ts (rules 4-10), src/app/api/cron/sparkbot-proactive/route.ts (lines 203-206, 422-431))
- **[HIGH] 3 Scheduled rules (end-of-day, weekly, pipeline) declared but not implemented** — Similar to reactive rules: 4 scheduled rules in system-rules.ts, but only 'Resumo matinal' has full implementation (loadDailyContext + buildDailyBriefingPrompt). Other 3 (end-of-day, weekly, pipeline) bypass dispatch and route to skipped_disabled (lines 186–198). These are created in DB as enabled=true but won't fire. No admin UI indicates 'Coming Soon' or deprecation status. (src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/system-rules.ts (rules 11-14), src/app/api/cron/sparkbot-proactive/route.ts (lines 132-143, 186-198))
- **[MEDIUM] Event-driven triggers require manual env var activation (PROACTIVE_EVENTS_ENABLED)** — Task reminders, tag triggers, and stage triggers are gated by PROACTIVE_EVENTS_ENABLED (default OFF). The flag is documented in code but not in .env.example, runbook, or admin UI. Production activation requires DevOps to set env var + redeploy. No telemetry confirms events are being routed (only webhook_samples log diagnostically). If flag is accidentally set to OFF in prod, system silently drops TASKCREATE/CONTACTTAGUPDATE/OPPORTUNITYSTAGEUPDATE webhooks with no alert. (src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/event-router.ts (line 26), src/app/api/webhooks/inbound-message/route.ts (line 199))
- **[LOW] Recurring cron calculation uses brute-force minute iteration** — reminder-runner.ts computeNextRun() (lines 590–602) iterates minute-by-minute up to 31 days to find next cron match. For complex cron expressions or high-frequency checks, this is CPU-inefficient. No issue at current scale (max ~50 reminders/cron tick) but will scale poorly if reminders grow 10× or cron interval shrinks. (src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/reminder-runner.ts (lines 590–602))
- **[MEDIUM] Silence gate fails open (orphan reps could receive proactives)** — loadSilenceDecision() when rep_identity fetch errors (non-PGRST116 errors), defaults to canSend=true (fail-open, lines 165–171). If rep is deleted (FK CASCADE) but has stale ghl_users[] cache entry, proactive could attempt send. PGRST116 (no rows) is caught and fails-closed, but transient DB errors (timeout, connection pool exhausted) are fail-open. This is partially mitigated by delivery-status-poller (failed sends trigger signal), but direct channel sends (WhatsApp) could cause ban risk if many false positives stack. (src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/silence-gate.ts (lines 144–178))
- **[MEDIUM] outbound_to_contact WhatsApp fallback to SMS is silent** — reminder-runner.ts lines 425–442: if WhatsApp API unavailable, silently falls back to SMS without user notification. Rep scheduled message to contact expecting WhatsApp (encryption, user experience) but receives SMS instead without visibility. Contact may see SMS as different sender. Audit trail records success but actual channel differs from intent. (src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/reminder-runner.ts (lines 425–442), src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/quiet-hours.ts)
- **[LOW] Daily proactive limit is global per rep (not per-agent)** — dispatcher.ts lines 320–341 check daily_proactive_limit from agent_configs, but limit is keyed per rep (not per-agent). Multi-agent orgs with multiple sales agents sending proactives to same rep would share a single quota bucket. Quota exhaustion for one agent blocks other agents' proactives. Design unclear — should be per-rep (total proactives) or per-agent (agent-specific quota). (src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/dispatcher.ts (lines 314–341))
- **[LOW] Cross-tick duplicate detection missing (relies on cooldown + claim atomicity)** — F58 dedup protects against in-turn repeats (same LLM call) and batch repeats (same cron tick). But duplicate reminders from different cron ticks (e.g., tick N fires, tick N+1 retries due to network hiccup) have no explicit dedup — rely on cooldown (rep_id, rule_id, target_id UNIQUE). If cooldown expires between ticks, same reminder could fire twice. Acceptable for current design (cooldown is guardrail) but worth documenting. (src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/reminder-runner.ts (lines 76–106), src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/dispatcher.ts (lines 144–180))
- **[MEDIUM] No circuit breaker for Stevo WhatsApp API** — delivery-status-poller.ts queries Stevo for delivery status every cron tick. If Stevo is down, messages marked pending→fallback_to_web after 3600s hardcoded timeout. No exponential backoff (simple requeue). No alert to admin that WhatsApp delivery is degraded. Repeated failures accumulate in sparkbot_messages.metadata (no cleanup of failed attempts). If Stevo outage lasts >1h, entire cohort of pending messages downgrades silently. (src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/delivery-status-poller.ts (lines ~160–200))

### Production blockers
- **[PARTIAL/MEDIUM] 10 of 14 system rules are non-functional (dead code in production)** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: 7 reactive polling rules (opp_stale, task_overdue, lead_cooling, etc.) and 3 scheduled rules (end_of_day, weekly, pipeline) are seeded as enabled=true but have no runtime implementation. Code paths log 'ainda não implementado' and skip. Admins enable rules via UI (if available), reps see them listed as active, but they never fire. Creates expectation gap and silent failures. CLAUDE.md explicitly states '3 were stub but were enabled=true' (the issue Pedro flagged 2026-05-05) but doesn't confirm they're now disabled.
  - Fix: URGENT: Either (1) implement all 9 rules before go-live (needs prompt templates + polling logic, ~2-3 days), OR (2) explicitly disable them in DB seed with migration comment, add UI widget showing 'Coming soon', and update CLAUDE.md. Recommend (2) for ship velocity: declare roadmap item 'Scheduled Rules Phase 2', ship 'post_meeting' + 'morning_briefing' only.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/system-rules.ts:22-244 — 14 system rules defined in code (10 reactive + 4 scheduled). src/app/api/cron/sparkbot-proactive/route.ts:425-431 — only post_meeting reactive rule implemented; others return {fired:0, skipped:0}. Lines 133-185 — only "Resumo matinal" scheduled rule implemented. Lines 186-198 — other scheduled rules get status='skipped_disabled'. Git commit 30432f2 (2026-05-27): seedSystemRules() function was orphaned and never called (verified by grep), then removed from codebase. src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/seed.ts existed but was never invoked, so the 14 rules never seeded into database with enabled=true. Therefore: (a) Rules don't exist in production DB; (b) If they did, 12 of 14 would be non-functional (9 reactive + 3 scheduled lack implementation), not 10; (c) CLAUDE.md claim "Disabled em 2026-05-05" has no supporting UPDATE statement in migrations or code.
- **[CONFIRMED/MEDIUM] PROACTIVE_EVENTS_ENABLED must be manually activated (no admin UI, no fallback)** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Task reminders, tag triggers, and stage triggers require PROACTIVE_EVENTS_ENABLED=1 env var (default OFF). Flag is undocumented in .env.example or runbook. If not explicitly set during prod cutover, these entire features (TASKCREATE/TASKUPDATE webhook routing) silently don't work. No telemetry confirms activation. If accidentally toggled OFF in prod, system drops webhooks with no alert.
  - Fix: Add PROACTIVE_EVENTS_ENABLED toggle to admin UI (settings page). Add post-startup diagnostic that logs 'Event routing: ON/OFF' with Sentry tag. Add monitoring alert if zero events routed in 1h (potential misconfiguration). Update .env.example and deployment runbook.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/event-router.ts:26 (gate function) + src/app/api/webhooks/inbound-message/route.ts:199-206 (gate checks before routeProactiveEvent) + .env.example:1-76 (documents 3 other OUTREACH/BULK/RECURRING runners but NOT PROACTIVE_EVENTS_ENABLED) + docs/RUNBOOK.md:98-107 (env rotation table omits PROACTIVE_EVENTS_ENABLED) + git commit ce4491e (empty commit message "liga PROACTIVE_EVENTS_ENABLED" — ativação via Vercel UI não git) + /src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/event-router.ts:89-90 (logs payload receipt but no telemetry on gate state)
- **[CONFIRMED/MEDIUM] Silence gate can fail-open on transient DB errors** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: loadSilenceDecision() defaults to canSend=true on errors other than PGRST116 (no rows). Transient DB timeouts, connection pool exhaustion, or network blips would allow proactive sends to reps whose state is unknown. Risk: if Supabase has brief outage, system sends many proactives simultaneously (no gate), potentially triggering WhatsApp ban. Mitigated by delivery-status-poller (failed sends surface as signals) but direct Stevo sends bypass polling.
  - Fix: Change fail-mode to fail-closed: if any DB error (except PGRST116), assume rep is paused (canSend=false, reason='unknown_state'). Add counter metric 'silence_gate_errors' to track how often this triggers (should be rare). Log with severity=high for monitoring.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/silence-gate.ts:165-171 — loadSilenceDecision() explicitly returns canSend=true on any error other than PGRST116 (no rows). Line 166-170 comment states "Erro transient (network, timeout, etc.) — fail-open com warn" and returns {canSend: true, warningPrefix: null, nextCounter: 1, markWarned: false}. The return type is identical to an "active rep" state, making the gate undetectable on transient DB errors. Called from dispatcher.ts:272-273 and reminder-runner.ts:177 before message delivery to WhatsApp.
- **[REFUTED/LOW] Daily proactive limit could be exhausted by one agent, blocking others** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: daily_proactive_limit is per-rep global (not per-agent). In multi-agent setup, if Sales Agent A fires 3 proactives/min, Cap (50/day) is consumed by lunchtime. Other agents (Recruitment, Custom) targeting same rep get skipped. Acceptable if design intent is 'rep receives max 50 total' but problematic if intent is 'each agent max 50'.
  - Fix: Clarify design intent with Pedro. If per-agent: migrate limit from agent_configs to per-agent setting. If global: document in UI that limit applies to total proactives (sum of all agents). Add admin visibility: show 'Proactive usage today: X/Y' per-agent.
  - Veredicto: The claim conflates two fundamentally separate systems and misunderstands the architecture:

1. ONLY SparkBot (account_assistant type) uses the proactive rules system and daily_proactive_limit — Sales and Recruitment agents are lead-facing agents that operate on the message_queue, NOT proactive rules. They have zero interaction with the daily_proactive_limit or assistant_alert_state table.

2. UNIQUE constraint enforces exactly ONE account_assistant per location (migration 00082: CREATE UNIQUE INDEX agents_location_type_noncustom_uniq ON agents(location_id, type) WHERE type <> 'custom_agent') — account_assistant is a single agent type, not a custom_agent, so only one can exist per location.
