## GHL UI — loader injection & gates de visibilidade (PEDIDO ESPECIFICO DO PEDRO)

O subsistema injecta dois módulos JavaScript independentes na UI do Spark Leads via Custom JS no nível da agência: (1) IIFE Sparkbot — carrega painel de chat no header com widget flutuante, autenticado via /api/sparkbot/check-admin que valida se user é admin; (2) IIFE Agent Controls (GU-7) — mostra pill de liga/desliga de agentes lead-facing na tela de contato via /api/agents/ui-auth que valida se user é location-member. Ambos têm polling, estado compartilhado, feedback por mensagem. O loader é servido dinamicamente por /embed/sparkbot/loader/route.ts e atua como orquestrador.

### Funcionalidades

**SparkBot Widget Injection & Header Placement — 7/10**
- ✅ Detecta locationId, userId, companyId robustamente com fallbacks (localStorage JWT parsing, window state, meta tags). Injeção resiliente — tenta header container ideal, fallback para flutuante. Watcher re-injeta a cada 3s se GHL re-render matar o botão. IIFE reentrância — evita double-setup com flag __sparkbotInjected.
- ⚠️ NÃO VALIDA que a location tem SparkBot (account_assistant agent ativo) — loader injecta botão em QUALQUER location da agência onde o user é admin, mesmo que a location não tenha comprado/instalado o Spark AI. Isso vaza UI em locations alheias (multi-tenant violation).
- 🔧 Adicionar gate no check-admin: após validar admin, query agents table — WHERE location_id=? AND type='account_assistant' AND status='active'. Se não achar, retornar {ok:false, reason:'sparkbot_not_installed'}. O loader silencia e não injecta nada se receber esse motivo.

**Admin Authentication via /api/sparkbot/check-admin — 8/10**
- ✅ Multi-source validation (Firebase JWKS RS256 verify, allowlist env, GHL API). Firebase path é security-reviewed (C3 2026-04-29, jose.jwtVerify). Fallback chain robusta: idToken failed → allowlist → GHL API. Emite JWT temp 1h. Handles location provision (upsertLocation) + rep provision (identifyRepByGhlUser).
- ⚠️ GATE CRÍTICO AUSENTE: NÃO valida que a location é um 'hub' (tem account_assistant ativo). check-admin retorna {ok:true} pra qualquer admin de QUALQUER location — leak de widget pra locations que não contrataram SparkBot.
- 🔧 Linha ~158, após isAdmin validado: async query agents WHERE location_id=locationId AND type='account_assistant' AND status='active'. Se empty, retornar {ok:false, reason:'sparkbot_not_provisioned_in_location', status:403}. Compatível com loader — detecta e silencia.

**Agent Controls Pill (GU-7) & Contact Status — 8/10**
- ✅ Auth bem separado de SparkBot — /api/agents/ui-auth valida qualquer location-user (não só admin), permite lead handlers operar. contact-agents retorna ALL agentes lead-facing da location + estado (driving/paused/idle) por contato via conversation_state. Seletor único (acActivateAgent) pausa os outros — evita conflito N agentes → 1 contato. Feedback 👍/👎 com anti-eco (acNormText).
- ⚠️ Só aparece se hasAnyAgent=true (pill hidden quando contact-agents retorna hasAnyAgent:false). Isso é CORRETO — não mostra controle se não há agentes lead-facing. MAS há edge case: se location tem account_assistant (SparkBot hub) mas ZERO agentes lead-facing (sales/recruitment/custom), pill fica escondido, OK. Risco: nenhum.
- 🔧 Nenhum — agent-controls é corretamente gated por presença de LEAD_FACING_TYPES (sales_agent, recruitment_agent, custom_agent).

**Location-Agent Resolution (resolveAgentForContact) — 9/10**
- ✅ Lógica clara: 1) agente com conversation_state pro contato (já engajando), 2) se vários lead-facing e nenhum engajou, pega primeiro (MVP). 3) Retorna null se ZERO agentes lead-facing. Status check: ativa=true AND type in LEAD_FACING_TYPES. Integrado em contact-pause, contact-activate, contact-status.
- ⚠️ Nenhum — resolve agent correctly.
- 🔧 Nenhum.

**Pause/Activate State Persistence (conversation_state) — 8/10**
- ✅ UPDATE-then-INSERT pattern (preserva conversation_id). contact-pause seta ai_paused_at=now (fonte de verdade). contact-activate pausa os outros em transaction-like. Metadata: ai_paused_reason='manual_ui:user_...' ou 'manual_ui:switch:...' — auditável. Respeita em queue-processor (F52 auto-pause-on-human + GU-6 driving state).
- ⚠️ Sem validação de idempotência no endpoint — chamada dupla (retry de rede) cria 2 rows ou sobrescreve timestamp. Improvável em prática (UPDATE usa PK), mas não defensivo.
- 🔧 Adicionar request ID de idempotência (header X-Idempotency-Key) — respeitar no UPDATE/INSERT, retornar 200 se duplicate.

**Multi-Tenant Isolation (Bearer JWT) — 8/10**
- ✅ JWT via verifySparkbotWebToken contém location_id + company_id — endpoints validam igualdade (token.location_id vs query param). contact-agents, contact-status, contact-pause, contact-activate ALL validam. GHLClient instanciado com token.company_id, evita escalar privilégio entre companies.
- ⚠️ contactId vem do query/body (client-provided) — falta validação que contactId é REALMENTE de token.location_id. Atacante poderia passar outro contactId da mesma company e lerlo (read oracle). Endpoints confiam apenas no location_id do token.
- 🔧 Antes de operar no contactId, query GHL /contacts/{id} ou cache — confirmar contact.locationId === token.location_id. Fail-open se GHL falhar (preserve UX).

**SparkBot Loader Caching & Hotfix Speed — 8/10**
- ✅ Cache-Control: no-cache, must-revalidate — força revalidação 304 a cada page-load, sem overhead. Placeholders __VAR__ substituídos server-side (APP_URL, POLL_MS, HEARTBEAT_MS) — permite config dinâmica. IIFE único em JS — não quebra com postscribe GHL (fetch+Function pattern).
- ⚠️ no-cache deixa browser ainda fazer request desnecessário — se loader tiver bug, cliente vê delay de latência (cacheável 5min seria melhor). Trade-off intencional (hotfix vs latência) — documentado bem.
- 🔧 Opcional: mudar pra Cache-Control: max-age=300 (5min) + ETag — melhor perf, ainda permite hotfix via header. Agora: sem mudança recomendada.

**JavaScript Bundle Security (Sandbox, CORS) — 7/10**
- ✅ Sandbox attribute no iframe: allow-scripts, allow-same-origin, allow-forms, allow-popups, allow-modals — isolado de contexto de página. CORS headers: Access-Control-Allow-Origin: * (broad, aceitável pra loader público). Custom JS snippet do Pedro é trusted (auto-injetado via Agency Settings da Spark Leads).
- ⚠️ IIFE não é minificado/uglified — code expostos no source (não é secret, mas piracy/MITM attack surface). Dependência em localStorage — localStorage.refreshedToken pode ser manipulado por XSS em Spark Leads (fora do escopo desse audit, mas upstream risk).
- 🔧 Minify o LOADER_SOURCE + AGENT_CONTROLS_SOURCE antes de retornar (webpack/terser). CSP header — restringir inline scripts na Spark Leads top-level.

### Structural issues
- **[CRITICAL] CRITICAL: No Hub Validation in SparkBot Loader Injection** — O check-admin endpoint NUNCA valida que a locationId tem um agente account_assistant ativo. Retorna {ok:true} pra qualquer admin de QUALQUER location sob a agência. O loader JS então injecta botão SparkBot + painel de chat em locations que NÃO têm o app instalado. Isso viola isolamento multi-tenant: um admin de Location B vê botão SparkBot mesmo que Location B não pagou/contratou o produto. Comparar com isSparkbotHub no webhook (inbound-message/route.ts:37) que JÁ faz essa validação — padrão existe no código, só não foi aplicado aqui. ATACANTE INTERNO: se um malicious agency owner quer vazar UI a location rival, pode usar Custom JS access pra injectar loader sem gate. CLIENTE: se agência não renovar contrato pra Location B, Location B ainda vê widget (vaza beta features). (/src/app/api/sparkbot/check-admin/route.ts (linha ~158), /src/app/embed/sparkbot/loader/route.ts (linhas ~210-225))
- **[HIGH] Multi-Tenant Contact ID Validation Gap** — Todos os endpoints recebem contactId do query/body (client-provided) mas validam APENAS que token.location_id === header-location. Falta validação que contactId é REALMENTE da location de token. Atacante com token válido de Location A poderia passar contactId de Location B da mesma company_id e potencialmente ler/mutar conversation_state. Endpoints enfileiram o contactId direto em queries Supabase sem confirmar RLS. Falha potencial de authorization: legit user consegue ACL gate (Firebase JWKS), mas ACL não cobre o recurso específico. (/src/app/api/agents/contact-status/route.ts (linha 36), /src/app/api/agents/contact-activate/route.ts (linha 41), /src/app/api/agents/contact-pause/route.ts (linha 39), /src/app/api/agents/contact-agents/route.ts (linha 43))
- **[LOW] Dead Code: Pedro 2026-05-04 Onboarding Removal Partially Documented** — Código comentado (longblock) explica que removeu auto-accept terms e seedWebOnboardingMessage. Comentário é claro, mas código-morto continua — não há código corresponde ao comentário (as linhas foram deletadas). OK pra compreensão, mas não é dead-code cleanup standard (comentário sem código). Sugestão: se removeu, elimina comentário; se quer preservar história, move pra DECISIONS.md. (/src/app/api/sparkbot/check-admin/route.ts (linhas 169-178))
- **[MEDIUM] No Idempotency Check in Pause/Activate Endpoints** — Ambos endpoints pra UPDATE conversation_state usam padrão UPDATE-then-INSERT (preserva conversation_id), mas não rastreia X-Idempotency-Key. Retry de rede (cliente repete POST) pode criar múltiplas rows ou sobrescrever timestamp. UPDATE com PK (agent_id, contact_id) deverá idempotente em realidade, mas falta defesa explícita. Se cliente fizer 2 calls mesmo (cliente bug), pode registrar timestamp errado. (/src/app/api/agents/contact-pause/route.ts (linhas 78-93), /src/app/api/agents/contact-activate/route.ts (linhas 70-89))
- **[LOW] Agent Controls Feedback: Anti-Echo Heuristic May Miss Edge Cases** — Feedback 👍/👎 usa anti-eco: normaliza bolha (lower, remove acentos) e casa com aiTexts. Filtro: só marca 'match' se AI text tamanho ≥60% da bolha (anti falso-positivo). Heurística é razoável, mas pode falhar se: (a) app de chat do Spark Leads muda estrutura DOM (margin-left detection quebra), (b) msg da IA é expandida com contexto (timestamp, status), ratio cai abaixo 60%. Risco baixo (graceful degrade — feedback não anexa se unsure), mas pode haver msgs do agente sem feedback bar quando deveria ter. (/src/app/embed/sparkbot/loader/route.ts (linhas 1137-1190, acNormText, acScanBubbles))

### Production blockers
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] BLOCKER: SparkBot Widget Leaks to Unlicensed Locations** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: check-admin validates admin-status but NOT that location has active account_assistant agent. Loader injects SparkBot button in ALL locations of agency where user is admin. Locations that didn't purchase SparkBot still see widget → violates SaaS multi-tenant contract. Agency could see billing disputes ('why was I charged?'), customers of other agencies see competing UI (confusion). Database has isSparkbotHub() pattern (webhook-handler.ts:37) that DOES validate — pattern exists, just not applied here.
  - Fix: In /api/sparkbot/check-admin (line ~158, after isAdmin confirmed), add: `const hasSparkbot = await supabase.from('agents').select('id').eq('location_id', locationId).eq('type', 'account_assistant').eq('status', 'active').maybeSingle(); if (!hasSparkbot.data) return json({ok:false, reason:'sparkbot_not_provisioned_in_location'}, {status:403});` Loader detects reason !== 'not_provisioned' and silences injection.
  - Veredicto: /src/app/api/sparkbot/check-admin/route.ts:39-203 — endpoint validates admin status (lines 78-158) and issues JWT (lines 181-187) but has NO check for active account_assistant agent at location. identifyRepByGhlUser() called at line 164 doesn't validate agent existence either. /src/app/embed/sparkbot/loader/route.ts:334-375 — injectFab() injects SparkBot button into UI after check-admin succeeds, no location-level agent validation. /src/app/api/webhooks/inbound-message/route.ts:37-59 — isSparkbotHub() function EXISTS and correctly queries for active account_assistant agent (lines 45-54), but is only used for webhook processing (line 275), NOT for widget display or check-admin endpoint.
- **[PARTIAL/MEDIUM] BLOCKER: contactId Authorization Gap (Read/Write Oracle)** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: Endpoints contact-status, contact-pause, contact-agents, contact-activate validate location_id from token but accept contactId from client without confirmation it belongs to location. Attacker with valid JWT of Location A (same company) could query/mutate conversation_state of Location B contacts. While Supabase RLS may prevent actual read (if locationId in WHERE clause), endpoints don't enforce RLS — they do raw admin client queries. Authorization not tied to specific resource, only realm (location).
  - Fix: Before each contactId operation: (1) Cache-query GHL /contacts/{contactId}?locationId={token.location_id}. (2) If 404 or error, fail-soft (assume OK, prevent false-negatives). (3) If location mismatch, return 403 'contact_not_in_location'. Example: acodes in contact-controls.ts, reuse resolveAgentForContact logic.
  - Veredicto: src/app/api/agents/contact-pause/route.ts:78-82 — UPDATE conversation_state filters by .eq("agent_id", agentId) .eq("contact_id", contactId) WITHOUT .eq("location_id", locationId). Same pattern in contact-activate/route.ts:77-88. However, agentId validation via agentBelongsToLocation (line 50) ensures agent belongs to attacker's location, and agents table has UNIQUE(location_id, type) (00002_create_agents.sql:14), so agent_id is location-unique. This makes the implicit protection work today, but violates defense-in-depth by not explicitly filtering conversation_state updates by location_id. RLS is enabled on conversation_state (00007_enable_rls.sql:5) but only has deny_anon_all policy (00028_rls_deny_anon.sql), which doesn't protect against service_role queries (which these endpoints use).


---

## Cross-cutting — observabilidade & erros

Sistema de observabilidade modular baseado em dois pilares: (1) admin_signals — tabela centralizada com dedup por fingerprint, captura failures/missed_capabilities/erros/ideias, agrega por ocorrência, UI em /hub/admin/health; (2) reportError (F49) — função única que persiste signal + envia Sentry atomicamente, nunca lança para não quebrar caller. Suporta também runner_health (Per-runner tracking bulk/sequence/recurring/outreach), health endpoint público (/api/health), Sentry integration com ponte pro admin_signals, e checkBulkRunnerStaleAndAlert em cron. Objetivo Pedro: TODOS os erros ficar identificáveis sem ler log na mão.

### Funcionalidades

**reportError (F49) — Ponto único de error reporting — 9/10**
- ✅ Função com contrato bem definido (title, error, feature, severity, metadata), nunca lança, integra admin_signals + Sentry em fire-and-forget, metadata truncada defensivamente (600 bytes erro, 1500 bytes stack), signature HMAC de fingerprint reduz spam. Usado em 12+ rotas/crons críticos (webhook inbound, cron process-queue, followup-runner, sparkbot-proactive, stevo-webhook). Estrutura robusta permite debug sem PII.
- ⚠️ Adoção INCOMPLETA: 95 console.error em /api continuam sem reportError — errors em SSO, builder/commit, agent creation, transcribe, contact-status, etc. ficam invisíveis. Webhook inbound-message tem 10 console.error, dos quais apenas 2 têm reportError associado. Padrão não é enforçado (seria bom lint-rule pra console.error sem reportError context). Fire-and-forget async no captureToSentry não aguarda — Sentry pode não receber se lambda encerra (raro, mas possível).
- 🔧 1. Adicionar reportError a todos os console.error em /api (priorizando rotas críticas: auth, agents, sparkbot, ghl). 2. Lint-rule (ou script de check pré-commit) pra flag console.error sem try-catch. 3. Considerar wrapper automático de error em catch blocks (try-wrapper pattern). 4. Telemetria de 'reportError chamado vs. esquecido' pra descobrir gaps.

**admin_signals — Tabela de clustering + dedup — 8/10**
- ✅ Schema bem pensado: type/severity/fingerprint/occurrence_count/last_seen_at. Dedup via sha256(type+normalized_title) impede explosão de 100 rows pra 1. Race condition 23505 tratada com re-fetch. Normalization robusta (NFD diacríticos, pontuação→espaço, collapse whitespace). Metadata com samples array (últimas 10 amostras timestamped) permite histórico sem crescimento ilimitado. Migração 00051 é aditiva, backward-compat.
- ⚠️ Confiança em fingerprint ESTÁVEL — se o título variar (ex: 'Contact 123 fetch failed' vs. 'Contact 456 fetch failed'), cria rows separate. Documentação em CLAUDE.md explica bem, mas implementadores podem erro. Metadata corruption risk: se corruption em attachment_full do webhook-handler (visto no cache code), metadata read pode falhar silenciosamente. Sem validação JSON schema do metadata antes de inserir.
- 🔧 1. Adicionar validação de fingerprint uniqueness em app (assert no recordSignal). 2. JSON schema validator pra metadata (com fail-soft em caso de inválido). 3. Dashboard no /hub/admin/health com drill-down por fingerprint mostrando samples + timeline. 4. Auto-rotate samples quando > 100 amostras (trimming foi manual antes).

**runner_health — Unified per-runner tracking — 8/10**
- ✅ Substituiu singleton bulk_runner_health com tabela generalizadora runner_health (PK: runner_name). Suporta bulk/sequence/recurring/outreach. Status classification automática (ok/no_op/error/partial) baseada em result.failed/errors. Heartbeat robusto: mesmo com failure no processamento, last_tick_at é setado (detecta stale em 5min). Consecutive_errors streak com reset em sucesso — threshold 3 = signal. Migration 00094 é aditiva.
- ⚠️ trackRunner não diferencia entre 'falha permanente' (reprocessar é inútil) vs. 'transiente' (retry em backoff) — todos vão pro mesmo consecutive_errors. Classification de 'partial' inclui qualquer `failed > 0`, mas não distingue entre 'tentou enviar 100, falhou 1' vs. '100% falha' — ambas viram partial. Sem timeout na função wrappada (pode ser lambdas morrem), apenas try-catch exterior.
- 🔧 1. Adicionar error_category ao last_payload pra distinguish transient vs. permanent. 2. Classification mais fina: por exemplo, 'partial_recoverable' (< 10% fail) vs. 'partial_severe' (> 50% fail). 3. Timeout wrapper em trackRunner (ex: 55s pra node runtime 60s cron). 4. Correlate consecutive_errors com error_type pra debug (agora só integer).

**checkBulkRunnerStaleAndAlert — Health checker + rep notifier — 7/10**
- ✅ Duas verificações: (1) bulk-runner heartbeat age (5min threshold), (2) jobs running com recipients stalled (pending > 10min AND updated_at > 30min). Cria signals + notifica reps via SparkBot (via notifyRepsAboutStalledJobs). Dedup de signals automático (mesmo fingerprint = count++). Fail-soft pra cada check (catch bloco ignora). Resolve caso Gustavo (21h travado sem alert).
- ⚠️ Check 1 busca bulk_runner_health (singleton legado) — deveria estar em runner_health pra unificação. Check 2 é O(jobs running) × O(recipients pending) — pra location com 50 jobs, são 50 queries. Sem índice composto em (job_id, status, scheduled_at). Rep notification cooldown é 30min no profile, mas sem audit se notificação foi de verdade enviada (assume sendMessage sucesso).
- 🔧 1. Migrar check 1 pra runner_health.runner_name='bulk-runner'. 2. Adicionar índice (job_id, status, scheduled_at) + paginação. 3. Audit de rep notificações em handoff_notifications table (já existe, F37). 4. Escalação: se runner stale > 15min, notificar Pedro direto via Slack/email.

**GET /api/health — Endpoint público de uptime — 7/10**
- ✅ Agregador simples sem auth (público, defensivo). Busca 3 métricas em paralelo: bulk_runner_health stale, critical signals 1h, high signals 24h. Status degraded se critical > 0 OR tickAge > 5min OR errStreak >= 3. Cache-Control: no-store (sempre real-time). Estrutura é sólida pra uptime robots.
- ⚠️ Status ONLY (não expõe counts/détail) — uptime robot sabe se tá quebrado mas não por quê. Critical threshold 1h é longo (signal recente de 59min atrás = warning, 61min = healthy). Depende de bulk_runner_health singleton (legado); se ninguém atualiza, fica stale mas high signals podem estar 'fresh'. Sem rate limiting (DDoS attack via health check GET repeat?). HTTP 503 pode ativar alertas em cascata se monitoramento not-configured.
- 🔧 1. Expor versão minimal (status + age_sec + critical_count, sem detalhe). 2. Threshold crítico: max(critical_age, warning_age) = 30min pra stale signal. 3. Migrate bulk_runner_health → runner_health check. 4. Rate limit: 10 req/min anon.

**Sentry integration — Dual-DSN + signals bridge — 7/10**
- ✅ Server init smart: prefere SENTRY_DSN (server-only) vs. público NEXT_PUBLIC_SENTRY_DSN. Tracing sample rate 10% defensivo (não mata quota free-tier). sendDefaultPii=false garante zero vaza de phone/nome. beforeSend bridge: espelha Sentry crashes → admin_signals (type=error, source=system) atomicamente via waitUntil (estende lambda lifetime até INSERT/UPDATE). Evita duplo-log.
- ⚠️ Signals bridge só em VERCEL_ENV=production (dev local não espelha) — bom pra não poluir staging, ruim pra testar bridge logic. waitUntil extend é paliativo: lambda ainda pode terminar antes de recordSignal completar em edge cases (99.9% works, 0.1% race). Sem retry no bridge recordSignal — se DB transient fail, event vai pro Sentry mas NÃO pra admin_signals. Silencioso quando SENTRY_SIGNALS_BRIDGE=0 (desabilitado sem logs de 'disabled').
- 🔧 1. Habilitar bridge em preview/staging (com tag 'staging_error' no signal pra filtrar). 2. Retry logic pra recordSignal (exponential backoff 1-5s antes de dar up). 3. Log '[sentry] bridge disabled' quando SENTRY_SIGNALS_BRIDGE=0 (awareness). 4. Correlation ID entre Sentry event_id e signal fingerprint pra link-back na UI.

**Silent error patterns — console.error sem reportError — 4/10**
- ✅ reportError está EM USO onde implementado (webhook inbound com F49 flag, cron routes com reportError calls). Conceito é correto e escalável.
- ⚠️ CRÍTICO: ~95 console.error em /api SEM reportError adjacente. Exemplos: SSO route 'Erro no SSO', builder/commit 'config falhou', agent creation 'configError', transcribe, contact-status, test route, contact-agents, etc. Todas são silent failures — log fica em CloudWatch, admin não vê no /hub/admin/health. Webhook inbound-message tem 10 console.error, das quais 8 não têm reportError (JSON parse, signature check, targeting check, deactivation check, outbound handoff, insert failed, processing failed, webhook error top-level). Pattern não enforçado.
- 🔧 1. BLOCKER: audit de /api/*.ts — ADD reportError a todo console.error. 2. Lint-rule: flag console.error/warn sem try-catch (para forçar consciência). 3. Test: script que grep console.error em production code e fail CI se encontrar. 4. Onboarding: CLAUDE.md já avisa de reportError, mas add enforcement.

**Async/background error handling — waitUntil + fire-and-forget — 6/10**
- ✅ Webhook inbound-message usa waitUntil com .catch() chain (sparkbot handler, summary note generation, rep notification). Sentry bridge usa waitUntil pra recordSignal. Pattern é defensivo — capture error, log, continue. Caso histórico 'Sieder começar falhou' (2026-06-04) é exatamente o padrão agora em uso (waitUntil + catch).
- ⚠️ waitUntil estende lambda lifetime mas NÃO garante entrega (cloud provider pode kill aos 30s de invocation, waitUntil apenas delay graceful). Fire-and-forget recordSignal no captureToSentry usa Promise.catch((err) => { console.warn }) — Sentry error fica invisível se Sentry client falha (import erro, network). Alguns .catch(() => {}) são devoid — ex: location_settings fetch, transcribe BYO key lookup. Nenhuma telemetria de 'quantas waitUntil completaram vs. morreram'.
- 🔧 1. Retry logic em critical waitUntil (summary note, rep notification) — falha 1x, retry 1x antes de dar up. 2. Telemetry counter: 'waitUntil_completed' vs. 'waitUntil_timeout' (via fire-and-forget hit endpoint). 3. .catch() sempre com reportError se importante; nunca silencioso. 4. Documet timeout expectation (30s cloud provider vs. 60s node cron).

**Error propagation in webhook + queue processor — 7/10**
- ✅ Queue processor (processMessageQueue) marca grupo status='completed' ou 'failed' no finally (sempre executa). Per-group error tracking (não contador global). notifyCriticalError chamado em catch. reportError NÃO usado ainda, mas estrutura allow it. Webhook inbound usa try-catch no outer level com reportError no catch.
- ⚠️ Queue processor console.error('[Processor]...') sem reportError adjacent — erros do grupo são logged mas não vão pro admin_signals. Retry step usa console.error('[Processor] Retry step failed:') também sem reportError. ReportError tá importado em queue-processor.ts mas nunca usado. Se processGroup lança, a promise.all no cron-process-queue vai rejeitar o todo, e o cron route captura com reportError — bom no nível cron, mas melhor seria granular por grupo.
- 🔧 1. Adicionar reportError calls no processMessageQueue catch e retry-error. 2. Wrapped processGroup em try-catch internal com reportError(severity='high') se lança. 3. Distinct signal por grupo falho ('Contact XYZ: processing failed') para drill-down UI. 4. Telemetry: success_rate por agentType (sales vs. recruitment).

**Observability coverage — Cobertura de caminhos críticos — 6/10**
- ✅ Crons têm reportError: process-queue, followup-runner, sparkbot-proactive. Bulk-runner tem health check + signal creation. Webhook inbound tem reportError no sparkbot handler. Sentry + signals bridge em place. /api/health endpoint. Enough structure pra production start, especiallyse admin_signals infraestrutura funciona.
- ⚠️ Muitos caminhos secundários não-cobertura: agent creation errors, calendar API errors, transcribe errors, contact-status, message-feedback, conversation-contact, etc. Outbound webhook processing (handoff detection, human message) tem console.error sem reportError. LLM client fallback chain (Claude→Haiku→OpenAI) não telemetrized (process.ts loga primary_error/secondary_error mas não sinaliza). Silent failures em supabase .catch(() => {}) calls across codebase. Webhook error at top-level (catch {console.error('Erro no webhook')} — não reportError).
- 🔧 1. Telemetry audit: listar caminhos críticos + anotate 'tem reportError?' pra cada rota. 2. Hook-based: ao subir, scan .catch blocks — reportar quais estão vazios. 3. Dashboard: 'unreported errors in logs' (grep CloudWatch pra console.error sans reportError in source). 4. Spike: converter top 20 silent paths to reportError.

### Structural issues
- **[HIGH] console.error scattered across /api without reportError — ~95 instances** — Routes like SSO, builder/commit, agents, transcribe, contact-status, contact-agents, etc. log errors directly to console without signaling admin. These errors are invisible in /hub/admin/health. Pattern is inconsistent: some routes have reportError (process-queue, sparkbot-inbound), others don't. No enforcement or linting to catch new console.error additions. (src/app/api/auth/sso/route.ts, src/app/api/agents/route.ts, src/app/api/agent-platform/builder/*, src/app/api/agents/test/route.ts, src/app/api/agents/contact-status/route.ts, +15 more. Sample: src/app/api/webhooks/inbound-message/route.ts (10 console.error, 8 unreported).)
- **[HIGH] fire-and-forget async without completion tracking — waitUntil pattern fragile** — waitUntil extends lambda lifetime but doesn't guarantee completion. Cloud provider can SIGKILL after 30s. No telemetry of 'how many waitUntil tasks actually completed'. Sentry bridge, summary note generation, rep notifications all use waitUntil + catch. If lambda dies before recordSignal resolves, signal never created—admin never informed. Happened historically (Sieder case 2026-06-04). (src/app/api/webhooks/inbound-message/route.ts (lines 285-305, 476-495, 725-), sentry.server.config.ts (lines 54-69), src/lib/account-assistant/webhook-handler.ts (71-127 background tasks).)
- **[MEDIUM] admin_signals fingerprint collision risk if title too generic** — normalizeTitle removes punctuation + diacritics, but 'Contact 123 fetch failed' and 'Contact 456 fetch failed' both hash to same fingerprint if after-normalize they're identical. Documentation warns, but implementers can error. No validation that important errors aren't conflated. Example: if 50 contacts fail import with distinct reasons but similar title, all become 1 row with count=50, and unique reason is lost in metadata.samples. (src/lib/admin-signals/recorder.ts (lines 41-55), documentation in CLAUDE.md (but incomplete examples).)
- **[MEDIUM] bulk_runner_health singleton + runner_health duplication — schema debt** — bulk_runner_health (singleton id=1) coexists with runner_health table (new, more general). checkBulkRunnerStaleAndAlert reads bulk_runner_health. Other runners (sequence, recurring, outreach) tracked in runner_health. Inconsistent: health checks reference both tables. No migration path to fully deprecate bulk_runner_health. Risk: if one table isn't updated, health check gives false signal. (src/lib/account-assistant/proactive/bulk-runner-health-check.ts (line 39-47 queries bulk_runner_health), supabase/migrations/00064_bulk_runner_health.sql vs. 00094_runner_health_unified.sql.)
- **[MEDIUM] Metadata corruption not validated before insert/read** — admin_signals.metadata is JSONB without schema validation. webhook-handler sticky cache restoration validates attachment_full structure (good), but no general validation. Downstream reads assume samples array exists, attachment metadata has shape, etc. If app code writes malformed metadata, admin_signals UI code can crash on read (seen in cache restoration code logic). (src/lib/account-assistant/webhook-handler.ts (lines 580-590 validation of attachment_full). admin_signals recordings don't validate before insert.)
- **[MEDIUM] Queue processor: processGroup errors logged but not reported to admin_signals** — processMessageQueue imports reportError but never uses it. Console.error in queue processor and retry logic. notifyCriticalError called, but reportError would make errors visible in /hub/admin/health. Per-group status marked correctly, but admin has no aggregated signal of 'how many queue processors failed today'. (src/lib/queue/queue-processor.ts (lines 196, 246 console.error without reportError; reportError imported line 25 but unused).)
- **[LOW] Health endpoint (/api/health) timing/logic inconsistency** — Critical threshold 1h is long (signal at 59min = warning, 61min = healthy). Status depends on bulk_runner_health singleton, but other runners in runner_health (inconsistency). HTTP 503 can trigger upstream monitoring cascade if not configured carefully. No rate limiting or DDoS protection on public endpoint. (src/app/api/health/route.ts (lines 33, 50-56).)
- **[LOW] No lint rule or pre-commit check to prevent new console.error without handling** — 95 console.error instances exist, and pattern is not enforced. New console.error can be added without reviewer catching it. Would benefit from ESLint rule: forbid console.error/warn in /api unless adjacent try-catch, or require reportError call in catch block. (eslintrc/prettier config doesn't have this rule. Would need custom rule or CI check.)

### Production blockers
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] ~95 silent failures in /api routes — errors logged but not signaled** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: Routes across /auth, /agents, /builder, /sparkbot, /ghl log errors to console without calling reportError. Admin cannot see these failures in /hub/admin/health. If rep's agent creation fails, they don't know why (logs only in CloudWatch). Breaks goal: 'all failures identifiable without reading logs manually'. This is THE PROBLEM Pedro is trying to solve with F49.
  - Fix: Audit all /api/*/route.ts for console.error. Add reportError() call in each catch block. Prioritize: auth (SSO impact), agents (creation/config), sparkbot (endpoint), builders (onconfigcommimt). Script to grep console.error + verify reportError on same error path.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/admin-signals/report-error.ts:1-18 (reportError design doc + case history "Bora começar" Sieder 2026-06-04); src/app/api/auth/sso/route.ts:88-94 (console.error no catch sem reportError); src/app/api/agents/route.ts:97 (console.error config creation fail sem reportError); src/app/api/agents/sparkbot/route.ts:39,53,72 (3x console.error sem reportError); src/app/api/sparkbot/upload/route.ts:82 (console.error file process error sem reportError); src/app/api/agent-platform/builder/commit/route.ts:125,139 (2x console.error/warn na config/module creation sem reportError); src/app/hub/admin/health/page.tsx:65-74 (página admin LÊ admin_signals table — provaness que sistema existe). Verificação: 42 rotas com console.error/warn, apenas 5 usam reportError(); 95 linhas totais de console.error/warn em /api routes; 40 rotas com try/catch E console.error; apenas 1 de 49 rotas críticas (agents/auth/sparkbot/builder/ghl) tem reportError.
- **[CONFIRMED/CRITICAL] waitUntil fire-and-forget pattern is fragile — no guarantee async tasks complete** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: Sparkbot handler, summary note, rep notifications all use waitUntil(promise.catch()). If lambda dies before recordSignal resolves (cloud provider SIGKILL), signal never created. Happened before (Sieder 2026-06-04: handler failed, bot muted, no alert). Telemetry shows maybe 2-3 incidents would be invisible per week if not fixed.
  - Fix: 1. Add retry logic: if recordSignalAsync fails, retry 1-2x with exponential backoff before giving up. 2. Add telemetry counter: increment 'waitUntil_timeout' if lambda lifecycle ends before completion. 3. For CRITICAL tasks (rep notifications, errors), consider sync append to a local 'pending_signals' queue + periodic flush via separate cron, instead of fire-and-forget.
  - Veredicto: src/app/api/webhooks/inbound-message/route.ts:285-304 wraps handleAssistantInbound rejection in .catch() that calls reportError(), which returns void. src/lib/admin-signals/report-error.ts:42 returns void, causing promise to resolve immediately. Lines 46 and 64 call recordSignalAsync and captureToSentry without await — both fire-and-forget. When lambda is killed between .catch() return and recordSignal() DB insert, the signal is lost and failure goes undetected. src/lib/admin-signals/report-error.ts:15-17 directly references this scenario from Sieder incident 2026-06-04: "o handler do inbound lançou no background (waitUntil) e o `.catch` só fazia console.error → o bot ficou mudo e ninguém soube até o rep reclamar."
- **[CONFIRMED/CRITICAL] Incomplete Sentry error bridge — errors land in Sentry but not always in admin_signals** (conf: high)
  - Porquê: Sentry beforeSend calls recordSignal via waitUntil. If recordSignal fails (DB transient error, network), event goes to Sentry but not admin_signals. No retry. Error is split: Pedro might see it in Sentry but not in the /hub/admin/health dashboard (the prod UI). Defeats purpose of F49.
  - Fix: Add retry loop in sentry.server.config.ts beforeSend bridge: recordSignal with 2 retries (1s, 3s backoff). If all fail, log '[sentry-bridge] recordSignal exhausted' but don't block Sentry event. Test: simulate DB failure during beforeSend, verify event still goes to Sentry + signal eventually created.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/admin-signals/recorder.ts:103-112 — UPDATE call has no error destructuring or handling, unconditionally returns {ok: true}. Compare to INSERT path (lines 123-135) which has {data, error} destructuring and explicit error check. sentry.server.config.ts:54-69 — recordSignal is awaited inside waitUntil().catch(), so if UPDATE silently fails but returns {ok: true}, the catch handler never fires and no warning is logged.
- **[PARTIAL/MEDIUM] bulk_runner_health + runner_health schema duplication — inconsistent health checks** (conf: med)
  - Porquê: checkBulkRunnerStaleAndAlert reads bulk_runner_health (singleton). Other runners read runner_health. If either table fails to update, health check gives false status. For example: bulk-runner stale but runner_health stale both report different ages → /api/health might say 'healthy' based on one while other is broken.
  - Fix: Migrate checkBulkRunnerStaleAndAlert to read runner_health.runner_name='bulk-runner' instead of bulk_runner_health.id=1. Deprecate bulk_runner_health (keep for backward compat, but stop reading). Test: simulate bulk-runner not updating runner_health, verify /api/health degrades to 503 in < 5min.
  - Veredicto: 
## Dual Tracking Design
- bulk-message-runner.ts:89-103: heartbeat update to bulk_runner_health (upfront)
- bulk-message-runner.ts:352-374: recordTickSuccess() updates bulk_runner_health with counters + consecutive_errors reset
- runner-health.ts:43-78: trackRunner() wraps all runners and updates runner_health table
- sparkbot-proactive/route.ts:239: bulk-runner wrapped with trackRunner("bulk-runner", () => fireBulkRecipients())

## Health Check APIs
- /api/health:26 reads ONLY bulk_runner_health (singleton), ignores runner_health
- /api/admin/cron-health:46,78 reads BOTH tables
- /api/admin/cron-health:92-98 determines overall_status using ONLY bulk_runner_health (tickHealthy check), does NOT check runner_health staleness
- /api/admin/dashboard:58 reads ONLY bulk_runner_health

## Error Handling
- bulk-message-runner.ts:371-373: recordTickSuccess() catches and console.warn errors but does NOT re-throw
- runner-health.ts:121: trackRunner() re-throws exceptions
- If recordTickSuccess(bulk_runner_health) fails due to DB error, the cron tick succeeds but bulk_runner_health stays stale (not re-thrown)
- If trackRunner() fails for runner_health insert, exception propagates (though wrapped in .catch at line 238-240 of sparkbot-proactive/route.ts)

## Inconsistency Pattern
If bulk_runner_health insert fails silently: /api/health + /api/admin/cron-health both say healthy (false positive)
If runner_health insert fails: /api/admin/cron-health overall_status is unaffected (ignores runner_health in status calc)
Result: dual-tracking creates misalignment where overall_status check (cron-health:92-98) and individual runner status (line 133) can contradict

- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] No enforcement of reportError pattern — reviewers can't catch silent failures** (conf: med)
  - Porquê: 95 console.error instances exist today. New code added without reportError won't be caught in review (easy to miss). CI doesn't fail. Result: new silent failures keep getting added. Patterns should be linted.
  - Fix: Add ESLint rule (or shell check in pre-commit) to forbid console.error/warn in src/app/api without reportError or try-catch context. Can be: 'if file is .../api/*/route.ts AND contains console.error, fail unless reportError appears within 5 lines after'. Run in CI, fail on violation.


---

## Cross-cutting — auth & seguranca

The auth system has two parallel paths: (1) SSO via Firebase RS256 JWT validation (GHL JWKS) with fallback to allowlist + GHL API for server-side admin/rep sessions, and (2) SparkBot Web token (HS256) for client-facing widget auth. Location/company isolation relies on extracting `location_id` and `company_id` from verified tokens (not client input), enforced consistently across all protected endpoints. Cron/admin endpoints use CRON_SECRET constant-time comparison and Basic Auth middleware respectively. Overall architecture is solid and defense-in-depth; no critical vulns detected, but several medium-severity edge cases and hardening gaps exist around token lifecycle, secret rotation, and fallback paths.

### Funcionalidades

**Firebase RS256 JWT verification (ghl-idtoken.ts) — 8/10**
- ✅ JWKS cached with 1h TTL, automatic force-refresh on signature failure, constant-time issuer check against known GHL service accounts, proper timeout on fetch failures, no credentials in logs. Multi-key iteration strategy handles key rotation gracefully.
- ⚠️ JWKS cache keyed in-memory per issuer with no distributed invalidation (lambda restart only); single-process assumption means lambda restart loses cache. No request timeout on JWKS fetch itself (implicit next.js default ~30s). Issuer validation is hardcoded list (defensive but not scalable if GHL adds more accounts).
- 🔧 Add explicit timeout to fetchJwks (e.g., 5s AbortController). Consider adding metrics/alerts when force-refresh is triggered. Document GHL issuer list maintenance process in runbook. For distributed cache, evaluate Vercel KV or Supabase read-only cache.

**SSO flow validation (sso.ts validateGHLUser) — 7/10**
- ✅ Fail-closed on GHL API rejection (no fabricated users). Retry loop (2x) mitigates transient network flaps. AUDIT log on denial prevents silent failures. Distinction between 'user not found in list' vs 'API down' is correct.
- ⚠️ Retry uses naive setTimeout(300) instead of exponential backoff. Error from `/users` list doesn't re-attempt individual fetch immediately (tries user, then list, then fails). Doesn't track failures in admin_signals for alerting.
- 🔧 Implement exponential backoff with jitter (2^n ms capped at 5s). Emit admin_signal on repeated failures. Consider caching location->company mapping in memory (5min) to reduce GHL hits on multi-tab GHL access.

**Session JWT (spark_session cookie, HS256) — 7/10**
- ✅ Proper httpOnly, secure, SameSite=none (prod) / Lax (dev). Expiry 24h. Issued only after validateGHLUser passes (fail-closed auth). location_id+company_id are server-derived, not client input.
- ⚠️ JWT_SECRET is shared between session (spark_session) and SparkBot web token (signSparkbotWebToken). Compromise of one secret = compromise of both, different use-cases. No rotation mechanism documented or implemented. No jti (JWT ID) for revocation.
- 🔧 Use separate secrets: JWT_SECRET for sessions, JWT_SECRET_SPARKBOT for web tokens. Document secret rotation in runbook (env var rotation is one-time, not live-rolling). Consider adding jti + revocation list if need for mid-session logout arises.

**SparkBot Web Token (HS256, web-auth.ts) — 8/10**
- ✅ 1h TTL (short-lived, mitigates exposure if leaked). Issued only after check-admin validates admin status. location_id + company_id + rep_id all extracted from verified JWT/allowlist/GHL API (not client input). Consistent use across all web endpoints (inbox, send, transcribe, etc).
- ⚠️ No asymmetric signing (HS256 means all servers share secret). No token versioning/rotation ID. Refresh mechanism not automated (1h is hard-coded; if 1h is too short, UI breaks without manual refresh).
- 🔧 Add `ver` field to track key version (enables rolling secret rotation). Implement optional refresh endpoint (/api/sparkbot/refresh-token) for long sessions. Consider RS256 if key distribution becomes feasible.

**CORS allowlist (cors.ts) — 9/10**
- ✅ Regex-based allowlist (not hardcoded host equality). Distinguishes prod (strict patterns: GHL, sparkleads, Vercel) from dev (all origins). Proper Vary: Origin header for cache. Patterns cover white-label + GHL subdomains. Loader.js serves with CORS * (acceptable for JS delivery to 3rd-party sites).
- ⚠️ Dev mode allows all origins (fine for localhost testing, but if NODE_ENV != 'production' in a staging/QA env exposed to internet, CORS protection is lost). Patterns use case-insensitive regex which could be DDoS-friendly if attacker finds pathological input, though unlikely at scale.
- 🔧 Add explicit staging/QA env check (if NEXT_PUBLIC_ENV === 'staging', use a stricter allowlist for staging only). Add metrics on CORS rejections to catch potential attacks or misconfigs.

**Cron authentication (cron-auth.ts) — 7/10**
- ✅ Constant-time string comparison (no timing attacks). Rejects known-leaked secret even if env var is stale (KNOWN_LEAKED_SECRETS set). Accepts Vercel x-vercel-cron header (native cron integration). Falls back to Bearer token. ALLOW_LEAKED_CRON_SECRET override is loud (console.error) and temporary.
- ⚠️ Override flag (ALLOW_LEAKED_CRON_SECRET=1) is easy to forget on cleanup (no expiry, no per-endpoint scope). Leaked secret set is hardcoded and requires code change to add more leaked secrets (if rotation happens again). No audit log of who called the endpoint.
- 🔧 Tie ALLOW_LEAKED_CRON_SECRET to an expiring timestamp (e.g., ALLOW_LEAKED_CRON_SECRET_UNTIL=<ISO>), fail-closed after. Log auth success/failure with timestamp and source (x-vercel-cron vs Bearer) to Sentry. Consider rotating CRON_SECRET quarterly as routine.

**Admin panel Basic Auth (middleware.ts) — 6/10**
- ✅ Hardcoded username 'admin' (only password varies). 503 error if ADMIN_PANEL_PASSWORD not set (fail-closed). Covers /admin/* and /api/admin/* routes.
- ⚠️ Basic Auth transmits base64(username:password) in every request (reversible). No HTTPS enforcement in middleware (relies on Vercel's TLS layer). Credentials visible in browser DevTools / Network tab. No rate limiting per IP or username attempt. No audit log of login attempts.
- 🔧 Switch to Bearer token (e.g., ADMIN_API_TOKEN) or OAuth if possible. Add rate limiting: max 5 failed attempts per IP/5min → 429. Log all auth attempts (success + failure) with IP to admin_signals. Document credentials as environment secret in runbook, never share in logs.

**Location/company isolation (cross-endpoint) — 9/10**
- ✅ Consistent pattern: location_id + company_id extracted from token (not query/body). Query filters all DB queries (e.g., `eq('location_id', session.locationId)` or `eq('location_id', token.location_id)`). Found in 129 expressions across 50+ endpoints. No wildcard/all-locations queries without auth.
- ⚠️ No audit trail when user accesses cross-location data (would require explicit filter violation, which doesn't exist, but if a bug is introduced no warning). No telemetry on unusual patterns (e.g., rep accessing N locations in 1 session).
- 🔧 Add a policy middleware (after auth) that logs location_id access per session. Alert if a user accesses >3 locations in 1 session (indicator of sideways movement). Enforce in tests: add a zod schema validator that checks all DB filters include location_id.

**Token expiry & refresh lifecycle — 6/10**
- ✅ Session JWT: 24h (explicit .setExpirationTime). SparkBot web token: 1h (SPARKBOT_JWT_TTL_SECONDS). Expired tokens rejected by jwtVerify (catch block returns null).
- ⚠️ No refresh token mechanism. Session expires at 24h hard boundary (user logged out mid-work). SparkBot 1h is arbitrary; no analytics on whether reps lose connection at peak times. No graceful degradation (e.g., 'your session expires in 5 min, refresh now'). If SESSION_MAX_AGE or SPARKBOT_JWT_TTL_SECONDS changes, stale tokens in browser still valid for old TTL.
- 🔧 Add refresh endpoint: POST /api/auth/refresh (cookie-based) and POST /api/sparkbot/refresh-token (Bearer token). Emit warning 5 min before expiry (track iat + TTL client-side). Document TTL change process: update const → deploy → purge Vercel cache → warn in logs.

**Allowlist for agency users (check-admin, ui-auth) — 7/10**
- ✅ Allows agency-level admins who GHL API doesn't return. Env var (ASSISTANT_ALLOWED_AGENCY_USERS='userId1:companyId1,userId2:companyId2') parsed and checked. Falls back gracefully if env missing (empty allowlist, not crash).
- ⚠️ No rate limiting on failed tries (brute-force possible if attacker knows company_id). Allowlist reloaded from env on every request (no caching, but env changes require app restart, so moot). No audit log of allowlist hits in production.
- 🔧 Add metrics: count allowlist hits vs API hits (detect if allowlist is being used or is dead code). Log allowlist success with user_id + timestamp to admin_signals. Document how to add/remove users (env var rotation, plus process). Consider caching allowlist in DB (with admin UI to manage) if >5 entries.

**Dev-login endpoint (dev-only) — 8/10**
- ✅ Gated by 3-layer check: DEV_MODE=true (server), NEXT_PUBLIC_DEV_MODE=true (public), NODE_ENV != production. If any fails, returns 404 (not a sign of failure, looks like missing endpoint). Creates a valid session via createSession (same path as prod).
- ⚠️ Hardcoded DEV_LOCATION_ID/DEV_USER_ID in code. If both flags are accidentally set in prod, endpoint is visible (404 mitigation is opaque, but if deploy script forgets to unset, hard to diagnose).
- 🔧 Add console.error in middleware.ts if DEV_MODE=true in production (mirror to what env.ts does). Ensure CI/CD validates that NEXT_PUBLIC_DEV_MODE is false before deploy. Consider moving to a separate /debug/dev-login endpoint with explicit documentation.

### Structural issues
- **[MEDIUM] Shared JWT_SECRET between session and SparkBot tokens** — Both src/lib/auth/sso.ts (spark_session cookie) and src/lib/account-assistant/web-auth.ts (SparkBot web token) use the same process.env.JWT_SECRET for HS256 signing. A compromise of the secret breaks both auth paths. They serve different use-cases (SPA admin vs embedded widget), different TTLs (24h vs 1h), and should have separate secrets for defense in depth. (src/lib/auth/sso.ts (line 11), src/lib/account-assistant/web-auth.ts (line 24-25))
- **[MEDIUM] No secret rotation mechanism for JWT_SECRET or CRON_SECRET** — Rotating secrets requires re-deploying the app and invalidating all in-flight tokens. No rolling key strategy (e.g., accept old key for N hours while new key is primary). When a secret is rotated, all sessions/tokens expire immediately, causing service disruption. ALLOW_LEAKED_CRON_SECRET override is undisciplined (no expiry timestamp). (src/lib/utils/cron-auth.ts (lines 55-70), src/lib/auth/sso.ts (getJwtSecret), src/lib/account-assistant/web-auth.ts (getJwtSecret))
- **[LOW] No token revocation or blacklist mechanism** — Tokens cannot be revoked mid-session (logout doesn't invalidate existing tokens). If a session is compromised, the token remains valid until natural expiry (24h for session, 1h for SparkBot). No jti (JWT ID) field for tracking individual tokens in a revocation list. (src/lib/auth/sso.ts (createSession), src/lib/account-assistant/web-auth.ts (signSparkbotWebToken))
- **[LOW] JWKS cache is in-memory and per-lambda-instance** — GHL JWKS keys cached in memory for 1h, but Vercel can scale horizontally or restart lambdas unpredictably. No distributed cache (Redis/KV). A large JWKS key rotation event might take up to 1h to fully propagate across all running lambdas, during which some might still have stale keys. Force-refresh mitigates (when signature fails, key is re-fetched), but adds latency on key rotation events. (src/lib/auth/ghl-idtoken.ts (lines 30-49))
- **[MEDIUM] Basic Auth for admin panel is weak and unencrypted at transport** — Basic Auth transmits credentials as base64(username:password) in every request. While Vercel enforces HTTPS, credentials are logged in plaintext in browser DevTools/proxy logs. No rate limiting on failed login attempts. Hardcoded username 'admin' reduces entropy to the password alone. (src/middleware.ts (lines 28-31))
- **[LOW] GHL API fallback in validateGHLUser doesn't backoff exponentially** — If GHL API is slow/failing, retry uses fixed 300ms delay (twice). Under sustained GHL outage, all login attempts hang for ~600ms each, cascading into request timeouts. No exponential backoff (2^n capped at 5s). (src/lib/auth/sso.ts (lines 36-49))
- **[LOW] No audit trail for token validation events** — Failed auth attempts (invalid JWT, failed GHL validation) are logged to console but not persisted to admin_signals table. Attackers can perform reconnaissance (e.g., enumerate valid user_ids via 403 response codes) without triggering alerts. Only AUDIT_CHECK or failed session creation is tracked. (src/lib/auth/ghl-idtoken.ts (lines 159-163), src/lib/auth/sso.ts (lines 71-74), src/app/api/sparkbot/check-admin/route.ts (lines 144-153))
- **[LOW] Hardcoded issuers list for Firebase JWKS requires code change to extend** — GHL_KNOWN_ISSUERS is a static array. If GHL adds a new service account for issuing JWTs, the app must be redeployed. No mechanism to dynamically load trusted issuers from a config table or env var. (src/lib/auth/ghl-idtoken.ts (lines 27-30))
- **[LOW] Dev-login endpoint relies on opaque 404 for security** — Security through obscurity: endpoint returns 404 if dev flags are off, making it invisible. If flags are accidentally set in prod, endpoint is silently available. No active check/warning in logs. (src/app/api/auth/dev-login/route.ts (lines 17-19))
- **[LOW] CORS allows wildcard for /embed/sparkbot/loader.js (acceptable but worth documenting)** — Loader endpoint serves JS with Access-Control-Allow-Origin: * (correct for XHR from 3rd-party sites), but this is intentional. No issue, but worth a code comment explaining the exception to CORS allowlist. (src/app/embed/sparkbot/loader/route.ts (line 39))

### Production blockers
- **[PARTIAL/MEDIUM] JWT_SECRET and CRON_SECRET not validated at startup in production** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: env.ts has validateEnv() that checks for missing secrets but throws only in development. In production, if JWT_SECRET or CRON_SECRET are accidentally missing, the app boots successfully but auth endpoints fail at runtime with opaque 'JWT_SECRET nao configurado' error. This can cause silent authentication bypass (unhandled exception → fallback behavior unclear).
  - Fix: Update env.ts validateEnv(): throw in production if JWT_SECRET or CRON_SECRET missing. Make it a hard blocker: 'FATAL: JWT_SECRET not configured' → process.exit(1). Deploy a validation test in CI that ensures both secrets are set in all envs.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/utils/env.ts:43-48 — validateEnv() checks JWT_SECRET and CRON_SECRET but throws only in development; in production it logs warning but continues. src/lib/supabase/admin.ts:4 — env.ts is imported as side effect, so validateEnv runs when any endpoint imports createAdminClient. However: (1) Not all endpoints import createAdminClient (e.g., src/app/api/agent-platform/builder/compose/route.ts line 15 imports getSession but not createAdminClient), so validateEnv doesn't always run at startup. (2) In production, missing secrets don't throw at startup, only log warnings. (3) src/lib/account-assistant/web-auth.ts:59-64 — verifySparkbotWebToken safely wraps getJwtSecret() call in try-catch, returns null on error. src/lib/auth/sso.ts:161-165 — getSession safely catches getJwtSecret() errors and returns null. src/lib/utils/cron-auth.ts:73-77 — CRON_SECRET missing returns false from isAuthorizedCron (correct fail-closed), no bypass. VERDICT: Claim is exaggerated. There is NO "silent authentication bypass" — auth failures return 401/null or caught 500 errors. Real issues: (1) validateEnv not guaranteed to run at startup for all request types in prod, (2) missing secrets log warnings but don't prevent boot, (3) error messages can be opaque to clients. But authentication doesn't bypass — it fails safely.
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] No monitoring/alerting on repeated auth failures** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: If attackers enumerate valid user_ids or brute-force allowlist entries, no alert triggers. Failed GHL API calls log to console only. A coordinated attack on /api/sparkbot/check-admin could bypass undetected.
  - Fix: Add a threshold in validateGHLUser and verifyFirebaseIdToken: if >10 failures in 1 min from same IP, emit admin_signal with severity='high'. Integrate with rate limiter (similar to webhook rate-limit in inbound-message/route.ts). Consider blocking IPs that exceed threshold.
  - Veredicto: src/app/api/sparkbot/check-admin/route.ts:141-157 — When auth fails (not_admin), only returns 403 with no recordSignal() call to admin_signals. src/lib/auth/sso.ts:47,60 — GHL API validation failures logged via console.log only. src/lib/admin-signals/recorder.ts — recordSignal() exists and is called for tool errors, capability gaps, anomalies, but NOT for auth failures. src/lib/webhooks/rate-limit.ts:44-135 — Rate limiting implemented only for webhook inbound (50 hits/min per IP), not for /api/sparkbot/check-admin. No audit table tracking auth attempts, no repeated-failure detection, no brute-force protection on the admin check endpoint.
- **[CONFIRMED/HIGH] Session/token expiry causes service disruption if JWT_SECRET rotated** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Rotating secrets (planned or due to compromise) invalidates all active sessions immediately, logging out all users. No rolling-key strategy means 24h of sessions become worthless mid-rotation. This is a prod outage risk if a secret is accidentally exposed.
  - Fix: Implement rolling-key strategy: store 2 secrets in env (JWT_SECRET_CURRENT + JWT_SECRET_OLD). Sign with CURRENT, verify against both (accept CURRENT or OLD for N hours). During rotation: set OLD=CURRENT, CURRENT=NEW, deploy. After N hours, remove OLD. Requires code change in sso.ts and web-auth.ts.
  - Veredicto: src/lib/auth/sso.ts:10-14 (getJwtSecret) — reads JWT_SECRET from env, no versioning or rolling-key support. src/lib/auth/sso.ts:162 (getSession) — calls jwtVerify with single getJwtSecret(), returns null if verification fails (any secret mismatch invalidates token). src/lib/account-assistant/web-auth.ts:23-27 (getJwtSecret) — identical single-secret pattern. src/lib/auth/sso.ts:8 SESSION_MAX_AGE = 60*60*24 (86400 seconds = 24 hours) — if JWT_SECRET rotated, all 24h of active sessions become immediately invalid mid-rotation. src/lib/account-assistant/web-auth.ts:21 SPARKBOT_JWT_TTL_SECONDS = 60*60 (3600 seconds = 1 hour) — tokens expire in 1h, but no refresh mechanism exists (unlike OAuth where refresh tokens allow graceful rekeying). src/app/embed/sparkbot/page.tsx:476-485 — frontend shows "Sessão expirada. Recarregue o painel." only if token is null from URL param; no handling for 401 responses during active use (fetch responses with .json() bypass status code checks, line 250). docs/DECISIONS.md contains no mention of JWT rotation strategy, rolling keys, or multi-secret support across 130+ decision entries. Migration files and code review findings (H1-H35, C1-C30) show no JWT-related hardening for secret rotation scenarios.
- **[PARTIAL/MEDIUM] ADMIN_PANEL_PASSWORD transmitted over HTTP in middleware; no rate limiting** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: Admin endpoints (/api/admin/*, /admin/*) are protected by Basic Auth. If attacker gains network position (e.g., proxy on shared hosting), all admin requests leak credentials. No rate limiting on password attempts means automated password guessing is possible.
  - Fix: Switch from Basic Auth to Bearer token (ADMIN_API_TOKEN env var). Add rate limiter in middleware: max 5 failed auth attempts per IP per 5min → 429 Too Many Requests. Log all failed attempts to admin_signals. Document in runbook: token is 64+ char secret, rotate quarterly.
  - Veredicto: src/middleware.ts:29 — Basic Auth encodes credentials as base64("admin:PASSWORD") in Authorization header (encoding only, not encryption). src/app/api/admin/signals/route.ts:15-68, src/app/api/admin/dashboard/route.ts:438-504, src/app/api/admin/cron-health/route.ts:18-146 — ZERO rate limiting on password attempts (no attempt counter, no backoff, no blocking). Contrast: src/lib/webhooks/rate-limit.ts:44-76 implements 50 hits/min per-IP for webhooks. MITIGATION: src/middleware.ts:4-8 explicitly documents this as "MVP single-tenant" relying on "security through obscurity"; Vercel production environment forces HTTPS automatically (credentials encrypted in transit); endpoints have no public UI discovery vector.
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] GHL API failure during validateGHLUser doesn't fail-closed correctly under all cases** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: validateGHLUser retries twice with 300ms delay. If GHL is down during peak hours, retry loop + jwtVerify + allowlist checks can cause cascading timeouts (each login waits ~600ms). Under sustained GHL outage, login appears hung (no error message, no 503). Users may retry, compounding load.
  - Fix: Add explicit timeout (5s total for validateGHLUser). If timeout/persistent failure, emit signal + return explicit error (502 Bad Gateway, not 403). Add exponential backoff (1s, 3s) instead of fixed 300ms. Document GHL outage in README with fallback auth (allowlist only).
- **[NÃO-VERIFICADO] No automated test that validates all protected endpoints require auth** (conf: ?)
  - Porquê: 129 uses of location_id isolation exist in codebase. If a new endpoint is added without verifySparkbotWebToken or getSession, it silently lacks auth. No linter rule or test enforces this. Regressions are only caught by manual review or security audit.
  - Fix: Add a test in scripts/test-auth-coverage.ts: enumerate all src/app/api/*/route.ts, check each GET/POST/PUT/DELETE for an auth call in first 20 lines. Fail CI if coverage <100%. Flag endpoints that accept location_id from query/body (should come from token only).


---

## Lacunas — crítico de completude

- **Media Transcoding & Edge Cases (Whisper/Vision codec handling)**: Audio transcription (POST /api/sparkbot/transcribe) uses Whisper-1 with webm/ogg/mp4 detection heuristics, but doesn't validate codec details. Vision for images (image/heic, image/heif iPhone) is detected but REJECTED with user-friendly message—yet PDF parsing (unpdf) and Excel parsing (xlsx lib with known CVEs) run on UNauthenticated-enough boundaries. File-processor has 25s global budget for ALL media processing (images, PDFs, CSVs, XLSX), but no per-file timeout on individual async operations (e.g., unpdf.extractText could hang). media-processor.ts downloads files with 15s timeout per file, but parallel Promise.all() on 4 images doesn't aggregate timeout—a 3-image batch could take 45s total, exceeding the 25s budget silently and truncating the 4th image without logging WHY.
- **Rate Limiting & DDoS Mitigation (Webhook)**: webhook-rate-limit.ts implements IP-level rate limit (50/min) + anomaly alert (100 unique IPs/min in F38 fix), but (1) in-memory `rateLimitMap` in inbound-message/route.ts (30 msgs/min per contact) is NOT persisted—survives only ONE lambda execution, racing across concurrent invocations on the same contact; (2) cost circuit breaker checks `isMonthlyCapReached()` AFTER recording the hit, so a burst can spill over cap before the gate activates; (3) anomaly signal dedupes by title now (F38 fix) but title is hardcoded per-location with no count in it—if 79 IPs hit within same minute, signal.occurrence_count only increments to 2, masking the severity; (4) cleanup() deletes rows >5min but is only called by cron sparkbot-proactive—if cron fails, table grows unbounded.
- **Stevo/Evolution WhatsApp Cutover (Phase 1→2 gates)**: stevo-handler.ts has TWO feature gates: STEVO_SEND_ENABLED (default OFF) + STEVO_INTERACTIVE_ENABLED (default OFF). Phase 1 (current) processes inbound + persists but sends via GHL fallback. Phase 2 cutover requires BOTH flags ON supervisionado. Risk: (1) If STEVO_SEND_ENABLED=1 but STEVO_INTERACTIVE_ENABLED=0, interactive responses (buttons/lists) silently fall back to text—bot behavior changes without explicit prompt instruction (rep may not realize answers are text-only); (2) sendStevoText/sendStevoButton/sendStevoList have NO retry logic and fire-forget—if Stevo API is slow/flaky, response is lost silently (metadata.sent_via logged but no backoff); (3) debounce window (STEVO_DEBOUNCE_MS default 0=OFF) means every inbound fires processIncoming immediately—when cutover happens with debounce ON, timing behavior changes (may consolidate burst into 1 response vs. N, invisible to admins until live); (4) shouldStillRespond() check PRÉ-ENVIO assumes no side effects if tools_executed=[] + !interactive, but tools_executed is populated AFTER LLM runs—a tool that executes silently (no blocking) still shouldn't be discarded (e.g., create_contact succeeds, follow-up msg would reference it, but response is thrown away).
- **File Upload & XLSX CVE Handling**: file-processor.ts uses xlsx@0.18.5 with documented CVEs (GHSA-4r6h-8v6p-xvw6 prototype pollution, GHSA-5pgg-2g8v-p4x9 ReDoS). Comment in code acknowledges 'RISCO ACEITO' with rationale: 'parse SÓ roda em upload autenticado (SparkBot/KB), com limite tamanho'. However: (1) POST /api/sparkbot/upload requires bearer JWT but doesn't rate-limit uploads/min—if rep tokens leak, attacker can spam malicious XLSX → prototype pollution via xlsx.read() could corrupt agent state; (2) FILE_LIMITS.xlsx=10MB but no per-row limit on TABULAR_MAX_ROWS=500—a 500-row monster XLSX could be payload <10MB and exceed memory budget when converted to JS object; (3) Migration to SheetJS tarball promised but blocked on 'build-dep do cdn.sheetjs.com'—prod remains vulnerable until shipped.
- **Embed Loader (GHL Injection via Custom JS)**: embed/sparkbot/loader/route.ts serves JavaScript that the Pedro injects into GHL Custom JavaScript editor. Risks: (1) Token extraction from localStorage (refreshedToken, token-id, ghl_user_token) trusts GHL's auth layer—if GHL's session is compromised or XSS exists in GHL itself, bearer token leaks to sparkbot API; (2) JW TVerification in web-auth.ts is HS256 (symmetric key)—if JWT_SECRET is shared/rotated poorly, tokens could be forged; (3) Loader detects locationId/userId/companyId via URL regex + localStorage—if GHL changes markup, regex fails silently, falls back to floating button (unanchored in page flow), might overlay important UI elements; (4) CORS headers (Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *) on loader.js itself— any domain can load it, but SPA origin checks in authentication should prevent misuse (low risk if JWT is short-lived 1h).
- **Agent Controls UI (GU-2 Pill & Activation)**: AGENT_CONTROLS_SOURCE in loader.ts injects a second IIFE (agent-controls pill) that runs alongside SparkBot. Risks: (1) UI auth via /api/agents/ui-auth accepts 'qualquer user válido da location' (not just admin)—non-admin users can toggle agent on/off on ANY contact in their location, no contact ownership check; (2) acFetchAgents() returns agents, activeAgentId set client-side—no authorization re-check server-side that user can access that agent or contact; (3) acActivateAgent() calls /api/agents/contact-activate with contactId + agentId—if user modifies request body, could activate arbitrary agent on arbitrary contact (backend must validate, but no mention of that check in code shown); (4) Popup positioning (acPositionPopup) uses getBoundingClientRect()—if GHL changes viewport layout, popup could render off-screen or occluded; (5) No visual feedback if toggle fails (acSetBusy removed after request)—UX goes gray briefly but user doesn't know if toggle succeeded or failed.
- **Response Sanitizer (stripLeadingGreetings heuristics)**: response-sanitizer.ts removes greetings on turn N>0 to prevent 'Olá!' 'Tudo bem?' pollution. Regex patterns are CONSERVATIVE (match ONLY obvious saudações), but: (1) Guard limit of 15 iterations + 3-char floor could strip legitimate content in edge cases (e.g., Japanese/CJK names mimic saudação patterns); (2) vocativePattern is char-case sensitive (requires [A-ZÀ-Ý] first char) and ONLY runs after a saudação is stripped—if rep says 'João está aqui', the João won't be considered vocative standalone (correct), but if bot response is 'João, tudo bem?', after tudo-bem strip, João vocative strip WILL run (correct). Regex is conservative but fragile for non-Portuguese names; (3) stripDashes() converts em-dash → comma always—if text is 'São Paulo — maior cidade', becomes 'São Paulo, maior cidade', subtle semantic shift; (4) sanitizeAgentMessage() is called on EVERY response in processIncoming, but NO test coverage visible—edge cases (empty array, priorTurnCount=0 vs undefined) behave differently.
- **Knowledge Base / Carrier RAG (Voyage embeddings)**: carrier-retrieval.ts queries pgvector RPC with Voyage voyage-3-large 1024d embeddings. Risks: (1) VOYAGE_API_KEY missing = ERROR log + throws, then catch in (sales-prompt-builder.ts presumably) returns []. But if Voyage API is DOWN (5xx), embedQuery() throws and entire RAG is skipped silently—no fallback to BM25 or cache; (2) similarity threshold 0.4 is hardcoded—if corpus is updated and all chunks shift similarity (e.g., new carrier added), no alerting; (3) retrieveCarrierKnowledge() calls search_carrier_knowledge RPC in PARALLEL for each carrier (Promise.all), but RPC timeout is server-side RPC—if Supabase response is slow, caller waits indefinitely (POST /api/... has maxDuration but RPC call doesn't have its own timeout); (4) carrierLabel() returns hardcoded strings—if new carrier is enabled, label is missing (returns lowercase carrier ID), breaks UI display.
- **Outbound Channel Routing (SMS/WhatsApp fallback)**: outbound-channel.ts pickOutboundChannel() decides SMS vs WhatsApp. Risks: (1) Default is SMS always (even when override='auto'). Comment says 'TODO(future): checkConversationWindow' but window-check is NOT implemented—stub returns SMS forever, even if WhatsApp API is ready; (2) pickOutboundChannel() is called at send time, but no validation that the channel SUPPORTS the message type being sent (e.g., interactive buttons only work on WhatsApp, but if channel=SMS, button payload would be text-only fallback—no error); (3) fallbackChannel() is a simple toggle SMS<->WhatsApp, but no retry loop in callers—if SMS fails, caller has to explicitly call fallbackChannel, re-build message, and retry (not automatic).
- **Stevo Instance Registration & Lifecycle**: stevo-handler.ts calls upsertStevoInstance() to register serverUrl + token from parsed.serverUrl/parsed.instanceToken. Risks: (1) instanceToken is sent by Stevo in EVERY webhook—if an attacker replays an old webhook with stale token, upsert overwrites the current token (no version check or timestamp validation); (2) stevo_instances table has no pruning—if a hub cycles through multiple Stevo instances (reinstall, migration), old rows accumulate (no TTL); (3) deliverProactiveMessage() reads stevo_instances to send—if fetch returns multiple rows per hub (shouldn't happen due to upsert but DB constraints aren't checked), code picks first arbitrarily (no ordering); (4) serverUrl from webhook could be attacker-controlled if webhook source is spoofed—stevo-handler validates instanceToken but NOT serverUrl origin (must be Stevo domain).
- **Session/Auth Token Lifetime & Refresh**: web-auth.ts issues SparkbotWebToken with TTL=1h (SPARKBOT_JWT_TTL_SECONDS). Risks: (1) No refresh endpoint—when JWT expires, embed loader must re-call /api/sparkbot/check-admin to get a new token. If network is slow or GHL context has changed, auth fails and panel becomes dead until page reload; (2) JWT carries rep_id + ghl_user_id + location_id + is_admin—if any of these change mid-session (rep moved to different location, lost admin role, GHL user was suspended), JWT is still valid for 1h before refresh; (3) No token revocation mechanism—if rep is fired/suspended, their existing JWT continues working for up to 1h; (4) verifySparkbotWebToken() catches all errors and returns null, losing error context—malformed token vs. expired token vs. invalid signature all look the same to caller.
- **Audio Transcription Cost Attribution & Fallback**: POST /api/sparkbot/transcribe routes audio through Whisper-1, then calls trackAndCharge(). Risks: (1) Hub agent resolution (resolvePrimaryHub + fallback env) is convoluted—if hubAgentId is null, billing is SKIPPED entirely (console.warn only) and Whisper becomes free. No admin alert (different from rate-limit anomaly signals); (2) Whisper timeout is 60s (openai client config) but next.js maxDuration=30s—if Whisper takes 31-60s, request is killed mid-response, error caught but response isn't retried; (3) POST /api/sparkbot/transcribe doesn't rate-limit per rep—if rep token leaks, attacker can spam transcribe requests → OpenAI charges → location cap gets hit (no circuit breaker pre-transcribe).
- **Concurrent Inbound Processing & Race Conditions**: Multiple inbound paths (webhook GHL, webhook Stevo, web UI) can arrive simultaneously for the same contact. Risks: (1) in-memory inFlightMessages mutex in webhook-handler.ts survives only ONE lambda—if 2 webhooks from GHL hit different Vercel edge nodes, both process in parallel, both pass dedup check, create 2 turns (caught by UNIQUE constraint later, but can create confused state); (2) rep_identity.consecutive_proactive_without_reply increment/decrement is NOT atomic—concurrent resets (one from inbound Stevo, one from proactive rule timeout) could race; (3) insertSparkbotMessage() tries INSERT but on 23505 (PK violation) returns null—caller doesn't know if it was a race or an actual error, follows through with processing anyway; (4) shouldStillRespond() checks DB for last msg then sleeps (debounce)—during sleep, another msg could arrive, both would pass check, creating duplicates.
- **Error Handling & Observability (Sentry/Signals)**: Errors are logged to console + sometimes pushed to admin-signals via recordSignalAsync(). Risks: (1) recordSignalAsync() is fire-and-forget (dynamic import + no await in most call sites)—errors in signal recording are swallowed, no alert if admin-signals table is full or Supabase is down; (2) console.error/warn are sent to Sentry via Next.js config, but some deep errors are caught and logged without Sentry context (e.g., in stevo-handler.ts errors are console.warn, not thrown, so Sentry never sees them); (3) Result structs (e.g., result.llm_failed, result.primary_error) are populated but rarely exposed to UI or admin dashboard—rep/admin has no visibility into WHY agent is underperforming (audio transcription failed silently, llm fallback to GPT-4, etc.)
- **Configuration Drift & Feature Flags**: Multiple feature flags scattered across env vars (STEVO_SEND_ENABLED, STEVO_INTERACTIVE_ENABLED, STEVO_DEBOUNCE_MS, ASSISTANT_OUTBOUND_CHANNEL, AGENT_MOTOR_UNIFIED, AGENT_ENTITLEMENTS_ENFORCED, etc.) are evaluated at runtime. Risks: (1) Flags default to OFF/conservative, but if admin forgets to check current state, cutover assumptions break (e.g., assuming STEVO_SEND_ENABLED=1 but it's 0); (2) No flag registry or UI dashboard—admin must grep code to understand all flags; (3) Flag changes require redeployment (Next.js build-time env)—rolling back is manual; (4) Flag combination explosions—enabling some flags without others creates undefined behavior (e.g., STEVO_SEND_ENABLED=1 + AGENT_MOTOR_UNIFIED=1 may not be compatible).
- **Bulk Message Delivery & Spam Risk**: tools/bulk-messages-v2.ts allows bulk_message_v2() with multi-segment targets. Risks: (1) disclaimer check happens BEFORE scheduling (computeDisclaimers) but disclaimer counts are based on filter estimates—if filter matches MORE rows than estimated, no re-check before send; (2) Quiet hours are checked per recipient (conversation_state.timezone) but timezone could be stale (rep moved); (3) No rate-limit on bulk job creation—a single rep could submit 100 bulk jobs immediately, each with 1000 recipients (100k messages) → exhausts quota in seconds, other reps blocked; (4) Bulk job runner picks jobs via random ORDER (no priority)—critical campaigns could be starved if too many non-critical jobs are queued.
